Summary 0:
UCITS management companies — marketing communications to investors (Regulation (EU) No 1286/2014 on marketing communications for UCITS
UCITS marketing communications — Marketing communications for investors
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2014/65/EU on the marketing of UCITS to investors
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It sets out the rules for marketing communications* to investors of a UCITS* management company.
KEY POINTS
The directive applies to all UCITS managed by a management company, whether or not it is externally or internally managed, depending on its legal form.
It does not apply to funds managed by credit institutions, EuVECA managers or EuSEF managers.
The regulation applies to companies, the regular business of which is the management of UC A UCITS, that are authorised by the European Commission to market units or shares of their AIFs to retail investors.
Management companies may only engage in pre-marketing on behalf of an authorised manager of a qualifying venture capital fund where it is authorised as an investment firm, as a credit institution or as a social entrepreneurship fund.
A UCITS management company must notify the competent authorities of the content or of the addressees of its marketing communications before it engages in premarketing.
Premarketing must be presented in a manner that is fair, clear and not misleading.
EU countries’ competent authorities must keep a central database of information on all notifications and notification letters and information that they have received under Directives 2009/2011/61/EU in relation to cross-border marketing activity, as well as information about any changes which should be reflected in that database.
In addition to the central database, EU countries must also keep a database of all information on any changes to that information, if such changes would result in a change to the information in that central database. This information should be sent to the European Securities and Markets Authority (ESMA) by 2 February 2021.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATION APPLYORKORK INTO FORCE?
The legislation entered into force on 2 August 2014.
BACKGROUND
   
 
For more information, see:
‘UCITS’ on the European Investment Bank's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Егародскабликова грацик голога   Пода

Summary 1:
EU harmonisation rules on products
EU harmonisations rules on goods
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2018/644 on the enforcement of certain EU harmonisation legislation
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
 
It sets out rules to ensure that products covered by EU legislation comply with the harmonisation requirements.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all products imported into the EU from non-EU countries.
It does not apply to:
foodstuffs and agricultural products;
medical devices;
personal protective equipment;
electrical equipment; and
electromagnetic fields.
EU countries must ensure that the legislation is applied uniformly throughout the EU’s supply chain and that it is enforced.
To achieve a high degree of compliance with the legislation, EU countries must:
ensure that products are checked at all stages of the supply chain, including the point of sale, the manufacture, the import and export of the product, the place of manufacture and the place where it is stored;
provide information to market surveillance authorities and economic operators on products that are not covered by the legislation.
Provide the relevant information to the authorities in charge of the control on products entering the customs territory of the EU and to the EU country in which the product is intended to be released for free circulation.
In addition, the Commission must be able to approve specific pre-export control systems.
The Commission is also able to authorise the use of ICSMSMS (Information and Communication System for Customs and Market Surveillance (ICSMS) for the exchange of information on products subject to EU legislation and on the results of controls.
Imporporporters and importers must inform the customs authorities in a timely manner of the release of products for the free circulation, and of the result of controls, where such information is relevant for enforcement of EU legislation on products.
If a product is found to be a non-compliant product, it must be notified to the competent authorities in the other EU countries and notified of the non-compliance and the measures to be taken.
National market surveillance and customs authorities must take the necessary measures in the case of a product that is not in compliance with EU legislation. These measures must be effective, proportionate and dissuasive.
FROM WHEN DOES THE IMPLEMENTATION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The legislation is part of a package of measures designed to modernise and modernise the EU market for goods.
For more information, see:
European Union harmonisation (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Products: products which are intended for sale in the EU.
* Importers: companies that manufacture, place on the market, import or export a product.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Implementing Regulation(EU) 2019/644 of 18 April 2019 on the Enforcement of certain Union harmonisations legislation

Summary 2:
Copyright and related rights for the retransmission of television and radio programmes originating in other European Union (EU) countries
Copyright and relevant rights for retransmissions of TV and radio programs originating in different EU countries
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2009/33/EC on the exercise of copyright and related copyright and other related rights in the field of broadcasting and broadcasting organisations
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It lays down rules on the collective management of copyright, related rights and the licensing of broadcasting organisations’ rights to retransmit their programmes to other EU countries.
KEY POINTS
The directive applies to broadcasting organisations, signal distributors and rightholders.
It does not apply to the broadcasting organisations themselves, but to collective management organisations that manage the rights of their programmes.
The Directive applies to all broadcasting organisations that transmit daily many hours of television or radio programmes, irrespective of their country of origin.
Direct injection of rights
A collective management organisation (collective management organisation) manages rights of the same category for the territory of the EU country for which the broadcasting organisation transmits its programmes. The organisation is responsible for the management of the rights transferred to it by the broadcaster.
Rights transferred to a collective management body
A broadcasting organisation may transfer certain rights to other collective management bodies, such as broadcasters’ organisations, to which it is entitled, for example, the right to transmit their programmes from one EU country to another.
Collective management organisations must ensure that the rights are transferred to them in accordance with the rules on collective management laid down in Directive 93/83/EEC on intellectual property rights (see summary).
The collective managing body must ensure the effective and efficient management of rights transferred by a broadcasting organisation to the collective managing organisation.
Licensing
The broadcasting organisation must grant or refuse the authorisation to a broadcasting service provider to transmit its programmes to another EU country, provided that it complies with EU law on limitations on limitations, including territorial limitations, to the exploitation of their rights.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
From 1 January 2010.
BACKGROUND
  
The European Commission published a report on the implementation of Directive 2009/34/EC.
For more information, see:
‘Copyright and Related Rights’ on the European Commission’s website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Directive 2009 /33/EU of 12 December 2009 on the approximation of the laws of the Member States relating to copyright and certain related rights (recast of programmes from other Member States)

Summary 3:
Mutual recognition of imports and exports of agricultural products in the European Union (EU) — rules for the application of the principle of mutual recognition of goods
MutUAL recognition of imported goods
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 764/2008 on mutual recognition
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that goods from one EU country can be freely marketed in another EU country on the basis of a mutual recognition declaration*.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to imports from non-EU countries and exports from EU countries.
It does not apply to agricultural products.
To benefit from the principle, goods must be lawfully marketed in the EU country in which they are produced.
EU countries must ensure that:
goods are lawfully marketed and that they comply with the relevant national technical rules;
they comply with EU law on conformity assessment* and prior authorisation procedures;
the goods are tested and certified in accordance with the applicable national conformity assessment bodies;
there is no need to restrict or deny market access to the goods.
The EU country of destination must inform the economic operator of the goods that are subject to its conformity assessment and the relevant prior authorisations procedure.
If the goods are not covered by the conformity assessment procedure, the country of origin must make a voluntary declaration on their behalf and on the producer's behalf and under the responsibility of the producer. The declaration must be easily accessible and is in a reliable format.
In addition, EU countries must provide the producer with a non-judicial problem-solving procedure to deal with any problems arising from the non-compliance with the declaration.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISTRYINGREDIENTS APPLACE IN THE RECOMMUTILITY
The European Commission is responsible for the implementation of the regulation.
KEY TERMS
* Mutual recognition: the principle whereby goods from the same EU country are treated as if they are the same goods if they have the same technical characteristics.
MAIN DOCUMENT
   
Commission Regulation (EU), Euratom, Euratom and the European Economic and Social Committee of 23 October 2018 on the application, on behalf of the European Parliament and of the Council, of 26 September 2018 of the Union of European Union, of the one part, and the Council of the other part of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU (OJ L 165, 30.10.2018, pp. 1-8)

Summary 4:

ACT
Regulation (EU) 2017/852 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 13 October 2017 on the functioning of the.eu Top Level Domain Name Registry
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It sets out the rules for the operation of the top level domain name (TOP-level domain name) in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation designates a designated registry to manage the top-level.eu TLD.
The registry is managed by the European Commission and is responsible for the organisation, administration and management of the TLD by the Commission.
It is managed in accordance with the principles of non-discrimination and transparency, and must implement measures to safeguard fair competition that are to be authorised in advance by the commission, in particular when the Registry provides services to undertakings with whom it competes on downstream markets.
A multistakeholder advisory group is set up to advise the Commission on the organisation of the registry and to ensure that it complies with the regulation’s requirements.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
 
The.eu top level TLD is one of the largest country code TLDs (ccTLDs).
It was designated by the EU countries in 2011.
For more information, see:
‘The top level domains’ on the Internet.
KEY TERMS
* Top Level domain name: a hierarchical system of unique identifiers (TLDN).
MAIN DOCUMENTS
Registry: a registry that manages top level.eu domain names.
Commission Implementing Regulation (EC) No 852/2017 of 20 October 2017 laying down the principles and procedures on the operation, organisation and maintenance of the Top Level.eu Domain Name Name Registry.

Summary 5:
Multiannual financial framework for the transport, energy and digital sectors (MFF 2021-2027) (see summary)
Multiannial financial framework (mFF 2021 - 2027)
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2021/695 — Multiannual Financial Framework for the Transport, Energy and Digital Sectors
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE IMPLEMENTING REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the multiannual financing framework (the MFF) for the European Union’s transport and energy sectors.
KEY POINTS
The MFF covers the period from 1 January 2021 to 31 December 2027.
The European Commission is responsible for managing, monitoring, evaluating, evaluating and controlling the MFF.
It is funded by the European Regional Development Fund (ERDF), the European Social Fund Plus, the Co 2021, the European Investment Bank (EIB) and the European Maritime and Fisheries Fund (EMFF).
The main beneficiaries of the funding are:
transport and energy infrastructure projects;
digital infrastructure projects in the transport and mobility sectors;
the development of renewable hydrogen or bio-methane to be increased.
In addition, the CEF provides financial support for the development of innovative infrastructure technologies that enable the transition to low emission energy and mobility systems and that improve security of supply, while seeking greater energy independence for the EU.
Cofinancing rates
The maximum co-financing rate is 70% for works relating to the specific objectives referred to in Annex III of the regulation. For works in the digital sector, the amount of EU financial support must not exceed 30% of the total eligible cost.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The regulation entered into force on 31 December 2021.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a number of measures to tackle climate change. These include:
the EU 2020 Strategy, which aims to reduce greenhouse gas emissions by 40% by 2020; and
the 2030 Agenda for Climate Change.
For more information, see:
‘Climate Change’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Implementing Regulation of 21 December 2021 laying down the rules of the Multiannial Financial Framework 2021- 2027 for the Transitional period (OJ L 183, 31.12.2021, pp. 1-3)
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Summary 6:
Removal of terrorist content on the internet
Removing terrorist content online
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 10/2013/EU on the removal of terrorist material on the Internet
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to improve the detection and removal of content online that incites terrorist acts.
It lays down rules for hosting service providers and users’ trust in the online environment.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to hosting services that host or host access to terrorist content, as well as to content that is not terrorist content.
Hosting service providers are responsible for removing or disabling access to such content. They must act with due diligence and implement safeguards, where appropriate, including human oversight and verifications, to avoid any unintended or erroneous decision leading to their removal of or disabling of access to the content that does not incite terrorist activity.
EU countries must ensure that a contact point is designated or established within the competent authority to handle requests for clarification and feedback in relation to removal orders issued by that competent authority.
The hosting service provider must provide the complainant with the reasons for its decision to remove or disable access to any content, including:
the reasons for the decision;
the content has been removed or access to which has been disabled;
a reasoned request to submit either a removal order or information within 48 hours of receiving the order or a reasoned request for a review of the removal order;
information on the content, depending on the outcome of those proceedings.
In addition, the service provider is required to ensure that information about the contact points is made publicly available.
Requests for clarification or feedback must be made to the competent authorities of the EU country where the service providers has its main establishment or where its legal representative resides or is established to scrutinise the order.
Removal is without prejudice to Directives 2000/31/EC and 2010/13/EU.
Service providers are subject to penalties for infringements of the regulation. These include:
a ban on hosting services providing access to content which incites terrorism or which is likely to incite terrorism;
charges for failure to comply with removal orders;
restrictions on access to certain types of content, e.g. pornography, child pornography, illegal drugs, illegal weapons and weapons of mass destruction.
Where a service provider fails to comply, it is subject to a ban on providing or hosting access to that content, i.e. it is liable for any damage to its reputation or to its business, unless it has complied with the regulation’s requirements.
Reporting and enforcement
The service providers must report to the European Commission every 2 years on their compliance with this regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to combat the spread of terrorism, including Directive 2014/35/EU, which aims to strengthen the fight against terrorism and to improve cooperation between EU countries’ law enforcement authorities and Europol.
For more information, see:
‘Fighting terrorism’ on the European Parliament's website.

Summary 7:
Framework programme for Research and Innovation 2021-2027
Framework Programme for Research & Innovation 2021 - 2027
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2018/1046 on Horizon Europe — the framework programme for research and innovation
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the implementation of Horizon Europe, the EU’s main research programme.
It aims to support R&I in an integrated manner, respecting all relevant provisions in the framework of the World Trade Organization (WTO).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The programme is designed to support research, innovation and technological development (R&I) in the fields of science, technology and innovation (S&T).
It covers the following areas:
basic and applied research;
science and technology policy;
environmental and social impact;
health and well-being;
sustainable development;
research and innovation in the areas of social and economic impact.
Objectives
The objective of the programme is to:
promote the development of innovative and sustainable solutions;
improve the quality of life of people and of the environment;
contribute to the economic and social development of the European Union (EU);
improve social and environmental impact of the EU and its Member States;
provide a high level of scientific, technological, economic, environmental and societal support to the European Research Council (ERC) and the European Atomic Energy Community (Euratom) and to contribute to the sustainable development of Europe.
Partnership and participation
A number of partners are eligible to participate in the programme, including:
the European Commission;
the EU countries’ research institutes, research centres, universities and other bodies;
non-EU countries and international organisations.
Participation is open to any legal entity, regardless of its place of establishment and including legal entities from non-associated third countries or international organisations, provided that the conditions laid down in this regulation have been met together with any conditions set out in the work programme or call for proposals.
Funding bodies and direct actions
The European Research Centre (ERC) is responsible for administering the programme. The ERC is assisted by a Joint Coordination Committee (JCC).
The EIC manages the programme and ensures that it is implemented in line with the rules of the WTO.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The regulation entered into force on 1 July 2018.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Horizon Europe’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Research and innovation: research that contributes to the development and sustainability of society, the economy, the environment and the environment.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Еграцига
Commission Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 1046/2018 of 18 July 2018 laying down the general rules applicable to Horizon Europe - the Framework Programme for R & I 2021–2027 (OJ L 283, 20.7.2018, pp. 1–8)

Summary 8:
Programme for the development of the European Space Industry
Programmes for the Development of the Europe Space Industries
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Decision (CFSP) 2021/698 on the European Union’s Horizon 2021 programme
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE IMPLEMENTING DECISION?
It sets out the rules for the implementation of the Horizon 2021 Programme.
KEY POINTS
The programme aims to develop space industry capacity across the EU and facilitate collaboration across space industry active in all EU countries.
It also aims to improve the safety and security of systems and services deployed by EU countries’ governments and the European Commission.
To achieve these objectives, the programme is divided into 3 sub-programmes:
Satellite communication (SST) sub-part, which aims to provide satellite communication capacities, services and user equipment to GOVSATCOM users or provide capacities, sites or facilities.
EU space debris remediation by managing the existing space debris.
Cooperation between EU countries and the International Space Agency (ESA) in the field of space debris management.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The Horizon 2021 Programmes are part of the EU’S overall financial framework.
For more information, see:
Horizon 2021 Programme (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Satellite communication: the use of space-based communication technologies to provide information and communication services to the public and the private sectors.
* Debris remediation: the process of removing space debris from the atmosphere.

Summary 9:
European Digital Innovation Hub (EDIH) programme for the period 2021-2027
European digital innovation Hub (EDIH) Programme for the year 2021 - 2027
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Decision (EU) 2021/2027 — programme for European digital innovation hub
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION AND THE PROGRAMME?
The programme aims to support the European Commission’s efforts to implement the objectives of the Gothenburg Social Summit and the European Digital Innovation Summit.
It sets out the general objectives for the programme, as well as the specific objectives for specific actions.
KEY POINTS
Objectives
The objective of the programme is to:
promote the digitalisation of public services and to support fundamental freedoms and operational mutual recognition in the European Union (EU);
encourage the development of innovative and high-performance computing (HPC) solutions;
improve interoperability between public and private sectors;
facilitate the mobility of workers and self-employed people between EU Member States;
support the creation of a European innovation hub in each Member State.
Specific objectives
The actions under Specific Objective 1 are:
improving interoperability of public administrations;
modernising public administrations’ IT systems and systems;
developing new and innovative solutions for the digital single market;
encouraging the use of exascale and ex-ascale computing;
enhancing the mobility and mobility of the workforce;
promoting the digital transformation of areas of public interest, such as health, education, social protection and the environment;
ensuring the availability of high-performing computing solutions to meet the needs of the public sector and the private sector;
creating a European Innovation Hub in each of the Member States.
Eligible actions
The following actions are eligible for funding under the programme:
high performance computing solutions for public services;
the creation of European innovation hubs.
The European Commission is responsible for implementing the programme.
Implementation and forms of EU funding
The programmes are implemented primarily through direct management. The financial envelope for the implementation of the Programme is EUR 7 588 000 000 in current prices.
Cumulative and alternative funding may be available from other EU programmes.
FROM WHEN DOES THE PROGRAMMENDING DECISION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a new multiannual financial framework (MFF) for 2021 to 2027.
For more information, see:
‘The EU's new financial framework’ (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* High performance computing: a new type of computing technology that is capable of performing a wide range of tasks, including high-definition video-conferencing, virtual reality and virtual reality.
* Exascale: a technology that can be used to perform tasks such as analysing, analysing and analysing data.
ACT
Commission Implementing Decision of 20 January 2021 laying down the general principles and implementing measures for the European digital Innovation Hub under the framework of the European Development Fund (OJ L 157, 21.3.2021, pp. 1-8)

Summary 10:
European Statistical Programme
European Statistical Program
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2021/2027 — financial framework for European statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE IMPLEMENTING REGULATION?
It establishes the European Statistical Programme (ESP) for the period from 1 January 2021 to 31 December 2027.
It aims to provide high-quality, comparable and reliable European statistics to underpin the design, implementation, monitoring and evaluation of all EU policies.
KEY POINTS
The ESP was established under Regulation (EC) No 223/2009 of the European Parliament and of the Council.
Since its inception, it has proved a major contributor to growth, competitiveness and employment and it should continue benefitting all citizens and businesses equally.
The ESP is funded by the European Commission, the European Economic and Social Fund (EEF), the European Social Fund and the European Regional Development Fund (ERDF).
The main objectives of the ESP are to:
ensure that European statistics are reliable and up-to-date;
support the development, production and dissemination of European statistics;
contribute to the sustainable development of the EU’s economy;
promote the exchange of information and best practice on EU policies and programmes;
encourage the use of innovative and cost-effective information and communication technologies (ICTs) to improve the quality of EU statistics.
In addition, the programme is designed to support the development of a European Statistical Information System (ESIS) to meet the challenges of the green and digital transition and of an increasingly competitive and fast-moving environment.
To achieve these objectives, the EPS is supported by:
the European Commission and the EEF;
the ESM and EEF, in particular through the European Research and Innovation Agency (ERISA);
the ESIS and ERSI, as well as the European Agricultural and Food Safety Authority (EAFSA);
a number of non-profit-making bodies and public bodies, such as universities and research institutes;
a European Consumer Centres Network (ECCN), which is an important source of information about challenges and problems that consumers encounter at local level, which are relevant for EU policy-making and for the protection of consumers’ interests.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULING APPLY?
The implementing regulation has applied since 20 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The European Statistical Program has been subject to Regulation (Euratom) No 966/2012.
For more information, see:
European Statistics (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* European statistics: a set of standards and procedures for collecting, analysing and disseminating information on EU policy and programmes.
* Statistical Information Systems: a collection of statistical data on EU and national policies, programmes and activities.
ACT
Commission Implementing Regulation(EU) 2019/852 of 20 January 2019 laying down the financial rules for the European Statistics Programme (OJ L 136, 20.2.2019, pp. 1-3)
RELATED ACTS
Regulation (EUR) No 541/2014 of the Euratom of 6 December 2014 laying down detailed rules and implementing measures for the implementation of Directive 2009/65/EC of the Parliament and the Council as regards the statistical information system and the information society (OJR L 283, 30.12.2014, pp.).

Summary 11:
EU rules on firearms and essential components and ammunition — confiscation and traceability of firearms and their essential components
EU rights and obligations
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 91/477/EEC on the acquisition and possession of firearms
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It lays down rules to prevent the illegal acquisition and sale of firearms, essential components* and ammunition.
KEY POINTS
The directive applies to the acquisition, manufacture, sale, transfer, importation, export and importation of firearms*, essential components*, ammunition and ammunition classified in the following categories:
automatic rifles, shotguns, pistols, assault rifles, revolvers, semi-automatic rifles and shotguns, as well as shotguns and assault rifles in combination with a detachable loading device having a high capacity;
automatic pistols and shotguns with a high number of rounds to be fired;
conventional rifles, carbines and shotguns.
It does not apply to handguns, shotguns or assault rifles.
EU countries may adopt more stringent rules than those laid down in this directive, subject to the rights conferred on residents of the EU countries pursuant to Article 17(2) of the Schengen acquis.
National authorities must ensure that:
dealers and brokers must keep a register of all firearms and the essential components they acquire and keep for a period of 30 years after the destruction of the firearms or essential components concerned;
firearms and ammunition are destroyed in accordance with national deactivation standards and techniques;
they must keep records of all transactions between dealers and brokers;
the relevant national authorities must report any suspicious transactions to the competent authorities.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It has applied since 13 June 2017 and had to become law in EU countries by 13 June 2018.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Firearms’ on the European Commission’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Automatic rifles: rifles designed to fire more than 10 rounds per minute and designed to carry more than 100 rounds per second;
Spirits: rapid fire rifles designed for use with a maximum velocity of more than 1,000 metres per second.
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 12:
Maritime information exchange system (EMSWe)
Maritime Information Exchange System (EMSW)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2018/1725 on the harmonised reporting interface module for the exchange and distribution of information received through the maritime National Single Window
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to improve the exchange of information between EU countries’ authorities and the European Maritime Safety Agency (EMSA).
It sets out the rules for the operation of the maritime national single window.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
ships arriving in and/or departing from EU ports;
ships departing from ports of EU countries.
It does not apply to vessels registered in non-EU countries, except in exceptional circumstances, such as when there is an urgent need to protect internal order and security or to address a serious threat against human or animal health or against the environment.
EU countries are responsible for their operation of their maritime single windows.
Harmonised interface module
The European Commission has developed a harmonised interface interface module.
The module allows EU countries to make available, separately, to providers of port services at the port of destination a subset of data elements pre-defined at national level.
Implementing acts
The Commission must lay down the functional and technical specifications, quality control mechanisms and procedures for deploying, maintaining and employing the harmonising interface module and the related harmonised elements of the Maritime National Single Windows.
Reporting obligations
The EU countries must ensure that:
ship identification information, particulars and exemptions are recorded in the Maritime Single Window ship database;
ship registration information is made available for any subsequent port calls within the EU.
In addition, the Commission must:
ensure that the data collected by the EU countries are made available to the EMSA at EU level, including among relevant stakeholders, and at the level of relevant international organisations.
Data processing
The processing of personal data by the Commission within the framework of this regulation should comply with Regulation (EU).
The data collected must comply with Directive 2002/59/EC and with the relevant data elements from the International Maritime Organisation (IMO) conventions and codes.
Monitoring
The directive requires the Commission to review the application of the regulation and submit to the European Parliament and the Council an assessment report on the functioning of the EMSWe on the basis of the data and statistics collected.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 15 August 2024.
BACKGROUND
The Maritime Reporting Interface Module (MIM) is part of the EU’s Maritime Information System (MIS).
For more information, see:
‘The MIM’ on the European Commission's website.
REFERENCES

Summary 13:
Electronic road tolls (ETS) — rules
Electronic Road Tolls (EETS)
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2016/680 — rules for the operation of electronic road toll systems
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It sets out the rules for setting up and operating an electronic toll system (ETS) in the EU.
KEY POINTS
EETS providers are required to:
provide toll-charging devices (OBEs);
ensure that their OBEs are compatible with other EETS domains and with the existing interoperability constituents of the EETS provider.
The EETS providers must also ensure that:
their devices are capable of detecting and applying tolls;
they comply with the applicable EU rules on the calculation of applied toll on the vehicles of EETS users by the toll chargers;
their vehicles are registered in a toll charger’s EETS domain.
Each EU country must establish a procedure for registering and authorising an OBE.
An OBE must be installed or used by a toll-charger in order to facilitate their contacts with the toll charger.
A toll charger may refuse to authorise or refuse it, in the form of a Decision, within 6 months from the moment it received the request.
EOTS providers must ensure that their devices:
operate in accordance with EU rules, as set out in Regulation (EU, 2016/679) on interoperability;
have the necessary technical capabilities to detect and apply tolls.
In addition, the EOTS provider must:
implement an implementing act for each OBE;
conduct an interoperability test to ensure that its OBE meets the requirements of the directive;
certify that the OBE is suitable for use in the toll charging domain and obtain certification of the successful completion of the respective tests.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The directive entered into force on 1 January 2017.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘EETS’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 14:
Deployment of immigration liaison officers for the purposes of return operations of the EU in accordance with Article 49 of Regulation (EU) 2016/679 (see summary)
Deployment OF IMMIGRATION LIFELINE OFFICERS
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 515/2014 on the deployment of the European Commission’s liaison officers in the field of migration
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the tasks and responsibilities of the liaison officers deployed by the Commission for the purpose of implementing the Schengen acquis.
KEY POINTS
The purpose of the regulation is to ensure that liaison officers dealing with migration-related issues are deployed by different competent authorities and that their mandates and tasks may overlap, in order to enhance cooperation among officers operating within the same non-EU country or region.
The regulation provides for the establishment of a Steering Board comprising representatives of EU countries associated with the implementation, application, application and development of parts of the Schegens acquis, as well as representatives of the Commission.
It also provides for a secure web-based information exchange platform to facilitate and support the networks provided for in the regulation.
Duties of the officers
The officers are responsible for:
collecting information, for use either at operational level, strategic level, or both, on migration flows;
assisting the deploying authorities in their deployment;
monitoring and analysing migration flows.
They must act accordingly when carrying out their tasks.
Information exchange platform
The European Commission is responsible for setting up the Steering board and maintaining it.
Implementing the regulation requires the Commission to:
notify the tasks of the deployed officers;
provide a report on their deployment to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee, the Committee of the Regions and the Committee on Foreign Affairs and Security Policy;
identify deployment gaps and outline possibilities for deployment of officers.
In addition, the Commission must:
ensure that the officers’ training is based on relevant national curricula;
prepare an activity report for each deployment of liaison officers, including a summary of the duties and responsibilities;
organise training courses for the officers and ensure that they have the necessary knowledge and skills to carry out their duties;
develop and implement information exchange platforms.
EU countries may receive EU financial support for the execution of the activities referred to in this regulation, in addition to the financial support provided by the EU budget for the period 2014-2020.
Notification of the deployment
The Commission must send a report to the Commission every 2 years on the number of immigration officers deployed and the activities they have carried out. The report must include an overview of the deployments of officers and a description of the tasks they have performed.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECAST APPLY?
The original regulation entered into force on 1 January 2016.
BACKGROUND
  
The Schengens is a legal instrument of the Treaty on European Union (TFEU) which aims to replace irregular and uncontrolled migratory flows with safe and well-managed pathways, through a comprehensive approach aimed at ensuring, at all stages, the efficient management of migration flows and protecting vulnerable persons.
For more information, see:
‘Migration and migration policy’ on the Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (Euratom) No 605/2014 of 20 December 2014 on the application of Article 49(2) of Regulation [Official Journal L 183 of 20.12.2014].
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Summary 15:
Biometric data in identity cards and residence cards for non-EU citizens and their family members who are not nationals of an EU country
Biometric information in identity card and residence card for non EU citizens
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/1954 — minimum security standards for biometric data and in residence cards
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out minimum standards for the collection and processing of biometric identifiers* for the issuing and renewal of identity cards in the EU.
KEY POINTS
EU countries must ensure that appropriate and effective procedures are in place to collect and store biometric information for the purposes of issuing and renewing identity cards or residence cards of non-nationals.
The data elements included on identity cards must comply with the specifications set out in part 5 of International Civil Aviation Organization (ICAO) Document 9303 on Machine Readable Travel Documents, which do not serve identification purposes in the issuing EU countries, such as the passport card issued by Ireland.
National IDENTITY CARDS
National identity cards are issued by EU countries in accordance with national laws. They must be issued by qualified and duly authorised staff of the competent national authorities.
Collection of fingerprints
The collection of fingerprints must be collected solely by qualified staff of such authorities, except in the case of applications submitted to the diplomatic and consular authorities of the EU country of origin. Children under the age of 6 years are exempt from the requirement to give fingerprints.
Personal data processing
The processing of personal data in relation to identity cards is carried out by the competent authorities of EU countries must be carried out in line with the technical specifications established by the Commission Implementing Decision C(2018) 7767.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLACE APPLYORKORK
The regulation has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
   
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to improve security and to facilitate the exercise of the rights of free movement of EU citizens and family members.
For more information, see:
‘Biometric identifiers’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Personal data: a person’s personal data consisting of their fingerprints, facial images, iris and iris images, and any other data that may be extracted from their personal data.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC) No 1030/2002 of 20 December 2002 laying down minimum security requirements for the processing of fingerprints and facial images in the context of the application of Directive 2004/38/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council on the recognition of biometrics (OJ L 286, 14.12.2002, pp. 1-8)

Summary 16:
ECRIS-TCN — criminal record information system
ECRIS-TNC
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2018/1725 on the use of the European Criminal Records Information System for the purposes of criminal proceedings
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
 
   
It aims to ensure that the competent authorities of EU countries have a complete overview of criminal records in order to prevent and combat crime, including organised crime and terrorism.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to criminal records of non-EU nationals who have been convicted in one or more EU countries and who are not citizens of the EU.
It does not apply to:
third-country nationals convicted prior to the date of entry into national criminal records;
non-EU citizens convicted as a third-country national after their conviction was entered into the national criminal record;
third country nationals convicted before the date on which their criminal record was entered in the national database.
EU countries may also create records in ECRIS for non-nationals convicted before their conviction.
Requests for access to data data
The competent authorities may request access to the data data at the same time, provided those time limits are met, provided that:
the purpose of the request for access is clearly defined;
the data transmitted as referred to in Article 5 of the regulation and the national file reference;
data used for a query; and
the date and exact time of the operation.
The data transmitted must be kept for a maximum retention period of 5 years.
A log must be maintained of all data data transmitted to and from the central system and the communication infrastructure.
Data protection rights and supervision
The relevant national authorities must ensure that data protection rights are respected and that the data is processed only for the purpose of reporting and providing statistics, without allowing for individual identification.
National authorities must also ensure that: the data transmitted by the central authority is stored in a secure central system;
relevant information is made available to the relevant national supervisory authority without delay.
If a national authority receives a request to access data from a central system, it must inform the competent national authority of the reason for the request, the nature and duration of the search, and the identifying mark of the official who carried out the search.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The aim of this regulation is to ensure the maximum effectiveness of the system.
For more information, see:
‘The use of European Criminal Record Information System’ on the European Commission’s website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Еграциганска гарскиблаков года   баракскога
Commission Implementing Decision 2014/852/EU of 12 December 2014 on the application of Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018 /1725 to the use by Member States of the Regulation (EEC) No 552/2014 on the operation of the Electronic Criminal Records Identification System (ECRIST) (OJ L 183, 14.12.2014, pp. 1-8)

Interoperation of EU Information Systems for Security, Border and Migration Management
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/817 on interoperability of the information systems used by the European Union Agency for Law Enforcement and Security Cooperation (eu-LISA)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to improve interoperability between the EU’s information systems to improve the work of border guards, customs authorities, police officers and judicial authorities.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
the common identity repository for identification (CIR);
the single identity database (SIS); and
the data processing operations in the ETIAS Central System.
Access to the CIR and SIS is subject to the conditions laid down in the regulation.
The CIR or SIS are queried and where a red link exists between data in two or more of the data systems, the border guard must carry out any additional verification necessary to take a decision on the status and colour of the link.
In cases where Europol has launched a query, it may access the application files stored in the EAS Central System in accordance with this regulation for consultation where the reply received reveals that data are stored in CIR.
EU countries, Europol and ETIAS central units must keep logs of all data processing activities in the ESP.
Data quality
The European Commission is responsible for ensuring that the interoperability components of the regulation are up-to-date and maintain a high level of data quality.

Summary 18:
Renewable energy: financial support for renewable energy projects and renewable energy efficiency
Renewables: Financial support for renewables
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2019/852 on financial support to renewable energy and renewable electricity
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
   
 
It sets out rules to encourage investment in renewable energy in order to help meet the EU’s 2020 renewable energy targets.
KEY POINTS
The directive sets out the rules for the financial support that renewable energy producers receive from the European Union (EU).
It aims to support the development of renewable energy resources in the EU and to reduce greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions from renewable energy sources.
It also aims to encourage the use of high-efficiency technologies to reduce GHG emissions.
EU countries have different renewable energy potentials and operate different support schemes at national level.
The legislation does not apply to:
grants of origin for renewable electricity;
joint projects, joint support schemes and the opening of support schemes to producers located in other EU countries.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
 The directive is one of a series of measures designed to help the EU meet the 2020 EU renewable energy target.
For more information, see:
EU renewable energy policy (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* GRANT OF ORIGIN
* Guarantee of origin: a guarantee of origin is issued by a producer to a producer of renewable electricity from renewable sources to a customer.

WHAT DO THE DIRECTIVES DO?
They set out rules on how renewable energy can be used to meet the 2030 EU target for GHG emission reductions.

These rules are designed to encourage renewable energy investment and encourage the efficient use of renewable resources. Summary 19:
Radio spectrum management — efficient use of radio spectrum and spectrum management rules
Radio Spectrum management — efficiency use of Radio Spectrum Management rules
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2015/1535 on radio spectrum management
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It sets out rules for the efficient and cost-effective use of the radio spectrum* in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The directive applies to all providers of mobile and fixed-line broadband internet access and voice communication services in the EU, as well as to operators of radio local area networks (RANs).
It repeals Directive 2002/19/EC, 2002/20/EC and 2002/21/EC.
It does not apply to:
telecommunications services, such as television, radio or television broadcast content providers;
radio spectrum management*;
the provision of wireless network equipment;
information and communication services;
mobile communications services.
Amendments
The new directive repeals and repeals Directives 2002/22/EU, 2003/19 /EC, 2004/22 /EU, 2005/21 /EU and 2006/23/EU.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
The legislation has applied since 1 January 2016.
KEY TERMS
Radio spectrum: the radio frequency spectrum used for the transmission of information and communications services, including radio and television broadcasting.

Summary 21:
EU solidarity for natural gas — emergency gas supply
EU solidarity with regard to natural gas
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2017/852 — EU solidarity for gas
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It sets out EU solidarity rules for the supply of natural gas to EU countries in the event of a natural gas emergency.
KEY POINTS
The directive applies to all EU countries’ natural gas supply to solidarity customers, regardless of whether they are in the EU or non-EU countries.
EU countries must ensure that gas is supplied to solidarity protected customers in the requesting EU country in accordance with the directive’s Annex I.
It does not apply to:
gas supplied to the EU country which is not satisfied with the level of gas supplied to its solidarity customers;
gas supply to the country which has not been satisfied with its level of solidarity;
the country which does not have the necessary capacity to meet its own gas supply requirements.
In addition, the directive requires EU countries to ensure that:
the gas supply of solidarity customers is not interrupted if:
a natural gas transmission system operator in the requested EU country has not met its capacity requirements;
a gas distribution company in the country concerned has not fulfilled its obligations;
an EU country is not fulfilling its obligations to provide gas to its gas distribution companies in the same EU country.
If a country is unable to provide the necessary gas supply, it must inform the European Commission of the reasons for its decision.
The Commission may decide to suspend or reduce the supply to a customer if it considers that the gas supply is not meeting its obligations.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE APPLY?
The Directive has applied since 1 December 2017.
BACKGROUND
EU gas solidarity
For more information, see:
‘Solidarity for gas’ on the Commission's website.

Summary 22:
Energy labelling requirements for energy-related products and energy-saving appliances
Energy labels for energy - related products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1025/2012 on energy labelling
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down minimum requirements for the labelling and information sheets of energy products and appliances.
It aims to improve consumer choice and reduce energy consumption in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
energy products placed on the market or put into service;
energy-related appliances, including heating, cooling, air-conditioning, lighting, heating and cooling systems;
gas turbines, compressors and compressors;
battery chargers;
electromagnetic compatibility with the EU’s energy efficiency targets;
compulsory maintenance and repair of batteries.
EU countries must ensure that the labels on energy products comply with the regulation and that the information sheet on the label is easily recognisable, simple and concise.
Suppliers and dealers are responsible for ensuring that the label and information sheet are clearly visible on the packaging of the product and on the product database.
Distributors and dealers must also ensure that:
the label is clearly visible, simple, clear and concise;
the information sheet is easy to read and easily accessible; and
the product database is kept up-to-date.
The European Commission may adopt delegated acts to establish specific product groups of products in accordance with a set of specific criteria and in order to establish product-specific information sheets.
the Commission may also adopt implementing acts for specific categories of products.
In the event of non-compliance, EU countries must take the necessary measures to ensure that a non-compliant product is withdrawn from their market and inform the Commission and other EU countries of the results of the evaluation and of the action which they have required the supplier or dealer to take.

Summary 23:
Personal data protection
Personal data processing
SUMMEMBER OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2014 on the protection of personal data
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
  
It aims to ensure that personal data are protected against the risks, rules, safeguards and rights of natural persons, economic operators and public authorities.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to processing of all personal data, whether or not the processing is carried out for commercial, economic or social purposes.
It does not apply to the processing of certain categories of data, such as:
personal data relating to health and safety;
data relating to criminal matters; and
data related to criminal proceedings.
Processing which does not require identification
The data subject has the right to:
have their personal data processed in accordance with the law of the EU country in which the processing takes place;
have the rights to have the processing carried out without their knowledge or consent;
be informed of the processing and of the reasons for the processing.
The processing must be subject to appropriate safeguards, including:
the right to have their data transferred directly from one controller to another.
Transfers to and from a non-EU country are subject to the same level of protection as those provided for in the EU directive on personal data protection (Directive 2000/31/EC);
the processing of their data is subject to a standard contractual clause.
Consultation of the data subject and the European Data Protection Board (EDB)
The EDB is responsible for providing guidance and guidance to the EU countries’ national competent authorities on the application of the regulation.
EU countries must ensure that their competent authorities have adequate level of data protection in relation to processing in their territory.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2015.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
The European Commission has published a report on the implementation of this regulation in the light of the Commission’s work on data protection.
For more information, see:
European Data Protection Regulation (European Commission website
KEY TERMS
	
Personal Data Protection: the right of a natural person to have his or her personal data protected.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Implementing Decision 2014/552/EU of 12 December 2014 on the harmonisation of the laws of the Member States relating to the protection and processing of personal Data (OJ L 183, 14.12.2014, pp. 1-8)

Summary 24:
Harmonised index of consumer prices
Harmonomically defined price stability
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — harmonised index for the harmonisation of consumer price data
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out detailed rules for the implementation of Regulation (EC) No 2494/95 on harmonised indices of price collection in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries, except Denmark, Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland.
It does not apply to non-EU countries.
The European Commission and the European Central Bank (ECB) use the HICP in their assessment of price stability in the EU countries under Article 140 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU (TFEU). The regulation does not preclude, however, the possibility of extending the application of the framework, in the future, if necessary, to the subnational level.
HICP is based on observed prices, which include taxes on products and services, and on taxes on services, such as charges by banks and post offices, and taxes on alcohol, tobacco, gambling of chance, prostitution and illicit drugs.
In addition, it covers:
the harmonised price index of the OOH price index and of the Household Price Index (HPI);
sub-indices of the HPI accounting for less than one part in a hundred of the total expenditure;
the price index for non-foods and non-alcoholic drinks and alcoholic beverages;
taxes on alcohol and tobacco;
other financial services;
services of carpenters.
Implementation of the regulation
EU countries must adopt implementing acts in accordance with the examination procedure referred to in Article 11(2).
The implementing acts must:
provide, where available, electronic records of transactions of transactions such as scanner data, and at the level of detail necessary in order to produce harmonised statistics and to evaluate compliance with the comparability requirements and the quality of the indices.
implement the implementing acts according to the criteria set out in Article 12(3) of the implementing act.
Provide the European Commission with detailed information on the structure of the inventories and the deadline for providing the statistics to the Commission (Eurostat).
Importers of alcoholic beverages and alcoholic drinks must provide Eurostat with detailed data on the prices charged to them by banks, post offices and other financial services.
Each EU country must provide the Commission with a detailed report on the harmonised prices of alcoholic drinks, alcoholic beverages, tobacco and other alcoholic beverages by the end of each calendar year.
Amendments to the regulation have been incorporated into the original text.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGOLATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
For more information, see:
‘The Harmonised Index of Consumer Prices’ on Eurostat’s website.
KEY TERMS
* Household price index: an index based on the observed prices of goods and services of the owner-occupier (i.e. the person who lives in the home) and the price of the goods or services that they buy.
* Non-food item: a product or service that does not have a price.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  И 
Commission Implementing Regulation(EU) 2018/722 of 12 December 2018 on harmonising index of price data in the Member States pursuant to Article 140 TFEU (OJ L 136, 12.12.2018, pp. 1-8)

Summary 25:
Dumping of agricultural products by non-EU countries
Dumping on agricultural products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 952/2013 — anti-dumping measures
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It lays down rules for the imposition of anti-subsidiary* and countervailing* duties on imports of certain agricultural products from non-European Union countries.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all agricultural products originating in the EU, except for certain products originating outside the EU.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EC) No 182/2011 on the application of the principle of subsidiarity.
Implementing measures
Imposition of duties
Importers are required to pay a duty of at least 2 % of the value of the imports they receive.
The duty is calculated on the basis of the average price of the products imported and the price at which the duty is being absorbed by the exporter through a form of compensatory arrangement and the measures are not being reflected in the prices of products subject to measures in the European Union (EU).
Imports must not be made subject to registration for a period longer than 9 months. Imports are subject to import duties of up to 2 % for individual exporters and they remain subject to proceedings and may be reinvestigated in any subsequent review carried out for the country concerned pursuant to the rules laid down in the regulation.
Provisional or definitive duties
Duties may be imposed by the EU countries on the following a request from an interested party to the European Commission.
Duty rates are calculated according to:
the average price paid by the country of origin;
the percentage of the duty paid by each exporter to the EU as a whole or by a group of exporters.
Duration, reviews and refunds
The Commission may, in accordance with the advisory procedure referred to in Article 15(2) of the regulation, accept satisfactory voluntary undertaking offers submitted by any importer to revise its prices or to cease exports at dumped prices, if it is satisfied that the injurious effect of the dumping is thereby eliminated.
An expiry review may be initiated where the request contains sufficient evidence that the expiry of the measures would result in a continuation or recurrence of dumping and injury.
Expiry of measures
The exporter may request the Commission to terminate the measures if it considers that a threat of injury is more likely to be realised if the dumped imports continue. The Commission must provide information to EU countries once it has received sufficient information justifying the reopening of the investigation and the Commission has completed its analysis of the case.
In addition, the Commission may grant exemptions to producers of the product concerned that can show that they are not related to any producer subject to the measures and that are found not to be engaged in circumvention practices as defined in Articles 1 and 2 of this regulation. In addition, exemptions may be granted to producers whose production process, producers' sales and profits are not affected by the measures.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATE APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a number of measures to combat dumping, including:
Directive 2014/56/EU on the harmonisation of the laws of the Member States on the protection of intellectual property rights and on the facilitation of trade in goods between the EU and non-member countries (see summary);
Implementation Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 558/2015 laying down the rules for implementing Implementing Decision 2014/58/EU laying down certain customs measures and implementing Decision (EU), Euratom Implementing Regulation (Euratom) 2018/852 laying down rules on the implementation of Implementing Directive 2014/57/EU (see Summary).
For more information, see:
Dumped imports and Countervailing Measures (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Imports: imports that are not covered by customs duties and which are not subject to a duty.
* Countervention: any practice or work that artificially reduces the price of a product in order to artificially increase its value.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Еграданска бакова гакта  года
Commission Implementing Decisions 2014/59/EU and 2014/60/EU of 20 December 2014 laying down detailed rules for applying Implementing Regulations (EC, Euratas) No 1099/2014 and (EU/EUR) No 852/2014 on the approximation of the rules of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Atomic Energy Community (OJ L 183, 29.12.2014, pp. 1-2)
Successive amendments to Regulation (C) No 1/2014 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.



Summary 26:
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1216/2009 on trade in agricultural subsidies
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules on the application of the EU’s rules on agricultural subsidies.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EC) No 182/2011/2011.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to imports of agricultural products from non-EU countries into the EU. It does not apply to imports from the EU that are subject to a customs duty.
To qualify for a subsidy, it must be demonstrated that the subsidised imports are causing injury to the production or export of the agricultural products concerned.
Importers must prove that the subsidies are causing damage to their production, export or export earnings.
A complaint must be submitted to the European Commission or to an EU country, which forwards it to the Commission.
The complaint must contain all the relevant evidence, including:
the product and the country concerned;
the type and quantity of the imports;
a description of the type of the subsidies and the nature of the damage caused by the imports.
If the Commission considers that the subsidy is causing injury, it may launch an investigation into the complaint.
In the event that an affirmative determination of subsidisation and injury is made, the investigation may continue in accordance with its terms and the provisions of this regulation.
An investigation may be terminated without any further action.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
It entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 1099/2013/2013 on the subject matter of agricultural subsidies (codified version).
It has been amended several times since its entry into force.
For more information, see:
Subsidised imports and countervailing duties (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Countervailing duty: a duty levied on imports of a product which is exempt from import duties or which is not subject to import duties.
* Importers’ customs duties: duties on imports which are exempt from customs duties and which are not covered by import duties, but which are nevertheless subject to customs duties or are not exempted from import taxes.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
  Еграцибликованска гародскога   барка, г.бъракодна болодка

Summary 27:
InvestEU programme for small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and small and mid-cap companies (SMCs)
InvestEU Programme for SMEs and small mid-caps
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2018/1092 on the InvestEU programme
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a dedicated just transition fund to support the EU’s sustainable growth and jobs policy.
KEY POINTS
The InvestEU Programme is designed to help small and micro-enterprises (SMs) and SMEs (micro-cap) to invest in innovative and sustainable sectors.
It aims to provide working capital and investment to support their technological leadership in innovative, sustainable and innovative sectors including by enhancing their digitisation and innovation capacity, and their global competitiveness, and by providing financing for the acquisition of businesses by employees or participation in the ownership of a business by employees.
The programme also aims to contribute to the just transition of the territories identified in territorial just transition plans, established in accordance with the Just Transition Fund Regulation.
To achieve this, the programme is divided into 3 policy windows:
1.
SME policy windows
2.
Small and medium sized enterprises
3.
Medium-sized and small-cap enterprises
The investment policy windows are designed to support SMEs, and SME companies, in particular through:
the provision of working capital, investment and risk financing from seed to expansion stages to ensure their technological and innovation capabilities, and the provision of risk financing, and in innovative or sustainable sectors;
financial support for the development of new technologies;
investment for the establishment of new businesses;
projects related to pollution prevention and control
projects equipped with carbon capture and storage or capture and utilisation installations;
industrial or research projects that could lead to substantial reductions in greenhouse gas emissions, and any regional ring-fencing*.
The InvestmentEU Advisory Hub
The Advisory Board is composed of an Advisory Board, a Steering Board and a fully independent Investment Committee. The Advisory Board and the Investment Committee are appointed for a term of up to 4 years, renewable once and renewable once.
A delegation from a non-EU country is responsible for managing the fund.
FROM WHEN DOES THE IMPLEMENTATION APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘InvestEU’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Just Transition Mechanism: a mechanism to help the EU transition to a low-carbon economy and reduce its greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions.

Summary 29:
Technical support for green and digital initiatives
Transparency, equal treatment and sound financial management of EU countries’ technical support instruments
Technical support measures
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2021/241 establishing a technical support instrument
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a Technical Support Instrument (TSI) to support EU countries in their efforts to tackle the challenges identified by the European Commission during the European Semester (1 January 2021 to 31 December 2027).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The TSI is designed to support the Commission’s work in the field of environmental and social policy in the context of the European Union (EU).
It aims to provide technical support to EU countries to:
foster the green, digital and energy transition;
support the sustainable development of the circular economy and the energy transition, in line with the 2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development;
contribute to the social and economic well-being of EU citizens and to the protection of natural capital, preserving biodiversity and the sustainable use of natural resources;
promote the social inclusion of women and children in the labour market, in particular in the light of the COVID-19 crisis;
encourage the development of sustainable employment policies that take into account guidelines for employment, social inclusion and gender equality.
Objectives
The TSI covers the following areas:
environmental and social challenges, such as climate change and climate change;
economic challenges, including poverty and social inclusion;
social inclusion, gender equality and health;
the protection of children and women;
health and safety;
climate change and resilience.
It also covers the social aspects of climate change, including social inclusion, poverty and health.
Coordination and complementarity
EU countries must:
cooperate with the Commission and the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee of the Regions;
coordinate and coordinate the activities of the Commission, the Parliament and the Council of the EU countries;
provide the Commission with information, communication and publicity on technical support projects;
regularly inform the Commission of projects in the Member States concerned;
make available final studies or reports produced as part of eligible actions set out in the TSI.
Implementation
The Commission is responsible for the implementation of the TSI, including:
implementing the technical support measures;
ensuring that projects are implemented according to the requirements laid down in the regulation;
monitoring and evaluating the effectiveness of the support provided by the instrument.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
The regulation entered into force on 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The ESI is one of a series of measures designed to improve the efficiency of EU policies and programmes in order to reduce the administrative burden on EU countries.
For more information, see:
European Semester 2021-2027 (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* Technical support instrument: a technical instrument designed to provide support to the Commission in its activities in the area of environmental policy.
ACT
Commission Implementing Regulation (EU), Euratom, Euratom of 20 December 2021 establishing a Technical support Instrument (OJ L 294, 20.12.2021, pp. 1-8)
RELATED ACTS

Summary 30:
Rail passengers’ rights and obligations on the EU’s railways (recast)
Rail passengers' rights and responsibilities on the European Union (EU)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1371/2007 — common rules on rail passengers' right and obligations
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down common rules for the carriage of passengers by rail in the EU.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all passengers travelling by rail on the territory of the EU, whether or not they have the right to travel by road or by rail.
It does not apply to:
passengers with disabilities and persons with reduced mobility;
persons with special needs;
travelers travelling by train, bus or other means of transport not covered by the legislation.
Passengers are entitled to compensation for the total or partial loss of, or damage to, articles, hand luggage or animals the supervision of which is the responsibility of the carrier, unless this loss or damage is caused by the carrier.
Compensation for delay in delivery
The passenger is entitled to a refund of the carriage charge and to a temporary replacement equipment or device if the delay is due to the fault of the railway undertaking or by the station manager.
The person with disabilities or the person who is reduced in mobility is also entitled to partial compensation for damage caused by delay in transport.
Amendments to the regulation
Amending the regulation introduces the right of passengers to be reimbursed for damage to their luggage or to their personal effects if the carrier or carrier is liable for the loss of the luggage or damage.
In addition, the regulation allows for the possibility to exempt regional services from certain obligations as regards the provision of through-tickets and re-routing.
Implementing Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2021/852 amends the regulation to take account of the fact that the regulation has been amended several times.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECAST APPLY?
The original regulation was adopted in 2007 and had to be amended in 2013.
BACKGROUND
The European Parliament and the Council of 23 February 2013 acceded to the COTIF.
For more information, see:
‘Passenger rights’ on the website of the European Commission's Directorate-General for Railways (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Carriage charge: a charge charged by the railway company to cover the cost of the transport of passengers between the point of departure and the place of destination.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
    барскаблакова грацик городскога

Successive amendments to Regulation (EC), as amended, have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 36:
European Union’s gross value added (GNI) statistics
European Union's gross value adds (GNIs)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 549/2013 on the transmission of data subject to statistical confidentiality to the European Commission (Eurostat)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the collection, transmission and dissemination of data on the gross national income* (GNI)* of the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation requires EU countries to provide Eurostat with data on their gross domestic product (GDP) aggregates and their components by 1 October each year.
The data must be reliable, exhaustive and comparable.
EU countries must also provide the Commission with information on the sources, their uses and methods used to produce the data.
Each year, the Commission must verify the sources of the data and the methods in the inventory to ensure that the data are comparable and reliable.
Eurostat must publish a report on the methodology used for producing the data at the same time as the national accounts experts of the EU countries.
Every 2 years, Eurostat must send a report to the Commission on the quality and reliability of the GNI data and on the methods used.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
The legislation applies from 18 April 2019.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has delegated the power to adopt delegated acts to ensure the reliability, exhaustiveness and comparability of GNI statistics.
For more information, see:
‘GNI’ on Eurostat's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Gross domestic product: the sum of the gross value of all the goods and services produced by resident producer units.
GDP: the total value added of the final result of the production activity of resident producers.

Summary 37:
EU type-approval rules for vehicles, systems, components and separate technical units following the withdrawal of the United Kingdom from the EU
EU type approval rules for certain types of vehicles
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2016/1628 — special rules to facilitate the placing on the EU market of vehicles and systems, systems and components after the withdrawal from the European Union
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules to ensure that certain types and components of vehicles which have been type-approved by the EU’s single market (the EU) are placed on the market in the EU after the EU withdraws from the UK.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all new and end-of-series vehicles (cars, trucks, buses, coaches, vans and light commercial vehicles) that have been approved by the European Commission or by a national authority of an EU country.
It does not apply to:
vehicles which have not yet been approved in accordance with Directive 2007/46/EC (see summary);
cars which are not yet in service;
cars and trucks which are still in service in the UK but have been withdrawn from service in other EU countries.
Manufacturers must apply to the EU type–approval authority of the EU country of the manufacturer of the vehicle to which the vehicle has been type–approved before 30 March 2019.
The type‑approval may become invalid before that date if:
the manufacturer has not applied for EU type‐approval in the relevant EU country;
the vehicle has not been certified by the relevant national authority in the same EU country as a year before the date on which the UK type‐approved vehicle has become invalid.
If the manufacturer has applied for a EU type approval, the manufacturer must submit a certificate of conformity and proof of conformity to the competent EU authority by 1 January 2019. The certificate must contain the following information:
type of vehicle;
type and type‐certificate of conformity;
manufacturer name and registered number of vehicles;
date of manufacture;
number of vehicles manufactured and registered in the previous year.
Applications for a vehicle type–category of vehicle must be submitted by the manufacturer to the appropriate EU type‑category authority.
Application for a type-category vehicle of the same type may also include any EC type–certificate or UN type‑certificate and its attachments, as part of the whole vehicle typeapproval.
Implementation of the regulation is governed by Regulation (EC) No 552/2013.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 30 March 2018.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
                   	
For more information, see:
Vehicles and systems (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Vehicle type: any type of vehicle, system, component or separate technical unit intended for use on the road or in service.
* End-of series vehicle: a vehicle of more than 10 years’ service life.
