Summary 40:
Early intervention and resolution of failing credit derivatives trading venues
Early intervention & resolution
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1132 on early intervention and early intervention of credit derivatives clearing venues
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE IMPLEMENTING REGULATION?
It aims to improve the early intervention* and resolution procedures for failing credit derivative trading venues (CCPs) in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all credit derivatives traded on the EU’s financial markets.
It sets out the rules for early intervention (i.e. when a CCP fails) and early resolution (e.g. when its assets or liabilities are deemed to be irrecoverable) of failing CCPs.
The resolution authorities must:
make a rapid valuation of the assets or the liabilities of a failing CCP;
prepare a recovery plan and submit it to the resolution authority within 3 to 6 months of the CCP's failure;
identify any measures that may adversely affect the resolvability of the failing CCP.
Implementation of the resolution plan must be subject to the approval or consent of the competent authority.
A resolution authority must examine the recovery plan in order to identify any measures which may adversely impact the resolution.
In the event of a non-default event, the CCP must submit a business reorganisation plan alongside a business restructuring plan.
An early intervention report must be prepared by the resolution authorities within 2 months of its failure.
If a resolution authority considers that the failure of a CCP would not effectively reduce or remove the impediments identified in the report, it must identify alternative measures which would reduce or eliminate those impediments.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULING APPLACE APPLY?
The implementing regulation applies from 1 January 2022.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a series of measures to ensure that the resolution of failed CCPs is as swift as possible.
For more information, see:
‘Early intervention’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 41:
European Year for Railways
European Year FOR RAINWAYS
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2021/852 — promoting rail transport
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION?
It aims to promote rail transport during the European Year 2021 to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and carbon dioxide (CO2) emissions by 90% compared to 1990 levels.
KEY POINTS
The European Green Deal is a new growth strategy that aims to transform the EU into a fair and prosperous society, with a modern, resource-efficient and competitive economy where there are no net emissions of greenhouse gases in 2050 and where economic growth is decoupled from resource use.
The year 2021 will be important for the EU rail policy, since it will represent the first full year where the rules agreed under the Fourth Railway Package will be implemented throughout the EU, namely on the opening of the market of domestic passenger services, on reducing costs and administrative burden for railway undertakings operating across the EU and on providing the European Union Agency for RailWAYS (ERA) with additional tasks that aim to lower technical barriers.
To achieve climate neutrality, a 90% reduction in transport emissions is needed by 2050. For that shift to take place, significant investments are needed, including investments made in the context of the recovery of the Trans-European Transport Network (TEN-T) and efforts to increase the efficiency of the rail freight corridors.
In order to achieve this, the European Commission must take the necessary measures to:
promote rail transport as a competitive and environmentally friendly mode of transport;
encourage the use of rail networks and encourage businesses to switch their transport to rail;
increase investment in rail infrastructure;
improve the safety of passengers and freight;
ensure the smooth operation of rail passenger services;
support the development of the European Rail Traffic Management System (ERTMS), terminals offering modal shift options, as well as modernised rolling stock.
During the year 2021, the Commission should consider initiating a study on the feasibility of creating a European label to promote goods and products transported by rail,
introducing a rail connectivity index, with the aim of categorising the level of integration achieved through rail services on the rail network and showing the potential of rail to compete with other modes of transport.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DECISION APPLY?
The decision has applied since 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The EU is committed to becoming a climate-neutral society by 2050, which means reducing its greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions and CO2 emissions from transport by 90%.
For more information, see:
European Green Deal (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision (EEC) No 852/2011 of 21 December 2011 on the promotion of rail transport for climate neutrality (OJ L 183, 28.12.2011, pp. 1-3)
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Report from the Commission to the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee on the implementation of Decision 2011/973/EEC on the Promotion of Rail Transport for Climate Neutrality (COM(2020) 699 final of 31.12-2.2020)

Summary 42:
European Initiative for the Exchange of Young Officers in the field of cyber security and defence (ESDC) (until 2023)
European Initiative of the Exchange and Development of Experts in Cyber Security and Defence
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (CFSP) 2021/2185 on the organisation and functioning of the European Initiative for a European External Action Service for the exchange of young officers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION?
It sets up a European initiative for an exchange of experts in the area of cybersecurity and defence.
KEY POINTS
The ESDC aims to provide EU countries’ and EU administrations with knowledgeable personnel familiar with EU policies, institutions, procedures and best practices in the areas of cybersecurity, defence and information society (CSDP) and to help promote professional relations and contacts among training and education participants.
The decision sets out the organisation, structure and structure of the ESDC.
Organisation
The organisation is managed by a Steering Committee. It meets at least 4 times a year. It is composed of senior representatives from EU countries and other actors identified by EU countries to support the organisation of ESDC activities.
It is chaired by the Director of EUISS or the Director’s representative. The Board of Directors and the Secretariat are composed of representatives of the EU countries, the European Commission and the European Atomic Energy Agency (EEAS).
The head of the organisation is responsible for ESDC and is selected by a pre-selection panel composed of 3 representatives from the EEAS. The head may delegate this task to one of the Chairpersons of the Board configurations or to a member of the secretariat.
Training and education
ESDC staff consist of:
staff seconded to the organisation by EU institutions, the EU agencies and EU agencies;
staff contracted staff when no national expert has been identified and following approval by the steering committee;
national experts seconded by EU states and EU countries.
Participation in ESDC courses is voluntary and must be based on the following criteria:
a minimum age of at least 18 years;
an average of 2 years of experience in CSDP and relevant CSDP fields;
at least 1 year of training or education experience in a CSDP field.
EU countries may designate one or more institutes to carry out training and/or education activities. The organising and conducting institutes must ensure that this principle applies without any exception.
Financing
Contributions in kind to ESDC are to be made in the form of grants, loans or other forms of financial assistance. The financial reference amount for the period from 1 January 2021 to 31 December 2021 is EUR 2 055 156.
Amendments to the decision
Amending Decision (EU) 2019/852 amends the decision to:
extend the duration of the mandate of the Head of the Executive Committee to 5 years from 20 October 2023;
ensure that the Head is selected on the basis of the vision and objectives set in the vision he or she presented during the selection process;
set out the rules and arrangements governing the creation and functioning by the Board of directors and the secretarial staff.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DECISION APPLY?
The Decision has applied since 20 October 2021.
BACKGROUND
The European Initiative is one of a number of initiatives launched under the European Pillar of Social Rights (see summary).
For more information, see:
European initiative for the European Exchange of Youth Officers (European Commission).

Summary 43:
Reclaiming waste water from urban and agricultural waste
Recovered waste water
Recovering wastewater
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/852 laying down rules for waste water reuse
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the rules for the reclamation of waste water* from urban waste treatment plants and agricultural land to be reused whenever appropriate.
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out the responsibilities of reclamation facility operators and obligations regarding water quality, traceability and transparency.
It also lays down minimum requirements for monitoring to verify that the water is in compliance with the minimum water quality requirements set out in Directive 91/271/EEC on waste water treatment and reuse.
The legislation does not apply to waste water that has been treated in an urban wastewater treatment plant or which has been used for agricultural purposes.
EU countries must ensure that the European Commission, the European Environment Agency and the European Centre for Disease Prevention and Control (ECDC) have access to the data sets on water quality and traceability of reclaimed water.
In addition, EU countries must respond to requests for assistance without undue delay.

Summary 44:
EU blue card for non-EU nationals who work in another EU country
EU Blue card for third-country nationals working in another country
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2014/67/EU on the EU blue card
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It sets out the conditions under which non-European Union (EU) citizens and their families can work legally in the EU without being subject to any discrimination on grounds of sex, race, colour, ethnic or social origin, genetic features, language, religion or belief, political or any other opinion, membership of a national minority, property, birth, disability, age or sexual orientation, as well as short-term mobility.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The directive applies to non-european nationals who have worked legally in an EU country for more than 3 years and who have obtained a higher education qualification.
It does not apply to:
non-EU citizens of EU countries who have been granted international protection by their country of origin;
third country nationals who are not citizens of the EU country in which they have worked since 1 January 2000.
The card is valid for a period of 5 years and can be renewed for a further 5 years after the expiry of the initial 3-year period of validity.
EU blue cards are valid for up to 5 years.
Applications
EU countries may refuse to issue a blue card if they consider that the applicant does not fulfil the criteria set out in the directive.
An application must be submitted to the competent national authority of the country of reference.
If the application is rejected, the applicant must prove that he or she is not a threat to public policy, public security or public policy or public health or safety, or that there is no grounds for rejecting the application.
Where a third country national does not meet the criteria, the country concerned may issue a new blue card.
Application procedure
The form of the application must comply with Council Regulation (EC) No 1030/2002 (14), thus enabling EU countries to refer to the information on the condition under which the person concerned is permitted to work.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
From 1 January 2015.

WHAT DOES THE DIRECTIVES DO?
The blue card is a form of residence permit that allows EU citizens to work legally and live legally in another Member State without any restrictions on their mobility. It allows non-members of their families to live and work in different Member States and to take up residence in different EU countries regardless of whether the non-member of their family is a resident of that Member State or not.
In addition, the blue card allows the holder of the card to be issued with an autonomous residence permit, which allows them to stay in the same Member State for a limited period of time, and to be able to travel between Member States without being required to pay a visa.
This directive complements and complements other EU legislation on the free movement of workers, such as Regulation (EU)(EU) 2019/856 on the rights of workers and their family members to work, study and travel within the EU and on the freedom of movement of students and workers’ family members.

Summary 46:
Family leave and flexible working arrangements for parents and carers - Directive 2014/36/EU (parental leave)
Parental leave and flexibility of working hours
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2016/18/EU on family leave and working arrangements
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
   
 
It aims to improve the rights of parents and childcare workers who are parents or carers.
KEY POINTS
The directive applies to all workers, irrespective of their gender.
It covers maternity and parental leave, paternity leave, flexible working periods and the right to return to the original working pattern before the end of the agreed period.
EU countries are not required to rename or otherwise change the different types of family-related leave that are provided for under national law or collective agreements, including Article 19 of Directive 2006/54/EC.
Employers must ensure that workers who take leave or who request flexible work arrangements are protected against discrimination or any less favourable treatment on the grounds that they have applied for, or have taken, or exercised, parental leave.
The employer must provide reasons for any refusal of such a request or for any postponement of such arrangements.
Flexible working arrangements can change if the need for flexible working conditions can be justified on the basis of a change of circumstances, for example in the case of illness or accident, or in the event of urgent family reasons.
Workers who take parental leave must be able to request to return back to the usual working pattern at the end if justified on grounds of illness, accident or injury or injury.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCELEGAL APPLYORKORKER RIGHTS
The Directive applies from 1 January 2017.
BACKGROUND
The EU has ratified the 1989 United Nations Convention on the Rights of the Child.
For more information, see:
‘Family leave’ on the European Commission’s website.

Summary 47:
Employment contract and employment relationship — minimum rights for workers
Employment agreement and employment contract — minimum rules for workers’ rights
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2017/159 on the minimum rights of workers who have an employment contract or employment relationship
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It lays down minimum rights that apply to every worker in the EU who has a contract or an employment relationship with an employer.
KEY POINTS
The directive applies to all workers, irrespective of the nature of the employment relationship.
It does not apply to fixed-term employment relationships, where no guaranteed amount of paid work is predetermined before the employment starts.
EU countries must ensure that the length of such a probationary period is proportionate to the expected duration of the contract and that any probationary periods are of a reasonable duration.
The minimum notice period should be at least a calendar week from their first working day.
In addition, employers must provide workers with information on the legal framework applicable to their employment contract and the nature and duration of their employment relationship, including:
the expected duration and nature of their work;
the nature and content of the work, including the expected remuneration;
a description of the actual performance of the relationship and the conditions under which the contract is to be terminated.
Employers must also provide training to workers to carry out the work for which they are employed.
Workers should be protected against loss of income resulting from the late cancellation of an agreed work assignment by means of adequate compensation.
Where employers are required by EU or national law or collective agreements to provide training, it is important to ensure that such training is provided equally to workers, including to those in non-standard forms of employment.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
The European Pillar of Social Rights provides that workers have the right to protection against abuse of their rights, including by prohibiting abuse of atypical contracts.
For more information, see:
‘Employment contracts and employment relationships’ on the European Commission's website
KEY TERMS
* Atypical contract: a contract which is not defined by the law, collective agreement or practice in force in each EU country.
* Procedure: a contractual relationship between two or more parties where one or more of the parties does not perform the actual work of the other.

Summary 48:
Criminal sanctions for fraud affecting the EU’s financial interests (Directive 2015/23/EU on fraud and other criminal offences affecting the Union’S financial interests)
Criminal penalties for fraud*
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2016/24/EU — criminal sanctions and other forms of financial crime
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It lays down minimum rules relating to the definition of criminal offences and sanctions in the area of fraud* affecting the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The directive applies to the following types of fraud:
misappropriation of EU funds;
other criminal offences that affect the EU's financial interests.
Penalties
EU countries must provide for certain types and levels of sanctions when the criminal offences defined in this directive are committed. These sanctions should not go beyond the level of financial penalties imposed by national law and should be effective and dissuasive.
In addition, EU countries may provide for sanctions other than criminal sanctions.
Limitation periods for criminal offences
Limit periods are at least 5 years from the time the criminal offence was committed. This period may include extensions of the limitation period arising from interruption or suspension.
The maximum sanction is at least 4 years of imprisonment. The maximum sanction may be reduced to at least 3 years if the offender is subject to the Staff Regulations at the time of the offence.
Exceptions to the maximum sanction are possible, such as:
a maximum sanction of at least 1 year of imprisonment;
an advantage of less than €10 000 or an advantage of €5 000;
a limitation period of no more than 3 years.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLYEARLY ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 6 July 2016.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has published a report on the implementation of the directive.
For more information, see:
‘Financial crime and sanctions’ on the European Commission's website.
KEY TERMS
* Misappropriation: any act or omission that is likely to result in the loss of, loss or loss of a significant amount of money to a third party.
* Other criminal offences: misappropriation, when committed intentionally, constitutes a criminal offence. The intentional nature of such acts or omission may be inferred from objective, factual circumstances.

E-payment fees
E-payments fees
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2014 on interchange fees for consumer debit card transactions
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to improve the functioning of the EU’s single market for electronic payments by removing barriers to the development of a level playing field for card-based payment transactions.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all payment card issuers and acquirers in the European Union (EU).
It does not apply to payment service providers* or to payment card companies.
It applies to:
bank-issued payment cards and payment card schemes*;
universal cards* and payment transactions carried out with universal cards.
In addition, it applies to the following:
interchange fees* for card transactions;
co-badging and choice of payment brand or payment application;
transparency and other measures related to business rules;
payment service providers’ information on the amount of merchant service charges, interchange fees and scheme fees applicable with respect to each category and brand of payment cards;
the amount of the merchant service charge, interchange fee and scheme fee applicable for each category of payment card.
The European Banking Authority (EBA) will submit draft regulatory technical standards to the European Commission by 9 December 2015.

Europass establishes a European framework to help jobseekers and employers to better understand and exchange information on their qualifications and skills.
ACT
Council Decision 2014/856/EU of 20 December 2014 on the European framework for the Transparency and Understanding of Skills and Qualifications acquired in Formal, Non-Formal and Informal Settings, including Through Practical Experiences, Mobility and Volunteering (Europass)
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS DECISION DO?
It establishes a framework to enable jobseekers to better know and exchange knowledge on their skills, qualifications and qualifications.
KEY POINTS
The framework is designed to support jobseekers who wish to move to another EU country and employers who want to recruit workers from other countries.
It is based on a portfolio of five document templates.
The portfolio comprises:
a standardised template for jobseekers’ CVs;
a template for employers to complete their CVs in a standardised format.
An online platform, the Europass online platform is set up and becomes operational.
A user-friendly interface is available to users to enable them to restrict access to their data or persons with disabilities, in accordance with the accessibility requirements established in relevant EU law.
EU countries and bodies must ensure that the format of the portfolio is consistent and that the content of the document templates is easily accessible to all users.
In addition, authentication measures could be used to verify the authenticity of digital documents on skills and qualification.
To facilitate the exchange of information between jobseekers, the European network of employment services (EURES) is a cooperative network for exchanging information and facilitating interaction between employers and jobseekers.
EURES is responsible for developing a web-based information system to support Europass.
WHEN DOES THE DECISION APPLY?

Summary 51:
Statistical coverage of inland waterways transport
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — statistical coverage of the inland waterways of the European Union
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the collection of statistical data on inland waterways in the EU.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
the movement of goods and passengers by inland waterways;
the loading and unloading of vessels and the movement of empty vessels;
transits of goods between EU countries and international (except transit) ports.
It does not apply to inland waterways used by the EU’s external aviation sector.
The European Commission is empowered to adopt delegated acts in accordance with Article 10 concerning the amendment of paragraph 2 of this regulation in order to raise the threshold for statistical coverage in inland waterways to take economic and technical trends into account.
Implementing acts
The implementing acts adopted by EU countries must:
provide the Commission (Eurostat) with a report on the implementation of the regulation and on future developments;
inform the European Statistical System Committee (ESSC) of all the information and data transmitted by the country concerned.
Each 5 years, the Commission, after consulting the ESC, must submit a report to the European Parliament and to the Council on how the regulation is being implemented and on any future developments.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 31 December 2019.

  * KEY TERMS

Summary 52:
European Union statistics on rail transport
Eurostat statistics on railway transport
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/852 — production of statistics on the production of rail transport statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It sets out the rules for the production and transmission of statistics by EU countries on the transport of passengers and freight by rail in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation requires EU countries to report statistics on passenger and freight transport by rail to Eurostat, the European Commission’s statistical office.
The data must be collected using any combination of the following sources:
compulsory surveys;
administrative data, including data collected by regulatory authorities, in particular the rail freight waybill if one is available;
statistical estimation procedures;
data supplied by professional organisations in the rail industry;
ad hoc studies.
Each EU country must report all available data.
Transmission of statistics
EU countries must ensure that:
the national authorities coordinate the data sources used and ensure the quality of the statistics transmitted to the European Statistical System Committee established by Regulation (EC) No 223/2009;
the geographical coordinates and other data needed to identify and map each network segment as well as the links between segments;
information on the characteristics (including the capacity) of the trains using each rail network segment.
Implementation of the regulation
Implementing acts
The implementing acts must be adopted in accordance with the examination procedure referred to in Article 11(2) of this regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2018.
It had to become law in the EU countries by 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The European Parliament and the Council have delegated the power to the Commission to adopt delegated acts.
For more information, see:
Rail transport statistics (European Commission).

Summary 54:
Visa-free travel for non-EU nationals of non-Schengen countries and their travel documents
Visa - visa - non-European Union citizens
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — visa-free entry for nationals of third countries of the Schengen area
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the application of the principle of reciprocity between the EU and non-european countries whose nationals are exempt from the visa requirement.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EC) No 1931/2006 on visa liberalisation.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to nationals of:
non-EU countries, who do not hold the nationality of any EU country, who reside in an EU country and who are holders of a travel document issued by that EU country;
nationals of new third countries formerly part of and stateless persons and other persons who do do not have the nationality or other persons’ nationality, who are not citizens of any country, but who are nationals of a third country, and who have the travel documents issued by the EU country concerned.
Nationals of countries which are not part of the EU but which have the right to take part in some or all of the provisions of the European Economic Area (EEA) are excluded from the regulation’s Annex II to the regulation.
The European Commission may adopt implementing acts to extend the period of exemption from the requirement of the visa. These implementing acts are adopted by the European Parliament or by the Council.
EU countries must notify the Commission of the date of implementation of their visa requirement and the types of travel documents and visas concerned, as well in advance as well as of any preliminary measures that they have taken with a view to ensuring that their nationals do not need to apply for a visa.
If the Commission considers it necessary, or upon request, it may suspend the exemption for a period of 6 months. The period of suspension of the exemption may be extended by 6 months if there is a substantial increase in the risk to the public policy or internal security of EU countries or a substantial decrease in cooperation on readmission.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY INTO FORCE APPLY?
   
It entered into force on 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The principle of reciprocal travel arrangements between EU countries and third countries is one of the main reasons why the EU has adopted a number of measures to ensure that its nationals are not subject to visa requirements.
For more information, see:
‘Visa liberalisation’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 56:
Combating money laundering by means of criminal law (SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2015/849 — criminal offences and sanctions in the area of money laundering
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It aims to combat money laundering through criminal law.
It sets out minimum rules concerning the definition of criminal offences, sanctions and information exchange between EU countries’ competent authorities.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The directive applies to the following types of criminal conduct:
the laundering of instrumentalities and proceeds of crime;
the proceeds of criminal activities derived from the criminal activity from which the property was derived.
Penalties
EU countries must take the necessary measures to ensure that the conduct referred to in points (a) and (b) of the directive is punishable as a criminal offence when committed by persons who committed, or were involved in, criminal activity.
The offence was committed within the framework of a criminal organisation within the meaning of Framework Decision 2008/841/JHA, or by a natural person acting as an obliged entity in the exercise of their professional activities.
Lawyers and officials of EU countries must be held liable where the lack of supervision or control by a legal person has made possible the commission of any of the offences referred to above for the benefit of that legal person by a person under its authority.
In criminal proceedings regarding money laundering, EU countries should assist each other in the widest possible way and ensure that information is exchanged in an effective and timely manner in accordance with national law and the existing EU legal framework.
Reporting
By 3 December 2022, the Commission must submit a report to the European Parliament and to the Council assessing the extent to which the EU countries have taken the necessary steps to comply with this directive.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
The legislation entered into force on 1 January 2016.
BACKGROUND
  
For more information, see:
‘Fighting money laundering’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
 
* Money laundering: the laundering of funds, instruments and proceeds from criminal activities, such as drug trafficking, organised crime, terrorist financing, money laundering and terrorist financing.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 			
Council Directive 2011/33/EU of 12 December 2011 on criminal offences in the field of money-laundering and amending Council Framework Decision 2001/500 on combating money laundering.
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Summary 57:
Recovery of bluefin tuna
Recovering bluefin tunas
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 — rules for the conservation and management of Atlantic tuna
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules to ensure the conservation, management and sustainable management of tuna stocks in the eastern Atlantic and Mediterranean.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all fishing vessels, including:
fishing vessels over 24 metres in length;
caging vessels, traps and farms;
jumping vessels;
captive fishing vessels.
It does not apply to fishing vessels that are not part of the International Convention for the Conservation of Atlantic Tunas (ICCAT) and which are not fishing in the area covered by the multiannual recovery plan.
Fishing authorisations
EU countries must grant or refuse fishing authorisations for vessels that:
catch tuna in more than 24 metres of water;
fry tuna caught by more than 12 metres;
transfer tuna to other countries’ ports or to a non-EU country’s ports;
take the necessary measures to ensure that tuna stocks are not over-fished.
Catching vessels and farms must comply with the rules laid down in the regulation.
Each EU country must keep a record of all prior notifications for the current year and the previous year, as well as a list of vessels that have been granted or refused fishing authorisation.
The EU countries must also keep a register of fishing vessels and of tuna caught in the previous years.
In addition, each year, each country must send a report to the European Commission on the number and weight of tuna caged and released into the sea.
Reporting obligations
Each year, the EU country responsible for managing tuna stocks must send the data for the preceding year to the Commission by 30 June each year. The Commission then forwards the report and the information to the ICCAT Secretariat.
By-catch
The Commission is responsible for collecting data on by-catch, including on:
the number of live and dead tuna caught;
the total weight of live tuna caught and the number of dead tuna released;
by-catch data on the total number of caught and released tuna;
data on the amount of live, dead or dead tuna transferred from transport cages or traps to the sea;
details on the type of fishing gear used;
information on the use of stereoscopical cameras systems in the context of caging operations.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
 
The European Commission adopted Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 609/2013 on the conservation of Atlantic tunas.
For more information, see:
Tuna stocks (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Bluefin tuna: a species of tuna that is highly migratory and highly economically important.
* Caging vessel: a fishing vessel that is used to capture tuna in order to keep them alive and to process them into food.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Еграшкова бласкога   бълга
Council Regulation (EC) No 550/2013 of 13 June 2013 laying down rules for fishing and managing bluefin tuna stocks and amending Council Regulation (Euratom), as amended by Council Decision 2014/852/EU, concerning the conservation measures and measures to be taken by EU countries in the field of fisheries management (OJ L 157, 16.6.2013, pp. 1-8)

Summary 58:
Shipbuilding injurious pricing: protection against sales of ships below their normal value which cause injury to EU industry
Shipbuilding injurious pricing
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2016/1036 — protection against the sale of ships of below-normal value to non-EU countries
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the protection of the EU’s shipbuilding industry against sales below its normal value to third countries.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EC) No 385/96 on protection against dumped imports from countries not participating in the Shipbuilding Agreement (see summary).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to ships of less than the normal value of a comparable price for a like vessel sold to a buyer of the exporting country.
The vessel is to be considered as being injuriously priced if the export price of the vessel sold is less than its comparable price when sold to the buyer of an importing country. If such sales to any appropriate third country do not exist or do not permit a proper comparison, the normal price must be calculated on the basis of the cost of production in the country of origin plus a reasonable amount for selling, general and administrative costs and for profits.
Importers of the ship are responsible for determining whether the sale is injurious to the EU industry.
If the shipbuilder concerned does not pay the charge, countermeasures under the form of denial of loading and unloading rights may be imposed on the vessels built by the shipbuilders in question.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
It entered into force
It has applied since 1 January 2017.
BACKGROUND
The Shipbuilding agreement between the European Commission and the EU countries, the European Free Trade Association (EFTA) and the International Maritime Organisation (IMO) provides for a system of protection against dumping of ships.
For more information, see:
EU Shipbuilding Injurious Pricing Code (European Commission).

WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?

KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:

substances and components intended to be installed on cableways;
safety components intended for the installation of such installations.

importers are responsible for ensuring that the relevant national authorities carry out the necessary inspections of the component concerned.
EU countries must also take appropriate corrective measures to ensure the safe operation of the installations covered by this regulation.

Summary 60:
Accessibility of products and services for persons with disabilities
Assessment and enforcement of the EU’s legislation on the accessibility of goods and services intended for the general public and for persons who are blind, visually impaired or partially sighted
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2016/852 on the approximation of the laws of the Member States relating to the general principles of the protection of persons with disability
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It aims to improve the level of protection of people with disabilities in the internal market of the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The directive applies to products, services and intellectual property rights (IPR) which are intended for sale in the EU.
It does not apply to:
services providing access to audiovisual media services (e.g. television, radio, newspapers, magazines, magazines and newspapers);
information services, such as websites, mobile device-based services including mobile applications developed or made available by operators of passenger transport services within the scope of this directive or on their behalf;
e-ticketing services, electronic ticketing services and interactive self-service terminals.
Manufacturers and economic operators dealing with products must ensure that their products comply with the requirements of the directive.
They must also ensure that:
their products are clearly visible, legible and legible;
their services are easily accessible to persons with visual impairments;
they provide information on how to use the product and how to make it work;
there is a user-friendly and user interface;
the product or service can be used in a manner that is accessible to people with visual or tactile impairments.
they must ensure their products meet the essential functional performance criteria.
EU countries must take the necessary measures to ensure that non-compliant products are withdrawn from their market and inform the European Commission accordingly.
The Commission may, if necessary, propose appropriate legislative measures which could include legislative measures.
In addition, EU countries should ensure that adequate and effective means exist to ensure compliance with this directive and should establish appropriate control mechanisms.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
From 28 June 2016.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘People with disabilities’ on the Commission's website.
KEY TERMS
* Accessibility: the ability of a person with disabilities to use a product, service or intellectual property right.
* Persons with disabilities: any person who is blind or visually impaired and who is unable to read, write or use a language other than their own.

Summary 63:
Enforcement of intellectual property rights in the context of customs action against infringements of EU-wide intellectual property (IPR)
En enforcement of IPR
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — EU application for the enforcement of European Union intellectual property right enforcement
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to make it easier for persons or entities to apply to customs authorities of a single EU country to enforce their intellectual property* rights.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all goods imported into the EU from non-EU countries.
It does not apply to small consignments of goods, such as small parcels of goods in small quantities, which are not intended for export.
EU applications are submitted to the competent customs department of the EU country in which the goods are imported.
The application must contain all the information necessary to determine whether the goods infringe the intellectual property of the holder of the right.
If the customs department considers that the application does not contain all of the information required, it will request the applicant to supply the missing information within 10 working days of notification of the request.
Where the applicant does not comply with the application, the customs authorities may decide to take action against the goods or to place them under a suspensive or free circulation procedure.
Implementation of the regulation is governed by Regulation (EC) No 1383/2003, which lays down rules on the application procedure and on the penalties for infringements.
FROM WHEN DOES THE IMPLEMENTATION APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
 
   
It entered into force on 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for implementing the regulation.
For more information, see:
EU application procedure (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENTS
Commission Implementing Regulation(EU) No 552/2017/965 of 12 December 2017 on the enforcement by customs authorities in the framework of the application for enforcement of EU Intellectual Property Rights
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATING DO?
  It sets out the procedure for applying to customs offices in a single country for the enforcement of EU rights. It also lays down the rules for the seizure, seizure, confiscation and destruction of goods that are suspected of infringing the rights of the holders.
REFERENCES

Summary 64:
EU customs programme
EU Customs programme
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2018/1046 on the European Union’s customs programme (‘the Customs programme’)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the implementation of the EU customs programme.
It aims to promote cooperation between EU countries’ customs authorities in the field of customs and customs control.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies from 1 January 2021.
The programme is implemented by the European Commission under the supervision of a Commission expert group. It is funded by the multiannual financial framework for the general budget of the Union.
Objectives
The objectives of the programme are to:
promote cooperation between the customs authorities of the participating countries in the area of customs control equipment;
encourage customs authorities or economic operators to make full and effective use of the European electronic systems;
support the development of information and communication networks focusing on information processing and exchange, including corporate information technology tools and other technical and administrative assistance needed in connection with the management of the Programme.
Award, complementarity and combined funding
Awards of grants are awarded without a call for proposals where the eligible entities are customs authorities from participating countries, provided that the conditions set out in Article 5 of the regulation are met.
Duties
The Commission must consult experts designated by each EU country in accordance with the principles laid down in the Interinstitutional Agreement of 13 April 2016 on Better Law-Making.
Exercise of the delegated act
The delegated acts are adopted by the Commission on the basis of the advice of the expert group appointed by the EU country.
Implementation of the programmes is governed by Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 541/2014/EU.
Amendments
The Regulation has been amended several times, most recently in 2018.
In 2018, the Commission adopted Implementing Decision 2018/852/EU amending Implementing Regulation(EU) No 1046/2018 on the financial rules applicable to the general budgetary framework of the United Kingdom, Ireland and Northern Ireland (see summary).
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for implementing the customs programme at EU level.
For more information, see:
‘The Customs Programme’ on the Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
  Еграшка года
Commission Regulation (EC) No 2023/2018 of 18 July 2018 on the Customs programme (OJ L 183, 30.7.2018, pp. 1-8)

Summary 65:
European Social Fund (ESF+) for the period 2021-2027
European Social Funds (ESFs) for 2021 to 2027
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2021/694 establishing the European Social Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a European social fund to support EU countries and regions to achieve high employment levels, fair social protection and a skilled and resilient workforce ready for the future world of work.
KEY POINTS
The ESF+ aims to support Member States and regions in their efforts to:
increase employment and social inclusion;
improve the quality of life of the most deprived people;
promote the social inclusion of third-country nationals;
support the social integration of non-EU nationals.
The regulation sets out the eligibility criteria for the ESF+.
It also sets out rules on the use of ESF funding.
Eligible actions
The European Commission has published a list of the types of actions that are eligible for ESF support. These include:
social inclusion and employment policies and actions;
education and training;
skills and employability;
employment and social protection;
training and skills development;
creative and digital skills and skills for the green economy and industrial ecosystems;
environmental and social innovation;
industrial ecosystems.
In addition, the European Commission publishes an annual list of priority investment projects to be supported by EU or national funding. The list is updated by the Commission every 2 years.
Specific objectives
EU countries must allocate at least 25 % of their resources to the specific objectives for the social and employment policy area set out in the regulation’s social inclusion policy area, including the promotion of the socio-economic integration of third country nationals and the development of social inclusion policies.
Where a Member State allocates its resources to a specific objective, it must:
target the least deprived persons, in line with the first subparagraph of Article 7(5) of Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 883/2013 of the European Parliament and of the Council;
provide financial support to the social partners, in particular areas such as education, employment and training, social inclusion and social entrepreneurship;
ensure that social partners are involved in the implementation of the programme;
encourage social innovation and encourage the social innovation of innovative solutions;
facilitate the sharing of best practice and best practice between social partners and the financial actors.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
 
It has applied since 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
European social fund (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* Social inclusion policy: a social policy that aims to improve the level of social protection for the most disadvantaged people in society.
* Employment policy: an employment policy that promotes equal opportunities and access to the labour market and fair working conditions.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Егρημηνηκάντικη γικός (European Parliament and Council Regulation (Euratom) 2019/852 of 21 December 2019 establishing the EU Social Fund for 2021–2027 (OJ L 183, 28.12.2019, pp. 1–8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC) No 752/2013 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 66:
EU solidarity programme for the period 2021-2027 (SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2021/817 on the European Union solidarity programme
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the EU solidarity programme (SPSP) which runs from 2021 to 2027.
KEY POINTS
The SPSP is designed to support solidarity activities in the EU and non-EU countries. It aims to promote the application of international humanitarian law and human rights law, as well as to strengthen the resilience and capacity of vulnerable or disaster-affected communities to cope with and recover from crises.
The programme is open to all EU countries, non-profit and youth sectors.
It is funded by the EU’s general budget and by the European Social Fund (ESF).
The European Commission is assisted by a committee composed of representatives of the EU countries and the European Parliament and of the Council of the European Economic and Social Committee.
Participation of individuals is voluntary and should not have an adverse effect on potential or existing paid employment and it should not be considered a substitute for it.
EU countries may only participate in the programme in its entirety and provided that they fulfil all the obligations which this regulation imposes on EU countries.
Organisations that wish to offer solidarity activities under the programme must first receive a quality label from the European Commission. They must also provide information on their activities, including:
the nature and scope of their activities;
the number of volunteers and the duration of their participation;
their objectives;
participation of young people with fewer opportunities.
In addition, the SSPP supports actions that aim to reinforce disaster preparedness and disaster risk reduction, link relief, rehabilitation and development and contribute towards strengthening the resilience of vulnerable and disaster-hit communities. These actions are compatible with and complementary to the relevant policies, instruments and programmes at EU level, in particular the Erasmus+ Programme.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
For more information, see:
European Union solidarity (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
 	
Voluntary service: an activity undertaken under the European Voluntary Service (Voluntary Service).
Volunteering: a form of voluntary activity that aims to improve the quality of life of people and to contribute to the development of local networks and communities.

Summary 67:
Equal Opportunities Fund
Equitable OpportunitiesFund
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 883/2013 — EGF
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the European Equal Opportunities Facility (EGF) to help EU countries tackle social inequalities and promote equal opportunities between men and women.
KEY POINTS
The EGF is the European Union’s response to the impact of the global financial and economic crisis.
Eligible measures
The regulation sets out the eligibility criteria for the EGF.
The measures eligible for EGF co-financing are:
measures in line with the European Social Fund (ESF+) and the European Regional Development Fund (ERDF);
measures that are part of the European Pillar of Social Rights (PSR) and which are not part of ESF+ or the European Stability Mechanism (ESM);
measures that are not related to the ESF or the ERDF, but which are considered to be part of PSR or ESM, but are not linked to ESF+.
Measures that meet the following criteria:
are part of a specific programme, such as a specific action plan for a specific sector;
contribute to the creation of jobs that require lower qualifications.
Implementing measures
EU countries must submit complete applications when applying for a financial contribution from the fund.
A beneficiary survey is to be conducted and the template to be used. The survey should be open to participants for at least 4 weeks and should be launched during the sixth month after the end of the implementation period.
An evaluation of the results of the beneficiary survey must be carried out by the Commission within 6 months of the end-of-the-programme deadline.
If the Commission considers that a measure does not meet the criteria, it may decide to cancel the financial contribution of the fund to the measure in question.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
From 20 July 2014.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission adopted a communication entitled ‘A new, modern Multiannual Financial Framework for a European Union that delivers efficiently on its priorities post-2020’ in February 2018.
For more information, see:
Gender equality and equal opportunities (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Gender equality: the principle of equal opportunities for all people, irrespective of their gender.
* Equal opportunities: the right of all people to be treated equally in the labour market, regardless of their sex, racial or ethnic origin, religion or belief, disability, age or sexual orientation.
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 68:
Registration of interest representatives in the EU’s interest-related activities register (2014-2020)
Registration of interests representatives
SUMMARY OF:
Agreement between the European Union institutions and interest representatives on the registration of their activities
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND OF THE DECISION?
The agreement aims to encourage interest representatives* to register in the register of EU institutions, bodies, offices and agencies.
The decision approves the agreement on behalf of the EU institutions.
KEY POINTS
The register is designed to facilitate the exchange of information between interest representatives and the signatory institutions on the activities covered by the agreement.
Eligibility and code of conduct
To become a registrant, interest representatives must comply with the following rules:
register on the register and provide information on their activities;
register with the relevant EU institutions and bodies, bodies and agencies, including the European Commission, on the basis of the information provided by them;
ensure that they declare the estimated total annual revenue generated that is attributable to their covered activities, as well as the names of their current clients;
provide the relevant information to the management board of the register, which decides whether they decide to make certain activities conditional upon registration;
participate or support activities that are not covered by this agreement, such as:
membership of Commission expert groups and other EU supported forums and platforms,
participation or support of, or participation in, intergroups and other unofficial grouping activities organised on the European Parliament's premises,
lists of persons with authorisation to access the premises;
the names of persons who are authorised to enter the register;
information on the information submitted by them and the accuracy of their information.
Registration is activated within 20 working days of receiving a notification from the register. Once an applicant has been activated, the applicant must become a registerrant.
Ineligibility
A registrant who is ineligible for registration is notified of the reasons for his or her exclusion. The registrant is given the opportunity to remedy his/her eligibility within 10 working days.
If the registrant does not comply with these rules, the institution may impose sanctions on him/her.
FROM WHEN DOES THE AGENCY APPLY?
   
 
It entered into force on 1 January 2020.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission adopted the agreement in 2014.
For more information, see:
EU interest representatives register (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Interest representative: any person or organisation whose main objective is to influence the formulation or implementation of EU policy or legislation, or the decision-making processes of the European institutions or other EU institutions or bodies.
ACT
Council Decision 2014/852/EU of 13 December 2014 on the signing, on behalf the European Community, of the Agreement between the Union institutions, body, offices or agencies on the Registration of Interest Representatives in the European Interest-Related Activities Register (OJ L 263, 14.12.2014, pp. 1-8)

Summary 69:
Budgetary discipline and cooperation between the European Parliament and the Council of the European Union (EU) and the European Commission on budgetary matters
Budgets and budgetary discipline
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU, Euratom) 2018/1046 on the signing, on behalf of the EU, and provisional application of the Agreement between the EU institutions on budgetary discipline, on budgetary cooperation and on sound financial management
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND OF THE DECISION?
The agreement aims to improve the functioning of the annual budgetary procedure and to ensure sound budgetary management, and to implement a roadmap towards the introduction, over the period of the multiannual financial framework 2021-2027, of new own resources that are sufficient to cover the repayment of the EURI (European Union Recovery Instrument).
The decision approves the signing of the agreement.
KEY POINTS
Objectives
The aim of this agreement is to:
ensure budgetary discipline;
improve budgetary procedure;
cooperate with the Commission and the Member States in the annual legislative work programme;
establish a roadmap for the introduction of new EU own resources.
Cooperation between the institutions and the Commission is based on a number of principles, including the following:
timely exchange of information on budgetary issues;
regular exchange of data on benefits and costs;
the sharing of information between the Institutions on budgetary and financial matters;
data on benefits, costs, costs and benefits;
financial management of EU funds;
sound financial management of the Union’s own resources;
compliance with the EU budget rules.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The Agreement entered into force on 1 January 2019.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS AGREACHIVE APPLY?

Summary 70:
Economic support for COVID-19
Economic support to COVID -19
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/1046 — financial instruments for the response to the COVID crisis
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up a financial instrument to support the EU’s economic recovery in the wake of the crisis caused by COVID (Coordinated action to deal with the impact of COVID).
KEY POINTS
The financial instrument is designed to provide financial support to EU countries and the European Commission to help them recover from COVID.
The measures to be financed under the instrument are:
loans to help EU countries cope with COVID;
non-repayable support, support through financial instruments or provisioning for budgetary guarantees and related expenditure by the EU;
support for agriculture and development in rural areas;
agriculture and rural areas in addressing the impact on poverty and inequalities.
Financing of the instrument and allocation of funds
The instrument is financed up to an amount of € 750 million in 2018 prices on the basis of the empowerment provided for in Article 5 of the Own Resources Decision.
EU countries are required to provide the Commission with the necessary financial resources to implement the measures set out in the instrument.
Implementation of the measures under the Instrument is to be carried out by the Commission or by its executive agencies by 31 December 2023.
In addition, the Commission must prepare a report by 31 October 2022 on the implementation of the Instrument.
To ensure a sustainable and resilient recovery throughout the EU and to facilitate the implementation, the EU programmes under the multiannual financial framework are to be used.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGULATION APPLACE INTO FORCE?
 
   
It entered into force on 31 December 2018.
BACKGROUND
The COVID situation has led to significant disturbances to economic activity which are reflected in a steep decline in gross domestic product (GDP) and a significant impact on employment, social conditions and poverty.
For more information, see:
‘CoVID crisis: COVID’ on the EU's website.

Summary 71:
Stability and growth pact
Sustainable and corrective parts of the Stability and Growth Pact
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE STRATEGY AND GROWTH PACT AND OF THE REGULATION?
The Stability & Growth Pact (SGP) is a series of measures designed to ensure the proper functioning of the economic and monetary union (e.g. the euro area).
The SGP allows the adoption of specific measures in euro area countries which go beyond the provisions applicable to all EU countries.
KEY POINTS
The Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU) allows for specific measures to be adopted by the Council of the EU to safeguard the stability and growth of the single currency area (the euro area) by imposing sanctions on countries that fail to comply with the SGP.
Sanctions in the stabilisation and growth part of the Stabilisation & Governance Pact
The stabilisation & growth pact applies to countries that are not in a position to meet the medium-term budgetary objective and that are making insufficient progress with budgetary consolidation.
The measures include:
an interest-bearing deposit with the European Commission;
an obligation on a country whose currency is the euro to lodge a non-interest-bearing bank deposit with it;
the imposition of a fine on any country that does not comply with this obligation;
a ban on the manipulation of statistics.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 1997.
BACKGROUND
 
The Stabilization and Governance pact has been in force since 1 February 1997. It was amended by Regulation (EC) No 1466/97.
For more information, see:
‘Stabilisation and governance pact’ on the European External Action Service’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Monetary policy: the economic policy adopted by an EU country to ensure that its budget is balanced and that its gross domestic product (GDP) does not fall below a certain threshold.
ACT
Council Regulation (EU) No 552/97 of 20 December 1997 laying down specific measures for the prevention and corrective aspects of the stability & growth Pact
SUMMARY
The stability & governance pact is a set of measures to ensure a proper and sustainable framework for the surveillance of national economic policies.
It allows the Council to adopt specific measures which go above and beyond the general rules applicable to the EU countries, for the purpose of ensuring the proper operation of the monetary union.
In particular, it allows for the imposition of penalties on countries which do not meet the minimum budgetary objective.
Scope
The regulation applies to all euro-area countries except Denmark, Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland.

Summary 72:
Visa for intended stays of no more than 3 months
VISA for longer stays
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 810/2009 — rules on visas for extended stays
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules on the granting of visas for an extended stay of more than three months in EU countries.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to non-EU nationals from non-European Union (EU) countries who are entitled to stay in the EU for a maximum of 3 months.
Visa applications
Applicants must present a valid travel document satisfying the following criteria:
its validity must extend at least 3 months after the intended date of departure from the territory of the EU countries or, in the case of several visits, after the last intended date for departure from another EU country;
it must contain the following information:
the applicant’s name, nationality, place of birth, date of birth and place of residence;
the date and time of entry into the EU country of destination;
a travel document containing the travel document and a stamp indicating that a visa application is admissible.
The application must be assessed on the basis of all available information. Applicants must pay a visa fee of EUR 60.
EU countries may refuse to grant a visa if the applicant presents a non-valid travel document or does not have the necessary documents.
If an application is refused, the applicant must appear in person for a personal interview.
An application may be reviewed by a consular official.
A visa with limited territorial validity is valid for up to 3 months and may be annulled or revoked if it is found to be in breach of the conditions set out in the regulation.
Applications must be submitted to the nearest consular office of an EU country.
Consular offices must be staffed by consular staff who are competent to deal with visa applications and who have the authority to grant or refuse a visa.
In addition, EU countries must ensure that their consulates are equipped with the necessary resources to examine applications and monitor the visa application process.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The original regulation has applied since 1 July 2009.
Amending Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 562/2006 has applied from 1 July 2006.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a series of measures to modernise and simplify the rules governing the application of the Schengen Convention on the Visa and Visas of the European Union (VIS).
For more information, see:
VIS (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Visas: visas issued by EU countries for the purpose of facilitating the movement of persons within the EU.
* Travel document: a travel document, such as a passport or visa sticker, which contains the visa number and the name of the country in which the visa is issued.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
    барска гаркова
Commission Implementing Decision 2009/810/EC of 20 June 2009 on the application for a visa for an extension of stay of no longer than 3 weeks in the Member States (OJ L 136, 22.6.2009, pp. 1–22)
RELATED DOCUMENTS
  г  
Regulations (EC, Euram) No 652/2008 and (EC), Euratom, Euratimes and Euratom Implementing Regulation (Euratom) of 15 June 2008 on the conditions for the granting and revocation of visas and on the procedures and conditions for issuing visas by Member States and repealing Council Regulation (EC).

Summary 73:
Statistics — population and housing data
Statistics — statistics
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2003 on the collection of statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the rules for collecting statistics on the population and the main family, social, economic and housing characteristics of persons, families and households in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries, except Denmark, Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway, Switzerland and the United Kingdom (1).
It requires EU countries to collect statistics on:
the population of the EU;
the main family and social, social and economic characteristics of households; and
the housing of households.
Data collection
EU countries must collect statistics covering the population covering determined demographic characteristics of individuals, families, households and households, as well as on housing at a national, regional and local level, as set out in the annex to the regulation.
The data must be collected by means of:
census data;
statistical data and metadata collected by the European Commission (Eurostat) in electronic form;
national surveys with rotating samples (rolling censuses); and
appropriate surveys with rolling samples.
National authorities must transmit to Eurostat the validated data and the metadata to meet the requirements of data protection.
Implementation of the regulation
Each EU country must adopt a programme of the statistical data and of the metadata, in accordance with the regulation’s programme, to be transmitted to the Commission.
Eurostat is assisted by the Statistical Programme Committee.
In addition, EU countries must report on the data sources and methodologies used to collect the data.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE APPLYORKORK
The Regulation entered into force on the 20th day following its 20th anniversary.

Summary 74:
Rules of procedure for the 9th parliamentary term
Rules of Procedure for the ninth parliamentary session
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2019/302 — rules of procedure
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE RULES OF PROCEDURE?
It lays down the rules for the procedure of the ninth Parliament of the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The rules apply to all legislative acts adopted by the Parliament during the current Parliament’s term.
The Parliament is the legislative body of the EU and has the power to adopt, amend or reject legally binding acts.
It is responsible for:
implementing, amending, repealing, repealing or amending the laws of the Member States, the European Economic Area (EEA) and the Treaty on European Union;
approving or rejecting EU treaties, agreements and treaties, as well as any other acts that are legally binding to the EU;
taking decisions on the implementation of EU treaties and agreements;
considering and voting on legally binding legislation.
Amending or rejecting legislative acts
The Rules of Procedure apply to:
legislative acts adopted in the course of the current parliamentary term (the 9th Parliament term) and any other legislative acts that have been adopted since the end of the previous Parliament term;
the EU treaties (the Treaty of Lisbon and the Lisbon Treaty);
the treaties of the EEA, the Treaty of Rome and the Protocol on the Functioning of the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia;
any other legally binding act that has been adopted by Parliament since the beginning of its term, unless it has been amended or repealed by the Council or the Court of Justice of the former Member States.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The new rules apply from 1 July 2019.
BACKGROUND
The 9th Parliamentary term will be the last term for which the Parliament has a president, vice-president and a quaestor.
For more information, see:
European Parliament (European External Action Service).

Summary 75:
European Data Protection Supervisor (EDPS) — rules on the processing of personal data by EU institutions, bodies, offices and agencies (GDPR)
European Data Privacy Supervisor (EDPB)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2018/1725 — rules for the establishment of an independent authority responsible for ensuring that the fundamental rights and freedoms of natural persons, and in particular their right to data protection, are respected by the EU institutions and bodies, bodies and agencies
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the tasks and powers of the European Union’s independent authority, referred to as the European Data Protection Supervisory Supervisor.
KEY POINTS
The regulation establishes the role of the EDPS.
The EDPS is responsible for:
ensuring the protection of the personal data of all EU citizens and their rights to data security and privacy;
collecting, analysing and analysing data and ensuring that it is processed in a safe and secure manner;
notifying the European Commission of any personal data breach to the European institutions or bodies;
providing the Commission with a report on the data breach.
It is assisted by the Directorate-General for Civil Liberties, Justice and Home Affairs (DGLC) and the European Court of Justice (ECJ).
The director and the Appointing Authority are responsible for the proper functioning of the management meeting of the Management Meeting.
In addition, the director assists the EDPB to ensure consistency and overall coordination of the tasks delegated to him or her by the European data protection supervisor.
A Staff Committee is composed of three members and three deputies, who make proposals on organisational matters and working conditions.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY
  
It has applied since 1 January 2019.

Summary 76:
EU’s own resources — recycling of plastic packaging waste
EU's own resources – recycling of plastics
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Decision (EU) 2019/852 — EU system of own resources
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION?
It sets out the rules for the collection of EU countries’ own resources to cover their annual appropriations for payments.
KEY POINTS
The decision sets up a system of EU own resources.
The system is designed to ensure that the EU has sufficient resources to meet its financial needs.
It aims to reduce the amount of waste generated by EU countries that is not recycled.
EU countries are responsible for collecting, by way of collection costs, 25 % of the amounts referred to in point (a) of Article 2(1) of Directive 2001/40/EC on the collection and recycling of waste from plastic packaging and (b) of packaging waste generated in non-recycled plastic packaging.
This collection rate is set at €0.80 per kilogram.
By 31 December 2058, the Commission will be able to call on the EU countries for up to €1.5 billion of the total amount of EU-wide own resources that it collects from each EU country.
In addition, the European Commission will establish a structured dialogue with national debt management offices and treasuries in respect of its issuance and repayment schedules. The Commission will regularly and comprehensively inform the European Parliament and Council about all aspects of its debt management strategy.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DECISION APPLACE INTO FORCE
  
It entered into force on 1 January 2020.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a package of measures to reduce plastic packaging packaging waste.
For more information, see:
Plastic packaging waste (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Plastic packaging waste: waste generated from the manufacture, import, export or import of plastic containers and packaging materials.
* Recycled plastic packaging: waste from the production, import or export of plastic products and packaging material.

Summary 77:
Wet grip tyre labelling
Wet-grained tyres
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/1242 — rules on the labelling of tyres
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to encourage end-users to purchase tyres with higher wet grip performance by providing them with harmonised information on the wet grip parameter.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all new heavy-duty vehicles with a capacity of more than 10,000 kg.
It does not apply to:
new heavy duty vehicles;
trucks, buses and coaches;
cargo ships;
motorcycles and light commercial vehicles.
Manufacturers must ensure that tyre labels on tyres at the point of sale, as well as in technical promotional material, provide consumers with the relevant tyre parameters at the time and place of the purchasing decision.
Tyre labels must be clearly visible and clearly distinguishable from other information on tyres, such as:
the manufacturer’s name and registered trade name;
the name of the tyre type;
a description of the tyres’ characteristics, including their wet grip class;
specific precautions, if any, that must be taken when the tyre is assembled, installed, maintained or tested;
any other information that may be included in the product information sheet.
Distributors must also ensure that distributors and potential consumers receive the relevant information on tyre parameters when they make a purchasing decision, including:
a list of tyres that meet the minimum and maximum wet grip classes;
details on the tyre label and on the information sheet;
information on the type of tyre, including the weight, racking resistance and rolling resistance (RRC), where appropriate;
instructures for tyres that comply with the requirements of the regulation.
Importers of tyres and distributors of tyres must ensure the tyre labels are clearly visible at all stages of the product life cycle, including during the check-out process, during the installation, during maintenance and during the life cycle of the vehicle.
The manufacturer of a tyre must also provide information on:
wet grip classes, including a list of tyre types and their characteristics, and
the measurement methods used to calculate the RRC and the rolling resistance, where applicable;
how the tyre performs in the event of a significant machine change or any drift in machine control tyre monitoring data.
In addition, tyre suppliers must provide the manufacturer with a product database before placing on the market a tyre produced after 1 May 2021.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
 
It has applied since 1 January 2021 and had to become law in the EU countries by 1 May 2022.
BACKGROUND
  
For more information, see:
‘Tyre labelling’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Wet grip class: a class of tyre that is capable of providing a higher level of wet grip than standard tyres, but which is not intended to be used for road use.

Summary 79:
Electricity transmission system operators
Electricity distribution systems operators
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2019/943 on the unbundling of the transmission system operator’s responsibilities
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It lays down rules to ensure that electricity distribution system operators (TSOs) comply with the rules of the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Transmission system operators are required to:
ensure that their network activities and supply and generation activities are independent from each other;
provide the relevant information to the European Commission, the European Energy Regulator (Euratom) or the European Atomic Energy Community (ACER) on the operation and operation of their network;
take the necessary measures to protect consumers’ rights and ensure that their energy bills are fair and transparent;
cooperate with the relevant national authorities to ensure the proper functioning of their networks.
The directive repeals Directive 2012/27/EU.
KEY TERMS
* Transmission system operator: a company that operates a transmission system and manages the transmission of electricity, gas, electricity and other energy-related products and services.
* Distribution system operator (DSO): a vertically integrated undertaking that is responsible for the operation of a network of transmission systems and for the supply and distribution of electricity and gas.
