Summary 80:
European High Performance Computing Joint Undertaking (EPCJoint Undertaking) (until 31 December 2033)
Europa’s Joint Innovation Fund supports the development and uptake of high-performance computing and quantum computing technologies, systems and applications.
ACT
Commission Decision (EU) 2020/852 of 19 February 2020 establishing a European High Performance Computers Joint undertaking.
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS DECISION DO?
It establishes a European high performance computing joint undertaking (e.g. EPCJ) for a period of 2033.
It aims to provide and manage access to a federated and interconnected supercomputing and data infrastructure and its services, as well as to training facilities and skills development opportunities.
KEY POINTS
The EPCJC is part of the Horizon Europe programme for research and innovation. It is funded by the European Union (EU), the European Commission, the European Atomic Energy Community (Euratom) and the European Economic and Social Fund (EESFF).
It is managed by a Governing Board composed of representatives of the participating countries and chaired by the Commission.
The Governing board is responsible for:
setting out the objectives and objectives of the EPCQJ;
identifying priorities covered by the programme;
designing the work programme for each year;
assessing the costs of implementing the programme.
Management of contributions from participating countries
The participating countries contribute to the cost of acquiring and owning high-end supercomputers and quantum simulators. The remaining total cost of ownership of the hosting entities is covered either by the hosting country or by the participating states in the hosting consortium, possibly supplemented by the contributions referred to in Article 6 of the Decision.
In addition, participating countries are responsible for ensuring the security of the supply chain and for the reimbursement of the costs incurred by the host entities.
FROM WHEN DOES THE DECISION APPLY?
The decision has applied since 20 February 2020.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission launched Horizon Europe in 2009.
For more information, see:
Horizon Europe (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* High-performance computer: a computer capable of performing complex calculations at a very high level.
* Quantum computing: a computing system that operates on a quantum state of the art.

Summary 81:
Climate-neutrality objective for the EU’s 2030-2050 climate policy
Climate - neutrality goal for the 2030-40 climate policy			
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — climate-neutralisation objective
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that the EU's 2030 climate policy is compatible with, and contributes to, the Paris Agreement and the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change (the UNFCCC).
KEY POINTS
The objective is to:
contribute to a low-carbon economy;
reduce greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions and removals in a cost-effective way;
ensure a high level of environmental protection and the improvement of the quality of the environment in accordance with the principle of sustainable development.
To achieve this objective, the EU is committed to stepping up efforts to tackle climate change and to deliver on the implementation of the Paris agreement adopted under the UN Framework Convention (the ‘Paris Agreement’), guided by its principles and on the basis of the best available scientific knowledge, in the context of the long-term temperature goal of 1.5°C above pre-industrial levels.
The EU is also committed to addressing climate change-related risks as well as climate change vulnerability and adaptation assessments into investment and planning decisions under the EU budget.
In order to achieve the objective, all relevant EU legislation and policies need to be consistent with and contribute to the fulfilment of the climate neutrality objective while respecting a level playing field.
A climate advisory board is set up to advise the Commission on the development of the EU climate policy. The Advisory Board is composed of representatives of national climate advisory bodies and experts from the EU countries. The Commission must take into account the advice of the Advisory Board and, where adopted, the relevant Union legislation implementing the EU 2030 climate target.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
 
 		 	
The Paris Agreement was signed in December 2015 and aims to reduce global warming to well below 2°C by the end of the century.
For more information, see:
‘Climate neutrality’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Climate neutrality: the objective of reducing greenhouse gas emissions and removing them from the atmosphere in a way that does not harm human health, the environment or the economy.

Summary 83:
Cultural and media strand of the European Union’s Horizon 2020 programme
Culture and media sector of the Horizon 2020 Programme
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/790 — European Union programme for culture and media
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the EU programme for cultural and media.
KEY POINTS
The programme covers the following sectors:
cinema and audiovisual works, including heritage works;
creative industries, such as music, film, television and digital media;
education and culture;
environmental and climate action, cohesion, regional and urban policy, sustainable tourism, State aid, mobility and international cooperation and development.
The main objectives of the programme are to:
promote and improve access to European cinema and television works, in particular through audience development measures, including film literacy;
encourage the creation of, distribution of and access to cultural works in the new digital environment, including through innovative business models, and to support the engagement and development of audiences of all ages, particularly young audiences, across Europe and beyond.
In addition, the programme supports the following activities:
the European Heritage Label (the ‘European Heritage Label’), the European Heritage Days, European prizes in the areas of contemporary, rock and pop music, literature, heritage and architecture and the European Capitals of Culture;
supporting the work of the Observatory of European Cinema and Audiovisuality (OCCA);
promoting the creation and distribution of European films and television series;
providing technical and administrative assistance to the OCCA;
contributing to the development of European film and television production and distribution.
Actions under the programme must comply with the following conditions:
they must be carried out in line with the objectives set out in Annex I to the regulation;
they should not duplicate or crowd out private financing or distort competition in the internal market.
They must be implemented in accordance with the rules laid down in Annex II to the programme.
Annex III sets out how the programme is financed.

Summary 85:
Aromatised wine products — protection of the geographical indications of certain aromatised wines and their production methods
Aromatic wine products – protection of their geographical indications
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1169/2011 — rules on the definition, description, presentation, labelling and protection of certain aromatic wine products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the protection of geographical indications* and the production methods of aromatisation of certain wine products.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to wine products produced in accordance with certain rules and restrictions, which guarantee that consumer expectations as regards quality and production methods are met.
It does not apply to:
wine produced in a non-traditional production method, such as the blending of grapes with other wine varieties;
wine which is not produced under traditional production methods; or
wine that is produced under a traditional production method.
The European Commission is empowered to adopt delegated acts to ensure product quality and traceability, including checks and verification to be carried out by the EU countries, including testing.
In addition, the Commission is assisted by the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) and the Committee on aromatising wine products, which assists the Commission in the implementation of the regulation.
Existing geographical designations may be supplemented by a customary name, provided that:
the name is protected in its country of origin;
the product is produced in the territory of the producer;
it is produced by a single producer, or in exceptional cases by a group of producers;
a single producer name in question is protected;
there is no risk of confusion between the name and the product’s final product.
EU countries must ensure that the product specification is published in the Official Journal of the European Union (OJ) and that it is accompanied by a list of the names and addresses of the producers of the product, as well as by a description of the production method used.
Regulations (EC) No 882/2004/2004 and (Euratom) No 1269/2008 on the classification and labelling of wine products (see summary).
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?

Summary 86:
Catch limits for certain species of fish in EU waters in 2020
Catch limit for certain types of fish
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2020/2021 — catch limits for some species of certain fish
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the total catch limits (TACs) for certain fish species in the EU’s exclusive economic zone (EEZ) in 2020.
KEY POINTS
The TACs are set out in Annex I of the regulation.
The regulation applies to the following species:
cod in the EEZ of the European Union (EU);
deep-sea sharks of the Selachimorpha super-order;
selected dogfish (Squalus acanthias);
southern swordfish (Xiphias gladius) south of 20° S by longliners.
It does not apply to certain by-catches of swordfish caught in the Kattegat.
EU countries must ensure that catches of certain species do not exceed the limit set in Annex II.
Fisheries in EU and international waters of 1 and 2 are subject to a precautionary TAC (Annex III).
The European Commission is responsible for setting the TAC for certain fishing species.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The 2020 TAC applies from 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
   
The EU has adopted a number of measures to ensure that fish stocks in its EEZ are not overfished.

Summary 87:
EU macro-financial assistance to Ukraine
EU macro–financial assistance for Ukraine
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2020/852 — EU macro–fiscal assistance
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION?
It provides for the European Union to provide financial assistance to the government of Ukraine to help it implement reforms in order to improve its economic and financial situation.
KEY POINTS
The decision authorises the European Commission to provide the EU’s financial assistance in the form of loans of up to €1.5 billion to Ukraine.
The loans are to be made available by the Commission in two equal instalments, each of which will consist of a loan. The loans will have a maximum average maturity of 15 years.
Under the conditions set out in a memorandum of understanding (MOU), the Commission will agree with the Ukrainian authorities on clearly defined economic policy and financial conditions, focusing on structural reforms and sound public finances, to which the assistance is to be subject.
In order to ensure uniform conditions for the implementation of the decision, implementing powers will be conferred on the Commission. The Commission will inform the European Parliament and the Council of developments in the operations referred to in the MOU, as well as the European Economic and Social Committee (EESC) and the European Stability Mechanism (ESM).
The assistance will be implemented under direct management.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DECISION APPLY?
 
It entered into force on 1 January 2021.
It has applied since 1 January 2022.
BACKGROUND
Ukraine is covered by the European Neighbourhood Instrument (ENPermanent Structural and Investment Facility for Financial Cooperation and Development (ESIF) programme.

Summary 88:
Management, conservation and control measures for Mediterranean swordfish in the context of recreational fishing in the Atlantic
Management, conserving and controlling measures for certain species of Atlantic swordfish
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2017/2107 — management, conservation, technological conservation, control and monitoring measures applicable in the Convention area of the International Commission for the Conservation of Atlantic Tunas (ICCAT)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out measures to manage, conserve and control the sustainable management and control of certain species* of Atlantic tunas (Mediterranean swordfish).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to vessels flying the flag of EU countries that:
fished for, retained on board, transshipped, transported or landed, or intend to land, in the area covered by the ICCAT Convention;
fisheries that are engaged in recreational fishing.
It does not apply to vessels engaged in commercial fishing or to vessels that are not part of the EU’s exclusive economic zone (EEZ).
EU countries may decide to use the number of vessels flying their flag that fished for or have landed, transferred, landed or landed the quota for the period 2013–2016 for the purpose of calculating the capacity limitation, if that number is lower than the average yearly number of fishing vessels during that period.
The European Commission is responsible for implementing the regulation.
Monitoring and surveillance
Each year, EU countries must submit an annual report to the European Commission on the number and type of vessels that have been authorised to fish for, retain on board and land Mediterranean swordfishing gear types.
Each EU country must inform the Commission without delay when the uptake of the quota allocated to a fishing gear type is deemed to have reached 80% or more.
Vessel monitoring and surveillance systems
The Commission must set up a vessel monitoring system to monitor and monitor the use of fishing gear by EU countries’ fishing vessels.
An annual report must be sent to the Commission by 30 June of each year.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGULTRY APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
The EU is a party to the International Convention for the conservation and management of the marine life of the Atlantic Tuna, the largest fish species in the world.
For more information, see:
‘Mediterranean Swordfish’ on the ICCT website.
KEY TERMS
* Maritime swordfish: swordfish caught using harpoons or pelagic longlines.
* Fishing gear type: harpoons used to capture swordfish using a hook size smaller than 7 cm in height.

Summary 90:
Sustainable fisheries and the conservation of marine biological resources (EMFAF)
Sustainable Fisheries and the Conservation of Marine Biological Resources (EMFF)
The European Union (EU) is providing financial support to the European Maritime and Fisheries Fund (EMF), which is responsible for managing the EU’s seas and oceans.
ACT
Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/1046 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 18 July 2018 laying down the priorities of the EMFAF, its budget and the specific rules for providing EU funding.
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It sets out the priorities and rules for the EMFF.
KEY POINTS
The EMFF is a key enabler for sustainable fisheries and conservation of aquatic biological resources, for food security through the supply of seafood products, for the growth of a sustainable blue economy and for healthy, safe, secure, clean and sustainably managed oceans and seas.
It is funded by the general EU budget and is managed by the European Commission.
The general rules apply to all EMFF programmes and operations under the 2014-2020 programming period.
Specific objectives
The objectives of the EU EMFF are to:
contribute to the sustainable management of the oceans, seas and biological resources;
ensure that the oceans are clean, safe and sustainable;
support the sustainable development of the blue economy, which is based on the sustainable use of the marine environment;
promote the sustainable exploitation of marine biodiversity and the sustainable utilisation of marine resources.
Support for sustainable fishing activities
The EU supports the permanent cessation of fishing activities and the joint first acquisition of a fishing vessel by several natural persons who fulfil the conditions for a reduced period of inadmissibility.
In addition, the EU provides financial support for:
the sustainable management and management of fisheries;
fisheries overcapacity and overfishing;
measures to reduce the impact of climate change and acidification on the oceans and on marine life;
environmental and climate change-related measures to protect marine life and to improve the environmental performance of marine ecosystems;
management of marine protected areas (MPAs) and the protection of marine mammals and birds;
prevention of marine pollution and the management of marine litter;
protection of marine habitats;
the protection of the biodiversity of marine and terrestrial ecosystems and of marine life.
Other objectives
Support is also provided for projects that contribute to aquaculture providing environmental services, as well as to ensuring animal health and welfare.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The regulation entered into force on 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The EFMF was established under Regulation (EC) No 1296/2013.
For more information, see:
‘Sustainable fishing’ on the EMAF's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU), Euratom, Euratas, Euronews, of 24 July 2018 on the priorities, budget and specific rules of the Environmental and Marine Fund and repealing Regulations (EC, Eur) No 1304/2013, (EC), No 1309/2013 and (Eur) No 223/2014 of the General Assembly and repealing Council Regulation (EEC) Nos 1304-2013 of 22 June 2013 on the financial rules applicable to the general budget of the Union (OJ L 183, 28.7.2018, pp. 1-8)

Summary 91:
Convention on the Conservation and Management of Straddling Fish Stocks and Highly Migratory Fish Species (IATTC)
Convention of the International Tribunal for the Law of the Sea and the Agreement for the Implementation of that Convention
SUMMARY OF:
Decision 98/392/EC on the conclusion of the United Nations Convention relating to the conservation and management of straddling fish stocks and highly migratory fish stocks
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION AND THE CONVENTION?
The decision approves the UN Convention on the conservation of species of fish stocks (known as the IATTC Convention) and the agreement for the implementation of the Convention on sustainable fishing practices.
The agreement aims to ensure that all fishing vessels in the area covered by the convention comply with the rules laid down in the convention.
By its decision, the Council approved the conclusion, on behalf of the EU, of the agreement.
KEY POINTS
   
The IatTC is a multilateral organisation set up under the International Convention for the Conservation of Species of Wild Fauna and Flora (ICSF).
The convention applies to all EU fishing vessels used or intended for use for the purposes of fishing in the areas covered by it.
EU countries must:
ensure that all vessels fishing in this area comply with all the rules set out in the annex to the agreement;
provide the International Maritime Organization (IMO) with a copy of the observer report on alleged incidents involving assault or harassment of the observers;
implement a monitoring programme to collect data on the number of discards and releases of Mobulid rays, as well as on the status (dead or alive) of sharks.
Fishing vessels are also prohibited from:
fishing on data buoys;
using any sealed wells on-board the vessel;
towing out of a purse seine net.
Observers must report to the Commission any instances of sealed wells being used for storing fish.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATION APPLY?
It has applied since 29 July 1998.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
The Convention on Sustainable Fishing Practices was adopted in 1982.
For more information, see:
‘The International Treaty on the Law and the Management of the Seas’ on the European Commission’s website.

Summary 92:
Common understanding on delegated and implementing acts and on the implementation of the Lisbon Treaty
Common agreement on delegated or implementing acts
SUMMARY OF:
Common Understanding on Delegated and Implementing Acts
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND OF THE DECISION?
The agreement establishes a common understanding between the European Parliament, the Council and the European Commission on the application of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU) and on implementing acts.
The decision adopts the agreement on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
Delegated acts
The three institutions recognise the need for the alignment of all existing legislation to the legal framework introduced by the Lisbon treaty, and in particular the need to give high priority to delegated acts, within the limits of the Treaties.
To achieve this, they agree to:
improve the efficiency and effectiveness of the legislative process by:
implementing delegated acts more frequently and in full respect of the principle of subsidiarity and proportionality;
using the legislative technique of recasting for the modification of existing legislation more frequently;
improving cooperation and information-sharing between the three institutions;
ensuring the effective implementation of delegated acts;
encouraging the participation of small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and other end-users in the legal process.
Implementing acts
In addition, the agreement sets out a common framework for implementing delegated acts and their implementation, including:
the use of the recasting technique for the amendment of existing laws;
the harmonised rules on the use of delegated legislation;
ex-post evaluation of existing law;
transposition of directives;
implementation and application of directives.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
  
The Agreement entered into force on 1 January 2016.
BACKGROUND
The EU’s Lisbon Treaty has been amended several times.
For more information, see:
The Lisbon Treaty (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENTS

Summary 93:
Citizens’ initiatives — registration and verification of statements of support (CITIS)
Citizens' initiatives — registering and verification OF STATEMENTS OF SUPPORT
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on the registration and verifying of statements on support for citizens’ initiative
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
It sets out the rules for the registration of statements* of support* for citizens' initiatives.
KEY POINTS
Organisers of citizens' initiative
The aim of the regulation is to make it easier for citizens to submit a proposal for a legal act of the EU for the purpose of implementing the Treaties similar to the right conferred on the European Parliament under Article 225 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU) and on the Council under Article 241 TFEU.
The regulation applies to all EU countries, except Denmark, Ireland and the United Kingdom (1).
It does not apply to:
non-EU countries, such as Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland;
the United States of America, Canada, Australia and New Zealand.
Organisations must collect the necessary information from signatories in paper or electronic form to verify their support for a citizens‘ initiative.
Signatories must be EU citizens of the age to be entitled to vote for the initiative and to submit their support to the Commission. The minimum number of signatories required in each EU country should correspond to the number of Members of Parliament elected in each Member State multiplied by 750.
EU countries must ensure that organisers are subject to appropriate penalties for infringements of this regulation and in particular for:
false declarations made by organisers;
fraudulent use of data.
National authorities must verify that the organisers comply with the regulation’s rules and that the information collected by the organisers is accurate and complete.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2014. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2016.
BACKGROUND
Citis (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* CITIS: an initiative which invites citizens to vote in a European Parliament, Council or other legislative body.

Pesticides: statistics on the use of pesticides and their use in the EU (2009-2013)
Pesticide statistics: data on the application of pesticides
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1107/2009 on the statistical collection, transmission and processing of data on pesticides
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the collection and transmission of statistics on pesticides used in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation requires EU countries to collect and transmit to the European Commission (Eurostat) and the European Agricultural Statistics Office (ESO) data on pesticide use in their territory.
The data must be collected, transmitted and processed in accordance with the rules laid down in Annex II of the regulation.
EU countries must compile statistics on pesticide applications for each selected crop within a reference period.
Data collection and processing must be carried out by EU countries’ competent authorities.
Eurostat must assess the quality of the data transmitted.
Each EU country must collect and send to Eurostat the data it receives from EU countries on the pesticide use of each crop and the number of pesticides applied.
In addition, EU countries must ensure that the data collected and transmitted are accurate, reliable and comparable.

Summary 95:
Authorisation for plant protection products
Authorisation of plants and plant products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2006 on the application for authorisation for the use of certain substances in plant protection
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules and procedures for granting authorisations for the manufacture, sale and use of plant protection* products.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to substances, including micro-organisms having general or specific action against harmful organisms or on plants, parts of plants or plant products, referred to as ‘active substances’.
It does not apply to substances that have been classified as pesticides.
Authorisations are granted at EU level on the basis of harmonised criteria.
EU countries must apply the following criteria when granting authorisation:
the active substance must be safe for human and animal health and the environment;
the plant protection product must not be harmful to human or animal health or the environment.
The application must be examined by the EU country proposed by the applicant, unless another EU country agrees to examine it.
Applicants must provide samples and analytical standards, as well as information on plant health and environmental conditions relevant to use of the product in question and representative of the conditions prevailing in the zone where the product is intended to be used.
Applications must be submitted to the competent authority of an EU country for approval within 6 months of receiving the application.
An EU country may withdraw or amend its measure if it concludes that the objectives of the authorisation are not achieved or that the application does not meet the criteria set out in the regulation.
Reporting and exchange of information
The applicant must provide the competent authorities of the EU countries with information on the substances covered by the regulation, including information on their use and the results of the tests and studies carried out on the active substance, safener or synergist, or of adjuvants used in the product.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2007.
BACKGROUND
The plant protection market in the EU is one of the largest in the world.
For more information, see:
‘Plant protection products’ on the European Commission’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Active substance: any micro-organism that has the ability to act as a natural or legal agent against a harmful organism or plant.
ACT
Commission Implementing Regulation (EU) No 550/2006 of 20 December 2006 laying down the rules for the application of certain active substances to the manufacture and sale of certain products intended for use in the Community and repealing Directive 91/414/EEC (see summary)

Summary 96:
SOLVIT Information Management Interface (MII)
SOLvIT Information Migrations Interface (IMI)
The SOLVIT information management interface (IMI) enables the exchange of information between European Union (EU) countries and the European Commission.
ACT
Council Regulation (EC) No 552/2012 of 15 December 2012 establishing a European Information Management Infrastructure (IMIs)*
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It sets out the rules for the use of information management interfaces (MIIs)* by EU countries.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all EU countries and to the Commission. It does not apply to non-EU countries, unless a specific EU act provides for a role for the Commission in such cooperation.
EU countries must ensure that the rights of data subjects are respected when processing their personal data.
Each EU country appoints one or more IMI coordinators to carry out any of the tasks listed in the regulation, in accordance with its internal administrative structure.
The national IMI coordinator is assisted by a committee composed of representatives of the EU countries, the European Data Protection Supervisor (EDPS) and the Commission, and is responsible for ensuring the proper functioning of the IMI network.
Information exchange between EU countries
The European Commission and EU countries may exchange information using IMI between their competent authorities.
If an EU country is an IMI actor, the Commission may act as an interlocutor of the Commission on any exchange of personal data processed in IMI with its counterparts in a third country.
When data subjects do not give their consent, the data processing may be carried out without their knowledge or consent, unless the processing is requested for overriding reasons in the public interest.
Data subjects have the right to be informed and to have their rights respected when data processing is carried out by their competent authority.
Rights of data subject
Information to data subjects and transparency must be provided by the competent authority, in cooperation with the European data protection supervisor.
An IMI user must be able to exercise their rights as data subjects in the context of the processing of their data, including:
processing by means of IMI without the data subject’s consent;
processing of special categories of data, such as medical records and personal data;
being able to submit requests for processing;
access rights to their IMI users in the internal market area for which it is competent.
In addition, data subjects must be informed of any limitations on or exceptions to their rights.
REFERENCES
Act
Entry into force
Deadline for transposition in the Member States
Official Journal
Regulation (Euratom) No 609/2012

Summary 97:
Fishing in the Mediterranean and Black Sea: rules to prevent, deter and eliminate illegal, unreported and unregulated fishing (GFCM Agreement)
Fishing on board, transhipment and landing of fish and shellfish caught in the GFCM agreement area
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1224/2009 on the rules for the enforcement of the General Agreement on the Conservation of the Common Fisheries and Marine Living Resources in the Eastern Mediterranean and the Black Sea
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for enforcing the general agreement on the conservation of the common fisheries and marine living resources in the European Union (EU)’s eastern Mediterranean and black seas.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to vessels of more than 15 metres in overall length that are not on the EU fleet register.
It does not apply to:
fishing vessels of less than 10 metres in length;
fisheries using fish aggregating devices (FADs);
common dolphinfish (Coryphaena hippurus) fisheries using FADs; and
common tunas and common tunas caught using fattening devices.
Penalties
EU countries must take the necessary measures to prohibit fishing, retention on board and transshipment of fish, retention of shellfish and the landing of certain species of fattened fish and crustaceans in the area covered by the agreement.
Vessels of an overall length of 15 metres or more are subject to the following penalties:
a ban from 1 January to 14 August of each year;
the exclusion from the EU Fleet Register of authorised vessels;
a prohibition of fishing vessels from the area in which the agreement is signed.
The European Commission must report to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Scientific, Technical and Economic Committee for Fisheries of all catches from such fishing operations.
Reporting of statistical matrices
The Commission is responsible for collecting statistical data on the fishing activities of vessels in the agreement area.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2010 and had to become law in the EU countries by 1 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
The agreement between the EU and the countries of the Mediterranean, Black Sea and the Gulf of Finland is one of a number of multilateral agreements between the European Community (now the EU) and its Member States.
For more information, see:
‘Fisheries’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Fattening device: a fishing net designed to capture and hold fish and/or shellfish using a fish aggregation device.

Summary 98:
Uniform patent protection within the internal market: unitary patent protection
Uniform product patent protection — unitary product protection
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1260/2012 — enhanced cooperation in the area of unitary application of the European patent with unitary effect
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the granting of a European patent to a non-EU country in the field of product invention.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to products which are patented in more than one EU country.
It does not apply to patents which are covered by national laws.
The European Patent Office (EPO) is responsible for administering the European Patent Organisation’s (EPC) rules on the grant of patents.
EU countries are required to ensure that the EPO publishes in its European Patent Bulletin the name of the EU country in which the patent has been granted, as well as the date of publication of the grant, in the national patent register of the participating EU countries.
When a patent is granted, it is treated in its entirety and in all the EU countries as a national patent of the country where the EPC has its headquarters in accordance with Article 6(1) of the Treaty on European Union (TFEU).
The EPO may grant a patent to any person who:
is prepared to allow any person to use the invention as a licensee in return for appropriate consideration;
has the right to oppose further commercialisation of the product; or
is willing to grant a license to any other person who is prepared to make use of the invention for commercial purposes.
In addition to the list of EU countries, the European Commission must report to the European Parliament and the Council on the operation of the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLYEAR OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
It entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
For more information, see:
Unitary patent protection (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Product invention: any invention which has the potential to be used for the manufacture of a product.
* Unitary patent: a patent which has a single object of property, such as a product or a service, which is protected by a single legal instrument.

Summary 99:
European Observatory on Counterfeiting and Piracy
European Observatory On Counterfeit andPiracy
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2014 on the European Observatory on Infringements of Intellectual Property Rights
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
  
It sets up a European Observatory (EOP) on counterfeiting and piracy.
KEY POINTS
The EOP is a centre of excellence on information and data relating to infringements of intellectual property rights.
It is managed by the European Commission, the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee (EESC).
It collects and disseminates information on intellectual property infringements on the EU’s internal market.
The European Commission is responsible for the operation of the EOP.
In order to carry out its tasks, the Office:
cooperates with national authorities, the private sector and the EU institutions relating to the enforcement of the intellectual property right and in particular their activities in the fight against infringement of those rights;
organises meetings of representatives from public administrations, bodies and organisations in the EU countries dealing with intellectual property, as well as private-sector representatives;
publishes a management report every 3 years on the activities of the Office and on the results of its work.
Implementation of the regulation
The regulation does not prevent EU countries from exercising their competences.
EU countries must ensure that the OOP is able to collect and disseminate information on copyright infringements and on piracy on the basis of reliable and comparable data.
To carry out the tasks of the Observatory, it must:
ensure that the information it collects is made available to the relevant national intellectual property offices;
provide the relevant information to the Commission and to EU institutions;
prepare and publish a report on the findings of the meetings it holds; and
publish the notices it receives.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
It has applied since 6 June 2014.
BACKGROUND

For more information, see:
European Trade Marks (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Copyright: the legal name of a product or service which is used to identify, describe, describe or describe a product, service or service.
* Piracy: the illegal practice of copying, copying or distributing a copy of a work without its authorisation.

Summary 100:
EU’s trade-related measures to protect its economic interests in the area of trade in services and goods with non-EU countries (trade-restrictive measures in the field of services and/or goods originating in non-European Economic Area (EEA)
EU‘s trade related measures to support the protection of its economic interest in international trade agreements
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2015/852 — EU’S trade-restricted measures
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that the EU has appropriate instruments to ensure the effective exercise of its rights under trade agreements in order to safeguard the EU's economic interests.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to the following sectors:
public procurement
trade in services.
It applies to:
goods and services provided by natural or legal persons or entities in the EU;
services and goods offered in public procurement by contracting authorities or entities operating in the territory of the EU countries;
contracts awarded by EU countries to contracting authorities, entities or categories of contracting authorities and entities that have a commercial presence within the EU.
In the case of public procurement, the origin of a service should be determined on the basis of the country where the service is provided. To provide the basis for this determination, each EU country must submit a list of appropriate contracting authorities* or entities to the Commission.
The Commission will seek information and views from the public authorities that may be involved in the implementation of possible commercial policy measures to be adopted by the EU in this sector. The Commission will take the input into account. It will promptly transmit the information to the European Parliament and the Council and report on its assessment to the Parliament and to the Council.
Suspension, modification and repeal of measures
EU countries may suspend, modify or repeal measures suspending concessions or other obligations in the sector of services. These measures may be suspended, modified or repealed in the light of any adverse economic impact resulting from a third country measure;
mandatory price penalty
A mandatory price penalty is an obligation on contracting authorities to increase, subject to certain exceptions, the price of goods and services originating in certain third countries that have been offered in contract award procedures.
Amendments to other acts
In addition, the regulation allows the Commission to adopt implementing acts suspending, modifying or repealing measures that are contrary to its interests. These may include:
suspension of concessions, other obligations or restrictions on trade in goods or services;
implementing acts suspending or modifying certain types of trade agreements;
restrictions on the supply of certain types or types of services or goods.
FROM WHEN DOES THE IMPLEMENTATION APPLY?
The implementing regulation has applied since 1 January 2016.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:

* KEY TERMS

Summary 101:
Bananas — EU-Central America stabilisation mechanism for imports of bananas
Bananas – EU-Cuba agreement
SUMMARY OF:
Agreement between the EU and Central America on the stabilisation of the trade in bananas
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on the application of the bilateral safeguard clause and the mechanism for stabilisation for bananas
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND THE REGULATION?
The agreement between the European Union and the Central American countries of bananas aims to prevent or remedy serious injury to the EU’s banana industry as a result of the reduction or elimination of a customs duty on bananas imported from Central America.
The regulation sets out the conditions for the adoption of provisional and definitive safeguard measures, for the imposition of prior surveillance measures and for suspending temporarily the preferential customs duty.
KEY POINTS
The EU and Côte d'Ivoire signed the agreement on 29 June 2012.
It applies to products originating in the EU or in Central America and those sectors to which monitoring has been extended.
In the event of an increase of imports concentrated in one or several of the EU's outermost regions or Member States, the Commission may decide to introduce safeguard measures.
Provisional safeguard measures apply to every product which is put into free circulation after the date of entry into force of the regulation.
Prior surveillance measures are applied in critical circumstances where a delay would cause damage which would be difficult to repair, pursuant to a preliminary determination on the basis of the factors referred to in Article 5(5 of the agreement.
Stabilisation mechanism
The stabilising measures apply only to products which have been reduced or eliminated from the customs duties in accordance with the Tariff Elimination Schedule (TES) and which are not covered by the agreement with Central America, except for bananas which are covered by a transitional period.
Implementing measures
The Commission may impose safeguard measures if:
there is sufficient prima facie evidence that imports of a product originating in a Central American country have increased as a consequence of a reduction in customs duty or a suspension of customs duty, and that such imports cause serious injury, or threat thereof, to the Union industry;
the level of production, production, productivity, capacity utilisation, profits and losses, and employment of the banana sector particularly vulnerable.
If the facts as finally established show that the conditions set out in Article 2(1) are not met, a decision terminating the investigation and proceeding without measures is adopted.
Before imposing a safeguard measure, a notice must be sent to the country concerned. The notice must include a summary of the share of the domestic market taken by the increased imports and changes in the level of sales, production and productivity of the sector.
A decision to initiate a proceeding must contain evidence that:
the conditions for imposing the safeguard measure are met and that there is evidence that the EU industry is adjusting;
there are special reasons therefor.
Termination of investigations and proceedings without measures
Implementation of the measures is subject to the consent of the country in question.
FROM WHEN DOES THE AGENCY APPLY?
   
The Agreement entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for the implementation of the Agreement.
For more information, see:
‘Bananas’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Customs duty: the customs duty levied on imports of goods which are exempt from customs duties and which have not been subject to any other customs duties or quotas.
ACT
Council Decision 2013/852/EU of 11 December 2012 on the signing, on behalf of the European Community, of the Agreements between the Union and its Member States with certain Central American neighbours on the harmonisation of customs duties, tariffs and quotas on bananas, and on the establishment of a system of stabilisation mechanisms for bananas (OJ L 347, 11.12.2012, pp. 1-8)

Summary 102:
Preservation order
Preservation Order
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2012 on the application of Directive 95/46/EC on judicial cooperation in civil matters having cross-border implications
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the conditions for issuing a ‘preservation order’ to prevent a debtor from being deprived of his or her funds by a creditor who has not yet obtained a judgment, court settlement or authentic instrument.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to claims against credit institutions and credit card companies.
It does not apply to claims for the use of a credit card.
Conditions for issuing the order
The creditor has to obtain a judgment or an authentic instrument from a court or competent authority in the EU country in which the debtor is domiciled.
If the creditor does not have such an instrument, the creditor has the right to apply for the release of the preserved funds if the debtor provides appropriate alternative security.
The order must be transmitted to the court or the competent authority of the creditor’s country of origin.
Implementation of the order is done by the issuing court or by the creditor, depending on who is responsible for initiating the enforcement procedure.
In the absence of a prior hearing of the debtor, the court may not issue the order unless it is justified, it should not issue it without first consulting the other party.
When the creditor receives a request for a preservation order, it must inform the debtor of the reasons for rejecting the request and inform the other than the reason for its refusal.
An application for an order may be made in any other official language of the institutions of the EU countries, such as English, French, German, Spanish, Italian or other official languages, if the creditor can accept such other language.
Any documents to be addressed under this regulation must be addressed in any official language other than that of the European Parliament or Council of the Union.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
  
It has applied since 1 January 2013.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to improve judicial cooperation between EU countries’ courts in the area of civil matters.
For more information, see:
‘Preservation orders’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 103:
Border surveillance at sea: protection of fundamental rights and the principle of non-refoulement
Border surveillance on the sea
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 10/2014/EU — protection of human beings during border surveillance
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules on the protection of the rights and principles of the European Union’s common rules on border surveillance.
It aims to prevent unauthorised border crossings, to counter cross-border criminality and to apprehend or take other measures against those who have crossed the border in an irregular manner.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all measures taken by EU countries or the European Border and Coast Guard Agency (BERF) to prevent and detect illegal border crossings and to detect persons who are attempting to enter the EU without submitting to border checks, as well as to address situations such as search and rescue that may arise during a border surveillance operation at sea and arrangements intended to bring such an operation to a successful conclusion.
Rights and principles
EU countries and the agency must ensure that the measures taken are based on the following principles:
the right to asylum and to protection against removal and expulsion,
the principles of non–foulement and non–discrimination, the right to an effective remedy and the rights of the child.
The measures taken must be based on an operational plan, which must contain details adapted to the circumstances of the operation concerned, including weather and marine forecasts.
Participation in border surveillance operations at sea
The participating units must:
identify the persons on board and inform them of their destination in a way that they understand or may reasonably be presumed to understand and give them an opportunity to express any reasons for believing that disembarkation in the proposed place would be in violation of the principle;
ensure that the vessel is in a phase of uncertainty in particular:
when a person has been reported as missing or a vessel is overdue;
when the vessel has failed to make an expected position or safety report.
Interception in the contiguous zone
The EU country in which the participating unit is located may approach the suspect vessel and take any of the measures listed above.
If the EU country is unwilling or unable to do so either directly or with the assistance of the Member State to whom the unit belongs, that EU country may request authorisation from the flag country to take any measures it considers necessary.
Operational plan
The operational plan must be established by the participating units in accordance with the operational plan of the host EU country. It must include:
a description of the actions to be taken in the event of a suspected illegal border crossing;
details of the conditions under which the vessel may be searched and rescued;
the weather and sea conditions, including forecasts;
measures to be used to bring the operation to the successful conclusion;
information to be given to victims of trafficking in human beings.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 1 January 2015.
BACKGROUND
  
For more information, see:
‘Border surveillance’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
  Еграциганска городна барка, г.бракстка    блакодка

Summary 104:
EU actions, emergency and technological assistance for migrants, refugees and migrants’ families
EU actions and emergency and technical assistance in migration and asylum
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 966/2012 — financial framework for EU actions, EMERGENCY and Technical assistance
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the financing of actions, emergencies and technological support for migrants and refugees under the EU’s common migration policy.
It aims to reduce the administrative burden for beneficiaries, the EU countries and the Commission, taking into account the principle of proportionality.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the period from 1 January 2014 to 31 December 2020.
Programmes covered by the regulation are:
the Asylum, Integration and Integration and Internal Security Funds (AISF) and the Emergency and Technological Assistance (ETA) programmes;
the Migration and Integration Fund (MIF) and its components;
The European Regional Development Fund (ERDF).
It does not apply to certain specific programmes, such as the European Maritime and Fisheries Fund (EMF), the European Social Fund (ESF) or the European Fund for Rural Development.
Beneficiaries
EU countries must:
ensure that beneficiaries are fully informed and cooperate with the Commission and the European Agency for Safety and Health at Work (EASW) in order to receive information, information, communication, monitoring, evaluation, evaluation and reporting on the national programme;
provide effective prevention against fraud, especially as regards areas with a higher level of risk.
Provide effective protection of the financial risk to beneficiaries’ financial interests.
The Commission is assisted by the asylum, integration and internal security funds committee.
Implementation of the regulation and the specific regulations
Each national programme is implemented in accordance with the implementing acts adopted by the Commission.
Each programme is financed by the EU budget and, in the event of reuse, is used in the first instance to finance expenditure under the Specific Regulations.
Financing
The budget commitments of the EU in respect of each national programme are made in annual instalments during the period 2014-2022.
Aims of the programme are to:
contribute to achieving the programme objectives;
promote the objectives of the project;
support the integration of migrants and asylum seekers and their families into the labour market;
improve the management of the external borders of the European Union;
facilitate the integration and integration of refugees, migrants' families and migrants' rights, including the protection of international and human rights law, including as regards actions implemented in non-EU countries, showing solidarity amongst all EU countries, and demonstrating an awareness of the need to respect national responsibilities in the process of ensuring a clear definition of tasks.
In addition, the programme is designed to contribute to the development of a coherent and coherent EU strategy for migration, asylum and integration.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The Regulation entered into force on 1 July 2012.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Migration and asylum policy’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Migration policy: a comprehensive EU strategy to cope with the pressures arising from the pressure of migration and irregular migration and to manage the external border of the Union.

Summary 105:
European return fund
European returns fund
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 514/2014 on the European return fund for the period 2014-2020
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
It sets up the European Return Fund (ERF) to support EU countries’ voluntary return of non-EU nationals.
KEY POINTS
EU countries are encouraged to give preference to voluntary return.
The ERF supports actions that take place in the framework of consistent strategies, taking into account the integration needs of third-country nationals at local and/or regional level.
In addition to supporting the return of persons as provided for in this regulation, the Fund should also support other measures to combat illegal immigration or the circumventing of existing legal migration rules, thereby safeguarding the integrity of EU countries' immigration systems.
EU actions must be implemented in accordance with the specific objectives set out in the regulation.
Specific objectives
The Fund supports actions in the following areas:
reception and asylum systems;
the establishment of a common European asylum system;
transnational actions or actions of fair and transparent distribution of resources among the specific priorities set out by the EU countries;

Fundamental principles of the European Union’s Internal Security Fund
SUMMARY OF:

WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the instrument to provide financial support to EU countries’ competent authorities in order to combat crime and terrorism.
KEY POINTS
The regulation establishes a European Union (EU)-wide instrument to support the work carried out by EU countries in the area of police cooperation and crime-fighting.

Summary 107:
Non-sustainable fishing of fish stocks of common interest by non-European Union (EU) Member States
Non-Sustainable fishing by countries of the common interest
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2012 on measures to prevent, deter and eliminate illegal, unreported and unregulated fishing
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the type of measures that may be taken with regard to non-EU Member States that are found to be allowing sustainable fishing of certain fish stocks*.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to countries that are not members of regional fisheries management organisations (RFMOs) or, where RFMOs have no competence for the stock in question, by means of ad hoc arrangements among the countries having an interest in the fishery.
It does not apply to:
non-EU countries, including territories enjoying self-governing status and endowed with competencies in the area of conservation and management of living marine resources;
third countries (e.g. Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway, Switzerland, the United Kingdom and the United States of America) that are members of the World Trade Organisation (WTO);
countries that are party to international agreements on sustainable fishing, such as the Convention on the Law of the Sea and the Agreement on the Functioning of the International Trade in Endangered Species of Wild Fauna and Flora (COSFESA).
The measures to be taken are based on objective criteria and are equitable, cost-effective and compatible with international law.
The Commission adopts implementing acts determining whether the measures adopted by the country concerned have been complied with and, where necessary, whether such measures should cease to apply.
Implementation of the measures is assisted by a committee composed of representatives of the Commission and assisted by the European Fisheries Management Organisation (EFMO).
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 31 December 2012.
BACKGROUND
The EU is one of the world’s leading fishing partners in the field of sustainable fishing.
For more information, see:
‘Fishery management’ on the European Commission's website.
KEY TERMS
* Non-EU country:
a country that is not a member of the European Economic Area (EEA).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC), Euratom, Euratom and the European Parliament of 16 December 2012 laying down the rules and general principles concerning mechanisms for control by the Commission of Member States of the exercise of implementing powers in respect of countries allowing non- sustainable fishing

Summary 108:
Bilateral investment agreements between EU countries and non-EU countries with a view to investing in the EU’s single market
Bilateral Investment agreements between the EU and non–EU countries
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2010 on bilateral investment agreements
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the conditions under which EU countries are empowered to amend or conclude agreements with third countries after 9 January 2013 on the basis of Article 2 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to any bilateral investment agreement concluded between the European Economic Area (EEA) Member States between 1 December 2009 and the end of 2013.
It does not apply to agreements signed between the Member States before 9 January 2009.
Amending or concluding agreements
The Member States must notify the European Commission within 90 days of the entry into force of the agreement and of any subsequent changes to the status of such an agreement. The Commission may request further information from the Member State concerned.
The Commission may decide to authorise the opening of formal negotiations on the grounds that:
the agreement does not constitute a serious obstacle to the negotiation or conclusion by the EU of bilateral agreements;
the Member State and the Commission must fully cooperate and take all necessary measures to ensure an effective defence;
an effective defence which may include, where appropriate, the participation in the procedure by the Commission;
participation of the Commission in negotiations.
the Commission may be assisted by the Committee for Investment Agreements.
Notification to the Commission of any amendments to the agreement is not sufficient for the purposes of authorising formal negotiations in accordance with Article 9 of the regulation.
Where the Commission grants an authorisation, the country concerned must notify it of its intention to enter into force. The notification must include a copy of the investment agreement.
If the Commission decides to take a decision, it must consult the other Member States concerned. Those consultations must take no longer than 90 days.
In the event of a failure of a Member State to fulfil its obligations under EU law, the Commission may ask for additional information.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
It has applied since 9 January 2010.

Summary 110:
Exports of firearms and ammunition to non-EU countries: customs controls and control measures
Exports from the customs territory of the European Union
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2017/852 — export authorisation, customs procedures and controls and import and transit measures relating to firearms
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to prevent, combat and eradicate the illicit manufacturing of and trafficking in firearms, their parts and components and ammunition.
It lays down rules for the export of firearms to and from the EU.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to transfers of firearms for civilian use within the EU, while this regulation focuses on measures in respect of export from its customs territory to or through third countries.
Export authorisation
EU countries must grant export authorisations and controls on the basis of a European Firearms Pass (EFP).
The EFP is valid for a period of 30 working days from the date on which the exporter applies for it. Under exceptional circumstances and for duly justified reasons, that period may be extended to 90 working days.
Before the competent authorities of a EU country grant an EFP, they must:
ensure that it is in compliance with the UN Firearms Protocol (UN Firearms Protocol);
check that the EFP has been converted into an authorisation form and that the authorisation has been validated by the competent authority of the EU country in which it is issued;
check the validity of the document, including whether it contains information relating to the import licence or import authorisation.
check whether the export is accompanied by the relevant authorities of the country of transit.
The exporter must provide the relevant information in advance to the countries of transit, including:
the name and address of the person who has the power to determine the sending of the item out of customs territory;
the date and place of shipment;
a description of the type and quantity of the weapon and of the parts and ammunition it contains.
Importers must ensure that the information contained in the export licence or the import authorisations is provided to the third countries in advance, at the latest prior to the shipment.
If the exporting country has no objection to the transit, it must notify the other EU countries of its decision to refuse, annul, suspend, modify or revoke the export.
FROM WHEN DOES THE IMPLEMENTATION APPLY?
The EU has applied the regulation since 3 July 2017.
BACKGROUND
The UN Firearms Convention requires EU countries to put in place or improve administrative procedures or systems to exercise effective control over the manufacturing, marking, import and export of weapons.
For more information, see:
The United Nations Firearms Convention (United Nations).
KEY TERMS
* Firearms: handguns, shotguns, rifles, assault rifles, pistols, shotguns and assault rifles.
* Ammunition: ammunition that can be fired by means of a magazine.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Implementing Regulation(EU) No 852/2017 of 23 June 2017 laying down implementing rules relating to exports of firearms (OJ L 157, 23.6.2017, pp. 1-8)
RELATED DOCUMENTS
   
 
Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 596/2013 of the Council of 11 March 2013 laying down detailed rules on export controls and controls of defence-related products within the Community and repealing Council Regulation (EEC) No 2913/92 on control of the acquisition and possession of weapons and ammunition and repealing Directive 91/477/EEC of 18 June 1991.
Commission Implementing Decision (EU), Euratom, No 597/2013 on the application of Directive 2009/43/EC on the simplification of terms and conditions of transfers of defence related products and ammunition within the European Community and amending Council Directive 2001/48/EC.

Summary 112:

EuroDac — fingerprints — processing, data protection AND liability
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 — Eurodac
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the processing, processing and liability of fingerprint data in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out rules for access to the EuroDac computerised fingerprint recognition system.
It applies to non-EU nationals and non-stateless persons who have applied for international protection and whose fingerprints have been transmitted to the Central System of the EU country of origin for comparison with the fingerprint data of applicants who have already been granted international protection.
The European Commission is responsible for the operational management of EuroDAC.
EU countries must ensure that the data they receive from Eurodatac are stored in a secure and unambiguous manner.
Eurodatac is managed by Europol and supervised by an independent external data protection supervisor.
KEY TERMS
* Eurodatasheet: a computerised database containing data relating to the processing and security of fingerprints and data integrity and security.
* KEY TERM
* Fingerprint recognition system: a system that allows the computerised recognition of fingerprints to be used for the purpose of identifying criminal suspects or victims of crime.

Summary 113:
Protection of designations of origin and traditional specialities in the agricultural and forestry sectors
Protecting designations and symbols of origin in the agriculture and forestry sector
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2011 — protection of designated names and symbols and indications of origin
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the protection of names, symbols and geographical indications* of agricultural products and forestry products in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Protection
The regulation applies to designations* and symbols* of origin (designations* or traditional specialties* which refer to a geographical area in a non-EU country.
It does not apply to products which are produced outside the EU.
The protection applies to the use of the registered names on goods as well as on services, such as food and pharmaceuticals.
Designations are used fairly and in order to prevent practices liable to mislead consumers and to prevent the misuse, imitation and evocation of their names.
Names and symbols are protected against:
misuse, imitation or evocation;
the use of their name in trade and, if necessary, by informing competent authorities, or any other competent authority within the framework of Regulation (EC) No 765/2008 setting out the requirements for accreditation and market surveillance relating to the marketing of products (17).
The European Commission is empowered to adopt delegated acts to establish the EU symbols and to ensure that the appropriate information is communicated to the consumer.
Application for registration of names
EU countries must apply to the European Commission for the registration of the names and the symbols of products covered by the regulation.
Applications must be submitted to the Commission within 6 months of the date of entry into force of the regulation, subject to certain conditions.
An optional quality term ‘mountain product’ may be used to describe products that comply with the corresponding conditions of use.
A non-binding declaration of origin may only be used for products which meet the conditions of protection under the regulation if they are:
originating in a country other than that of the EU country where the designation of origin is registered;
produced in an area other than the country of origin of the protected name or the traditional speciality;
originated in an EU country which is not part of the European Economic Area (EEA);
produced outside the EEA, but which bears the name of a country of the EEA.
If the Commission considers that an application to register a name or a symbol does not meet the requirements, it must examine the validity of the application and inform the Commission of the reasons for its rejection. The Commission may decide to grant or deny the application.
Registration of names is voluntary for products originating in non-EEA countries.
Protected symbols and designations are mandatory for products produced in the EU and those originating in an EEA country which bear the name ‘traditional specialities’.
National authorities may encourage the formation and functioning of groups on their territories to ensure adequate legal protection by administrative means.
In addition, EU countries may introduce measures to ensure the proper functioning of the protection scheme.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 4 January 2023.
BACKGROUND
 
For more information, see:
‘Traditional specialities protection’ (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* Designated name: a name, symbol or other marking of origin which refers to a specific geographical area of origin.
* Traditional speciality: a product which is closely linked to agricultural products or to the rural economy.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 			
Commission Implementing Decision 2011/852/EU of 4 January 2011 on the application for registration in the field of protection of designated names and traditional symbols and marking of geographical indications of the agricultural, forestry and aquaculture sectors (OJ L 218, 7.5.2011, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 652/2010 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 114:
Single-hull oil tankers — accelerated phasing in the application of MARPOL rules
Single-Hull oil tanker rules — accelerated phase-in
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2012 on the introduction of a scheme for the accelerated application of the requirements of the International Maritime Organisation’s (IMO) MARPOL 73/78 on single-HULL oil tanker design
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out a scheme to apply the MARPOL requirements on the design and construction of single hull oil tanker (SOHO) vessels.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to SOHO vessels flying the flag of an EU country and to vessels of Category 2 or Category 3 which are equipped only with double bottoms or double sides not used for the transport of oil and extending for the whole length of the cargo tank.
It does not apply to ships of Category 1 or Category 2 that are equipped with a single bottom or a single side and which are designed to carry only a cargo tank or are not designed to transport heavy grade oil.
In addition, the regulation bans the transport to or from ports of the EU countries of heavy-grade oil in single hulls.
The European Commission has delegated the power to the European Maritime Safety Agency (EMSA) to adopt delegated acts to ensure that the regulation is applied.
EU countries are obliged to apply this regulation to all ships flying their flag, irrespective of their tonnage, construction and age.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY APPLY?
From 1 January 2013.
 
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted Regulation (EC) No 2099/2002/2002 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 5 November 2002 establishing a Committee on Safe Seas and the Prevention of Pollution from Ships (COSS) and amending the Regulations on maritime safety and the prevention of pollution from ships.
For more information, see:
Maritime safety and pollution prevention (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
Single hull: a vessel of less than 20 metres in length and with a maximum gross tonnages of less that 10,000 gross tonnes.

Summary 115:
European Financial Supervisory Authority
European Financial Stability Authority
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on the European Financial Supervision Authority
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
It sets out the structure and tasks of the European financial supervisory authority (ESAs).
KEY POINTS
The ESAs are responsible for assisting national supervisory authorities in the consistent interpretation and application of EU rules and contributing to financial stability necessary for financial integration.
They are accountable to the European Parliament and the Council of the EU.
The purpose and tasks are to:
ensure that the relevant national authorities comply with the relevant EU rules;
assist the European Commission in developing and applying the relevant technical standards and implementing technical standards;
provide guidance and guidance on the application of the relevant rules and guidelines and recommendations;
cooperate with the European Insurance and Reinsurance Stakeholder Group and the Occupational Pensions Stakeholders Group to ensure the proper functioning of the ESAs and to ensure their independence and effectiveness.
In addition, the ESC is responsible for:
assisting the European Banking Supervisory Mechanism (EBM) and the European Securities and Markets Authority (ESMA) in their respective tasks;
ensuring that the ESC’s tasks are aligned with those of the EBM and the ESM;
coordinating the activities of the ESC with regard to the prudential supervision of cross-border financial institutions and groups of financial institutions;
helping the European Central Bank (ECB) in its activities;
supporting the ECB in its work in the field of financial supervision;
contributing to the effective supervision of the financial sector of the euro area.
It is composed of a board of supervisors and a management board.
Its term of office is 5 years and may be extended once. It meets at least 5 times a year and may meet at least twice a year on an ad hoc basis. It may also require the group supervisor to schedule a meeting of the college or add a point to the agenda of a meeting.
Duties and responsibilities
The ESC assists the competent national authorities in applying EU rules. It assists the Commission in drawing up and implementing the relevant regulatory technical standards. It also assists the European Stability Mechanism in its role as a single point of contact between the Commission and the national authorities.
Delegation of responsibilities
EU countries may set out specific arrangements regarding the delegation of responsibilities that have to be complied with before their competent authorities enter into such delegation agreements, and may limit the scope of delegation to what is necessary for the effective supervising of cross–border institutions or groups.
Regulatory technical standards
The European Commission may adopt a draft implementing technical standard prepared by the ESC without prior coordination with the ESC. It must be published in the Official Journal. The competent authority must receive advanced notice of such publication.
If, during the 6-week period referred to in the fourth subparagraph, the Commission has not adopted an amended draft regulatory technical standard, it may adopt the standard without prior consultation with the Commission.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The ESM was set up under Regulation (EC) No 223/2009.
For more information, see:
Financial Supervision (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* Financial institutions: financial institutions that provide financial services to the EU and that are subject to EU rules (e.g. banks, insurance companies, insurance and reinsurance companies, pension funds, etc.).
* Statistical information: information on the financial activities of a financial institution, such as its assets, liabilities and liabilities.

Summary 116:
Freedom of movement of workers and their families in the European Union
Freedom of mobility of work
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2005 — freedom of movement
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the conditions under which workers from one EU country who wish to work in another EU country can do so.
KEY POINTS
Eligibility for employment
Employment and equality of treatment
A worker who is a national of an EU country and who is employed in the territory of another EU State must enjoy the same social and tax advantages as national workers.
The employment and employment rights of a worker who does not live in the EU country where he or she is employed must not depend on medical, vocational or other criteria which are discriminatory on grounds of nationality by comparison with those applied to nationals of the other EU country.
Equal treatment for employers and employers’ associations
Employers must ensure that their workers are treated equally in terms of:
membership of trade unions and the exercise of rights attached thereto, including the right to vote and to be eligible for the administration or management posts of a trade union;
the right to participate in the management of bodies governed by public law and from holding an office governed by the public law of the country in which the worker is employed;
participation in the selection and selection of representatives of the various economic sectors of the EU countries;
representation on the Advisory Committee and on the Technical Committee of the European Atomic Energy Community (see Annex I to the regulation).
The Member States must also ensure that the Member States communicate to the specialist services of the countries concerned the details of suitable applications.
Vacancy clearance
A Member State must forward to the services of its first Member State the information on vacancies for a post in another Member State.
In the event of vacancies, the Member State which receives the application must inform the specialist service of the first EU State of any information it has received on the application.
Information must be kept up-to-date regularly.
Amending Regulation (EU) 2017/852 amends the regulation to take account of developments on the EU labour market.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY APPLY?
   
It has applied since 8 November 2005.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
For more information, see:
‘Equality of treatment of workers’ on the European Commission’s website.
