Summary 117:
EU rules on the placing on the market and the use of certain chemicals
EU controls on the putting on the sale and use of some chemicals
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 2037/2010 — rules for the placing of certain substances on the European Union (EU) market
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for placing on and using certain chemicals on the EU’s market.
It repeals and repeals Regulation (EC), which had to become law in the EU countries by 1 January 2010.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to substances used for essential laboratory and analytical purposes, as listed in Annex I to the regulation. It does not apply to chemicals used as process agents.
Imports of controlled substances or of products and equipment containing or relying on controlled substances are prohibited.
Exports of chemicals to the EU from non-EU countries are also prohibited, as are imports of chemicals used in the manufacture, manufacture or use of essential laboratory or analytical processes.
The European Commission may, at the request of the competent authority of an EU country, grant derogations from the end dates for existing applications or cut-off dates for new applications, provided that no technically and economically feasible alternative is available.
EU countries must ensure that the substances listed in the annexes are used only for essential lab and analytical uses and that they are not used for the manufacture or manufacture of products or equipment that do not function without them.
Any undertaking using controlled substances other than hydrochlorofluorocarbons must register with the Commission, indicating the substances being used, the purpose, the estimated annual consumption and the suppliers of those substances, and any purchases from and sales to other undertakings in the Community.
In addition, the Commission is empowered to align Annexes to this regulation with decisions of the parties to the Kyoto Protocol, in particular with those concerning approved destruction methods, conditions for the place on market of chemicals, and processes in which controlled substances may be used.
Amendments to Annexes
Annexes to Annex I and II to Annex III to Annex IV to Annex V to Annex VI to Annex VII to Annex VIII to Annex IX to Annex X to Annex XI to Annex XII to Annex XIII to Annex XV to Annex XIV to Annex XVI to the Annexes.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
The Kyoto Protocol is the cornerstone of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Atomic Energy Community (TFEC).
For more information, see:
‘The Treaty on European Union’ on the Commission's website
KEY TERMS
* Chemicals: substances that have been classified according to their physical, chemical, physical, biological or chemical properties.
* Process agent: a substance that can be used as a process agent in a chemical, biological, chemical or biological process, such as a catalyst, to produce a substance or a mixture of substances.

Summary 118:
European Union Environment Agency
European Union Environmental Agency
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1210/90 — setting up the European Environment Agency (EEA)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up a European Union (EU) Environment Agency.
KEY POINTS
The EEA is responsible for collecting, analysing and disseminating information on the EU’s environmental situation.
The main areas of activity of the EEA are:
the quality of the environment;
the pressures on the environment,
the sensitivity of the environmental, including placing these in the context of sustainable development;
land use and natural resources;
waste management;
noise emissions;
chemical substances which are hazardous for the environment and coastal and marine protection;
coastal and marine conservation.
In addition, EEA provides information and services to EU countries’ national environment information networks, especially in the priority areas listed above.
EEA staff are appointed by the European Parliament and the Council and are assisted by a Management Board.
Each year, the Management Board, on the basis of a draft drawn up by the Executive Director, produces a statement of estimates of revenue and expenditure of the Agency for the following financial year. The programme may be adjusted in the course of the year by the same procedure.
By 1 March at the latest following each financial year, it communicates the provisional accounts to the European Commission and the Court of Auditors, together with a report on the budgetary and financial management for that year.
Every 2 years, the EAA draws up its final accounts under its own responsibility and sends them to the management board for an opinion. The management board then adopts the budget for the next financial year by a qualified majority vote.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 March 2009.

Eco-management and audit scheme (EMAS) for businesses
Eco - Management and Audit scheme (EASM) for business
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 765/2008 on the registration of organisations complying with EU environmental law
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to encourage businesses to comply with EU legislation on the environment.
KEY POINTS
It sets out the rules for the registration and verification of organisations that comply with the EU’s environmental law.
The regulation applies to all EU countries except Denmark, Ireland and the United Kingdom (1), Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland.
It does not apply to non-EU countries, Iceland, Norway, Switzerland and the former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia.
EU countries must apply the rules of the regulation to organisations that are not covered by it.
Registration of organisations
To become a registered organisation, an organisation must:
provide an updated environmental statement to the competent body of the competent authority of the EU country in which it is located;
submit a copy of its environmental management and audit report to this competent body every 2 years;
publish a report on its environmental and sustainable development performance every 3 years.
Organisations benefiting from an extension of up to 2 years, as referred to in paragraph 1, must forward the non-validated updated environmental statements to the relevant competent body each year that they are exempt from the obligation to have a validated environmental statement.
A registered organisation must ensure that the organisation:
ensures that the information it provides on its website is accurate, reliable and up-to-date;
provides the competent authorities with information regarding the applicable legal requirements relating to the environment;
implements the necessary information to ensure that it complies with the relevant environmental requirements;
supports the work of environmental verifiers;
cooperates with the competent enforcement authorities in the application and enforcement of EU environmental legislation.

Summary 120:
Spirit drinks
Spirits
ACT
Regulation (EC) No 552/2006 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 26 February 2006 on the definition, description, presentation and labelling of spirit drinks and on the protection of geographical indications of certain spirit drinks.
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It sets out the rules applicable to spirit drinks, as well as the rules on their description and presentation.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all spirit drinks which meet the requirements for inclusion in categories 1 to 46 of Annex II of the directive.
It does not apply to drinks falling within CN codes 2203, 2204, 2205, 2206 and 2207 which are not considered spirit drinks because they do not meet the definition of ‘spirit drink’.
The definition of a spirit drink is based on the characteristics of the fruit, berry or vegetable it is derived from.
A spirit drink may be classified as a spirit if it meets the following criteria:
it is a spirit of agricultural origin;
it has a maximum alcohol content of at least 0.5% alcohol per litre of 100% vol.
it contains no more than 2 grams of sugar and not less than 1.5 grams of natural or synthetic anethole;
has a maximum hydrocyanic acid content of 5 grams per hectolitre of 0.2%.
It is not intended to be used as a substitute for wine or wine-product cocktails.
its sales denomination must be shown clearly and visibly in a prominent position on the label and must not be replaced or altered.
Certain spirit drinks may be sold under the name of any predominant flavour with the word ‘vodka’ or ‘pomace’, provided that no grounds for its invalidity or revocation exist as specified by First Council Directive 89/104/EEC of 21 December 1988 to approximate the laws of the Member States relating to trade marks.

Summary 121:
Common rules for safeguarding civil aviation against acts of unlawful interference with civil aircraft (common basic standards on aviation security)
Common rules on safeguarding Civil Aviation Against Acts of Unlawful Interference With Civil Aircraft
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 — common rules for the protection of civil aircraft
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down common rules to protect persons and goods within the European Union (EU) against acts that jeopardise the security of civil aviation.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries’ airports.
It does not apply to flights from non-EU countries.
EU countries must ensure the application in their territory of the common basic standards referred to in the regulation.
Each EU country must draw up a national civil aviation security programme.
The programme must describe the methods and procedures which are to be followed by the airport operator in order to comply both with this regulation and with the national security programme of the EU country in which the airport is located.
Air carrier security programme
Air carriers must ensure that passengers and their cabin baggage are screened and that they are not mixed with arriving passengers, unless:
the passengers arrive from a Member State that does not have aviation security standards equivalent to those laid down by this regulation, provided that the Commission or that Member State has not not granted a derogation;
they have not been recruited or trained to carry out basic security controls;
there is no need to rescreen passengers or their baggage arriving on flights from a non-European country that do not have security standards comparable to those set out in this regulation;
the passenger and their baggage are not allowed to mix with departing passengers.
Every year, the Commission must present an annual report on the implementation of this regulation to the appropriate authority of the Member State concerned.
Implementing measures
The Commission must take into account the measures taken by the Member States to remedy any deficiencies in their national security programmes.
Penalties
The penalties for any breach of the regulation must be effective, proportionate and dissuasive.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLACE?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
 
For more information, see:
‘Airport security’ on the European Commission's website.

Restricting funds and economic resources against the financing of terrorism
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2018/1725 — restrictive measures against terrorist financing
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to impose sanctions on individuals and entities responsible for, providing support to or otherwise involved in serious violations of human rights or abuses, as well as those associated with the individuals, entities and bodies covered.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
any natural or legal person, entity or body, which is incorporated or constituted under the law of an EU country;

WHAT DOES THIS REGULATING DO?
Directive 2014/EU/EU allows the EU countries to impose restrictive measures in response to terrorist activities.
The measures are effective, proportionate and dissuasive. They are designed to prevent, deter and limit the ability of the individuals or bodies to benefit from the funds and resources frozen.

WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up the Facilitating the Exchange of Information on Authentic Document and Falsified Document Online (FAADO) system.

EU countries decide which competent authorities are to be provided with access and the level of access with which they should be provided.
In addition, EU countries must ensure that personal data are only processed to the extent strictly necessary for the purpose of operating the system in line with the principle of data minimisation in a way which does not permit the identification of any natural person through the system without using additional data.
Personal data may only be processed in the context of the purpose for which it is necessary.
Any processing of personal data by EU countries is in accordance with the regulation’s.

Summary 125:
Non-discrimination and proportionality of the requirements on access to, or the pursuit of, regulated professions
Non–discrimination and the requirement to respect the principles of non–discrimination
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2016/852 on the application of the principle of non-discrimination to the regulation of certain professions
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It aims to ensure that EU countries do not discriminate on the basis of nationality or residence when it comes to the access to certain professions.
KEY POINTS
The directive applies to the following:
the freedom to choose an occupation, as well as the freedom to conduct a business.
The freedom of establishment and the freedom of providing services.
It does not apply to professions that are not covered by the Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union (‘the Charter’).
It is a matter of national competence for EU countries to decide whether and how to regulate a regulated profession within the limits of their competence.
Regulation
EU countries must ensure that:
there is no discrimination based on nationality or on the grounds of race, religion, colour, sex, age, disability, age or sexual orientation;
there are no grounds for discrimination on grounds of public interest, such as the health and life of humans or the protection of intellectual property rights;
the regulation of a profession is proportionate and does not lead to a disproportionate burden on service providers, nor does it hinder or render less attractive the exercise of the right to provide services, as long as it does not go beyond what is necessary to achieve the objective of the objective pursued.
the measure does not prevent the free movement of persons and services within the EU.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE APPLYORKORK
It entered into force on 1 July 2016. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 July 2020.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Access to regulated professions’ on the European Commission’s website.

Summary 126:
Fisheries management of stocks of common interest in the North Sea and the Baltic
Fishing management of species of common interests in the north sea
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1380/2013 on the EU’s fisheries management of North Sea stocks
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the management of common stocks of stocks belonging to common interest (MSY) in EU waters.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all stocks of species belonging to the common interest of the EU and its Member States.
It does not apply to:
fishing opportunities;
by-catch stocks;
fisheries managed in mixed fisheries;
target fishing mortality (FMSY).
The European Commission is empowered to adopt delegated acts adjusting the geographical distribution of stocks set out in the plan if the scientific advice provided by the International Council for the Exploration of the Sea (ICES) indicates a change in the distribution of the relevant stocks.
Management of MSY
The aim of the regulation is to restore MSY to levels that can produce MSY as determined by their biological characteristics.
To achieve this objective, the European Commission must draw up a multiannual management plan. The plan must contain objectives, quantifiable targets with clear timeframes, conservation reference points, safeguards and technical measures designed to avoid and reduce unwanted catches.
The plan must contribute to the elimination of discards, by avoiding and reducing, as far as possible, unwanted catches, and to the implementation of the landing obligation for the species which are subject to catch limits and to not more than 20 % of the maximum allowable catch.
In addition, the Commission must take into account the significant impact of recreational fisheries on MSY on the marine ecosystem.
Fishery opportunities
The target fishing mortality must be fixed at levels consistent with a fishing mortality that is reduced below the upper range of FMSY, taking account of the decrease in biomass.
Mixed fisheries
The management of mixed fisheries with regard to stocks referred to in Article 1(s) of this regulation must take account of:
the difficulty of fishing all stocks at MSY at the same time, especially in situations where that leads to a premature closure of the fishery;
the inter-species stock dynamics;
in order to limit variations in fishing opportunities between consecutive years to a maximum of 20 %.
Limiting discards
The Commission is also empowered to introduce measures to reduce discards.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATING APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a series of measures to tackle overfishing, illegal, unreported and unregulated fishing and destructive fishing practices.
For more information, see:
‘Overfishing and illegal fishing’ (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Common interest: a stock of fish belonging to a common interest that is not exploited by non-EU countries.
* By-catch: fish that are not part of a common fishery.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
Council Regulation (EU), Euratom, Euratom and the European Economic and Social Committee of 13 December 2013 on the European Union fisheries management regulation (OJ L 347, 14.12.2013, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (Euratom) No 347 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

SUMMARY OF:

WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION AND OF THE AGREEMENT?

KEY POINTS
Scope

fishery resources caught in association with these resources that were harvested in the SPRFMO;
activity (fishing/transit or transhipping) of vessels engaged in bottom fishing activities in the area.
EU countries must ensure that:
the data collected are collected by qualified observers;
the information collected is recorded and transmitted to the Commission by electronic means;
inspections are carried out by qualified inspectors from EU countries.

Summary 128:
Controls on cash entering and leaving the European Union (EUR10,000 and more)
Countries must impose controls on cash in and out of the EU (Eur10 000 and more).
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 10/2010 — controls on the movement of cash
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It introduces a system of controls with respect to cash entering or leaving the EU to complement the legal framework for the prevention of money laundering and terrorist financing.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to any natural person who carries cash on their person, in their luggage or in their means of transport.
Carriers who carry cash of a value of EUR 10 000 or more must declare that cash to the competent authorities of the Member State through which they are entering or departing the EU and make it available to them for control.
The obligation is subject to a threshold of € 10 000.
Carryers must also make a disclosure declaration, systematically or on a case-by-case basis, in accordance with national procedures.
National authorities must inform the European Anti-Fraud Office (OLAF) and the Financial Intelligence Unit (FIU) of any information they receive on cash.
In addition, national authorities must share information relating to sub-threshold amounts of cash with other Member States if there are indications of criminal activity.
Where cash is suspected to be related to criminal activity, it must be seized and seized by the authorities.
If cash is seized, the carrier must provide a statement of reasons for the action and, where appropriate, be detained.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLYORKORKORKEN INTO FORCELEVEL
The legislation entered into force on 1 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
The introduction of cash controls in the EU is part of a package of measures designed to protect the EU’s financial interests.
For more information, see:
‘Cash controls’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Cash: any amount of cash on the person or in the luggage of a carrier that is not accompanied by a carrier.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC) No 11/2010/2010 of 20 December 2010 on controls on certain types of cash in the Union (OJ L 309, 21.12.2010, pp. 1-8)
RELATED DOCUMENTS
   
 
Directive 2015/849/EU of the European Parliament and of the Council of 11 December 2015 on the prevention and combating money laundering, combating terrorist financing and combating the financing of terrorist activities (Financial Intelligence Unit Directive) (see summary) (Obligations of Member States on the establishment and functioning of Financial Intelligence Units (FIUs) and amending Council Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 89/2005 on the control of cash and on the exchange of personal data between national authorities and the European Data Protection Supervisor) (See summary).
Regulations (EC), Euratom and the Commission have adopted a series of measures to strengthen the cooperation between the EU countries’ financial intelligence units and the OLAF, in particular by:
ensuring that cash is detained by competent authorities if it is suspected of being used for criminal activity;
establishing an EU-wide information campaign to combat money laundering;
introducing penalties for infringements of this regulation.

Summary 129:
Energy Union — energy security, decarbonisation and energy efficiency (2020-2026)
Energy Union – energy security and decarbonising
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2018/842 — Energy Union
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out a framework for the implementation of the Energy Union, which aims to achieve the EU’s objectives and targets to reduce greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions and to improve energy security.
KEY POINTS
The Energy Union covers five dimensions: energy security; the internal energy market; energy efficiency; decarbonised energy infrastructure; and research, innovation and competitiveness.
The objectives are:
energy security;
energy efficiency;
decarbonisation;
research and innovation; and
competitiveness.
It covers the following areas of cooperation between the Commission and EU countries:
climate change and energy policies and strategies;
environmental policies and measures;
regional cooperation for energy and climate change;
climate and energy policy coordination;
transparency and information exchange.
In addition, the regulation sets out the responsibilities of the Commission, the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee (ESC) in implementing the energy union.
EU countries must:
ensure that:
the Commission publishes a national climate and energy and energy plan by 31 December 2020;
provide the public with information on the progress made by each EU country on its objectives, targets, targets and strategies for 2030 and 2026;
long-term strategies and targets;
report to the Commission every 5 years on their progress towards achieving the objectives and strategies.
Each EU country must ensure that the public is informed of the progress it has made towards achieving its objectives and its targets.
If the Commission concludes that insufficient progress is made by an EU country towards meeting its objectives or targets and its reference points for renewable energy, its energy efficiency targets or in implementing its policies and energy measures, it must issue recommendations to the EU country concerned.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLYEAR OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
It entered into force on 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The energy union is one of the largest emitters of greenhouse gases in the world.
For more information, see:
‘Energy Union’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 130:
POPs — EU action to reduce their release and their toxicity (Regulation (EU) 2021/2021)
POPS — Regulation (EU).
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It aims to reduce the release and toxicity of polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons (PAPs) by reducing their toxicity.
KEY POINTS
It repeals Regulation (EEC) No 552/2008 on POPs.
The regulation repeals and repeals Directive 2000/532/EC on the list of POPs which are unintentional by-products of industrial processes, with the aim of eliminating POPs as soon as possible.
It sets out a list of substances, mixtures and articles which are considered to be POPs and which are subject to control measures.
In addition, the regulation sets out the limits for the use and management of notified stockpiles of certain POPs, as well as the penalties for their use and disposal.
EU countries must ensure that POPs are used only in quantities that are safe for human health and that they are disposed of in the most environmentally sound and environmentally sound manner.
There is no longer a need for EU countries to keep stockpiles on their territory.
Exemptions from control measures
Certain substances are excluded from the regulation’s list of controlled substances, such as:
cyclohexane,
polychlorinated biphenyl chloride (PCD) and
polycyclic fatty acid esters (PFCEs)
cyclopropyl esters,
dichlorohexanhydrochlorohexanoacrylamide,
pentabromodiphenyl ester,
piperazine,
perfluorocarbons and
pyrrolidinium bromide.
However, certain substances are not covered by this list.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
 
The regulations have applied since 16 July 2021.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a series of measures to reduce POPs in line with the Paris Agreement on the elimination of hazardous substances.
For more information, see:
European POPs (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* POPs: compounds which are unintentionally released into the environment as a result of industrial activities.
* Cyclohexyl chloride: a compound which is a by-product of the manufacture of polychlorinated hydrocarboxylic acid (PCB) and is toxic to humans and animals. It is a hydrochloric acid with a maximum toxicity of 1,000 mg/kg and a maximum density of 1.5 kg/year.

Summary 131:
Single-use plastic products — reducing their environmental impact
Single use plastic products— reducing their environment impact
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2017/852 — reducing plastic waste
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It aims to reduce plastic waste in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The directive introduces measures to reduce the environmental impact of single-use products.
It requires producers of plastic products to cover the costs of cleaning up litter and to ensure that their products are made available to the final consumer free of charge.
EU countries are required to regularly monitor the properties and quantities of marine litter, including plastic marine litter. They must immediately inform the European Commission of the results of the monitoring and report to it every 3 years.
To minimise administrative costs, EU countries should be able to determine financial contributions towards the cost of cleaning litter by setting appropriate multiannual fixed amounts.
In addition, the directive introduces producer responsibility requirements in addition to those laid down by Directive 2008/98/EC, for example, the requirement for producers of certain plastic products, such as fishing gear, to pay for the cleaning up of litter.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
From 1 January 2022.
BACKGROUND
   
The plastic waste directive is part of a package of measures designed to tackle plastic pollution in the EU.
For more information, see:
‘Plastic waste and plastic pollution’ on European Commission's website.
KEY TERMS
MAIN DOCUMENTS
European Union directive (EU directive on plastic waste (Directive Directive (EU):
—
WHAT DO THE DIRECTIVES DO?
Directives (EU countries must ensure that plastic waste is collected and disposed of in a non-toxic and non-hazardous manner and that plastic products are not made available for reuse or re-use at the point of sale to the consumer.
The Directive lays down rules on the producer responsibility for plastic waste and on the disposal of plastic waste.
Scope
It applies to all plastic waste, whether it is plastic, paper, paperboard, cardboard, cardboardboard, plastic bags, plastic bottles, plastic containers, plastic packaging, plastic toys and plastic fishing gear. It does not apply to:
plastic bottles and containers used for personal care and personal care products;
personal care products used by professional and domestic care workers;
paperboard and plastic containers used by schools and hospitals;
single-use toilet paper and plastic toilet paper.

Summary 133:
EU trade mark registration and certification system (EU-TRADE)
EU-TEACHING MARKS
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 608/2013 — rules on the registration and licensing of EU trade mark systems
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the rules for the registration, licensing and certification of trade marks and collective marks in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all trade marks, collective marks and certificates of use in the EU.
It does not apply to:
collective marks*;
trade mark certificates* and marks of use* in non-EU countries, such as the United Kingdom (1) and Canada (2) and to the United States of America (3) and the European Economic Area (EEA);
international trade mark certificates (e.g. those issued by the World Intellectual Property Organisation (WPO) or the World Trade Organization (WTO).
It also applies to trade mark recognition systems in other EU countries.
Registration
The European Trade Marks Office (ETMO) is responsible for registering, licensing, certifying and enforcing EU trade marks.
Rules on the application procedure

The Executive Director of the ETO manages the register of trade mark applications.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?

Its main tasks are:
registering and certifying trade marks;
providing information to the public on the trade mark system;
assisting the European Commission in the implementation of the regulation;
facilitating the exchange of information between EU countries on the EU-trade mark system.
KEY TERMS

* Trade mark certification: a certificate of use issued by an EU country on the basis of an application for a collective mark or collective mark.

Summary 134:
Access to published works for persons who are blind, visually impaired or otherwise print-disabled
Assessment of the application of the Marrakesh Treaty to Facilitate Access to Published Works for Persons who are Blind, Visually Impaired, or Otherwise Print Disabled
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/1564 on the application, on behalf of the European Union, of the Treaty on the Functioning of the Community to facilitate the exchange of copies, in accessible formats, of certain works and other protected subject matter
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to improve the access of persons with disabilities to the published works of authors, publishers and other authorised entities.
It requires contracting parties to provide for exceptions or limitations to copyright and related rights for the making and dissemination of copies in accessible format, and for the cross-border exchange of those copies.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
published works for the benefit of beneficiary persons between the EU and non-EU countries that are parties to the treaty;
the importation of, and access to, accessible format copies made in accordance with the implementation of the treaty, from a third country, by beneficiary persons in the EU, and authorised entities established in a Member State, for non-commercial purposes;
an authorised entity established in an EU country may distribute, communicate or make available to beneficiary persons or to an its primary activities, institutional obligations or as part of its public-interest missions.
Authorised entities must ensure that:
the content of the published in an accessible format does not constitute an unreasonable or discriminatory barrier to access to cultural materials for persons with visual impairments or disabilities, insofar as, as a result of such impairments, those persons are unable to read printed works to substantially the same degree as persons without such disabilities.
Exceptions and limitations
The exemption or limitation of copyright or related rights does not prevent the authorisation or distribution of, or making available to beneficiaries of the covered works in a manner that would be normally acceptable for reading.
The authorisation and distribution of the covers of the above-mentioned covered works must comply with Directive 2001/29/EC on the protection of intellectual property rights (see summary).
Authorisations and distribution
An authorised entity may also provide the same services as a public institution or non-profit organisation that provides the same service for beneficiary persons as one of its primary or institutional obligations.
Export and import
An authorised entity may export, communicate and make available from a non-European Union country, to an authorised entity in another EU country, any accessible format copy of a covered work under the same conditions as those for which it has been authorised.
Imports of the same covered works under the above conditions are subject to certain conditions as the import of those covered by Directives 2001/30/EC and 2001/65/EC.
Dispute settlement
An EU country must settle any dispute between the authorising entity and the other EU country on the interpretation of the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
   
It has applied since 11 October 2017.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Accessible format: a format in which a person is able to move the eyes to the extent that would normally be normally considered for reading a printed work.
* Authorised entity: an organisation or public institution, such as a library, which is responsible for making accessible formats available for the use of beneficiaries.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Еграшка закова глакска, г.к.г.б.
Council Regulation (EU), Euratom, Euratom and the European Economic and Social Committee of 11 October 2023 on the approximation of the laws of the Member States relating to the making, distribution, communication and making available of accessible formats of certain written works and of other protected subjects and repealing Council Regulation (EEC) No 552/2006 (OJ L 115, 17.4.2023, pp. 1-8)
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Summary 136:
In vitro diagnostic medical devices — rules for their manufacture, testing and use
In vitro diagnostic medical devices— rules for its manufacture, test and operation
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2014 — rules on the manufacture and use of in vitro diagnostic devices
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It lays down rules for the manufacture, placing on the market and putting into service of medical devices designed to be used in vitro for the diagnosis of diseases.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all medical devices intended for use in vitro (i.e. in vitro diagnostics).
It does not apply to:
medical devices designed and manufactured in the EU for the purpose of medical research;
in vitro diagnostic tests for the assessment of human health and safety;
diagnostic devices for the testing and evaluation of diseases, such as cancer and infectious diseases;
personal care devices.
Manufacturers must ensure that their products comply with the regulation’s requirements, including:
the labelling and labelling of the devices and their technical documentation;
the conformity assessment of the medical devices;
compliance with the relevant safety and health requirements.
The manufacturer is responsible for ensuring that the devices meet the requirements of the regulation and that they can move freely within the EU and be put into service in accordance with their intended purpose.
Importers and distributors must:
ensure that the manufacturer has carried out a performance study on the devices before placing them on the EU market;
within 3 months of placing them into service
conduct a market surveillance and market surveillance report to the manufacturer and the competent authority of the EU country in which the devices are placed on sale.
conduct assessments of the technical documentation based on its sampling plan and taking account of the relevant scientific and ethical review.
Monitoring of the manufacturers’ compliance
The European Commission must carry out market surveillance, monitoring and surveillance of the manufacturer, the distributor and the market surveillance system of the device manufacturer.
EU countries may apply this provision also to manufacturers of devices that are not covered by this regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLYORK INTO FORCE?
It has applied since 1 January 2015.
BACKGROUND
 			
For more information, see:
‘In vitro medical devices’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 137:
Benchmark integrity and reliability requirements
Benchmark Integrity and relationability requirements
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1095/2010 on benchmarks
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the use of benchmarks to ensure their integrity and independence.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
investment benchmarks* and non-interest rate benchmarks* that are used in the European Union (EU).
It does not apply to interest rate benchmarks such as Libor, Euribor or Eurica.
It applies to benchmarks that are not considered to be critical benchmarks and that are subject to a process to determine whether they should be considered critical benchmarks.
The European Securities and Markets Authority (ESMA) has the power to impose sanctions on any non-compliance with the regulation’s rules.
Contributors to a benchmark
A benchmark is considered a critical benchmark if:
it is used in more than one EU country;
it has a significant impact on the financial stability of the economy of the country in which it is published.
A critical benchmark may not be used if it does not meet certain conditions, such as:
a minimum level of liquidity;
a high degree of reliability;
an absence of conflicts of interest between the contributor and the author of the benchmark;
the contribution of a non-significant benchmark to a significant benchmark does not exceed a maximum amount of €500,000.
Critical benchmarks can be determined using a quantitative criterion or a qualitative criterion.
Non-significant benchmarks
A significant benchmark is defined as a benchmark that does not have a significant effect on the economic stability of an EU country.
Administrators
An administrator must publish, by means that ensure fair and easy access, a benchmark statement for each benchmark or, where applicable, for each family of benchmarks, that may be used in EU countries.
In addition, an administrator must:
ensure that a benchmark is published in a language that is easily understood by the general public;
keep a register of all the contributors and users of a benchmark.
If an administrator does not publish a benchmark, he or she must inform the competent authority of the EU country where the benchmark was published or disseminated, as well as publish a corrective statement about any past contributions to or figures of that benchmark, in accordance with the rules of the European Commission.
Monitoring
An EU country may decide to prohibit a benchmark from being used in another EU country if it considers that it is not consistent with the requirements of the regulation or that it has not complied with its obligations under the relevant legislation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 30 June 2016.
BACKGROUND
 
For more information, see:
Key terms used in benchmarks (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Critical benchmark: a benchmark which is considered to have significant effects on economic stability and the financial health of an economy.
* Significant benchmark: an important benchmark that is used to determine the value of assets and liabilities of a company.

Summary 138:
Ecodesign requirements for energy-related appliances and fittings — rules for their sale and putting into service in the EU and non-EU countries
Ecodesigned requirements for electricity-efficient appliances and fitting
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on the harmonisation of the laws of the Member States relating to energy-efficient products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the sale of energy efficient products and appliances in the European Union (EU).
It repeals Directive 2009/142/EC.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all new and second-hand electrical appliances and electrical fittings, whether new or secondhand, imported into the EU or imported from a third country.
Manufacturers and distributors are responsible for ensuring that the products comply with the requirements laid down in the regulation.
It does not apply to:
new or second hand electrical appliances or fittings imported from outside the EU;
old or second- hand appliances or appliances imported from the EU.
Importers must ensure that the appliances or the fittings are compatible with the local gas supply conditions.
The manufacturer is responsible for drawing up the EU declaration of conformity, which must be accompanied by a certificate of conformity.
Distributors must ensure the appliance or the fitting bears the CE conformity marking and provide the relevant national authorities with information on the conformity assessment results.
National authorities must ensure they carry out conformity assessments and inform the manufacturer of the results of the assessments.
In addition, national authorities must take account of the safety requirements of Directive 2014/53/2014/35/EU when carrying out market surveillance checks.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISOLATION APPLYEAR OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
 
It entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The legislation is part of the ‘new approach’ principles, as set out in the Council Resolution of 7 May 1985 on a new approach to technical harmonisation and standards.
For more information, see:

* Conformity assessment: an assessment of whether a product complies with the relevant safety and environmental requirements.

Summary 139:
Cash-in-transit (CIT) transport of euro cash in CIT vehicles
Cash cash-in–transit
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1072/2010 on cross-border transport of cash in–cash transport by road
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the cross–border transport by cash in transport (CTT) of euro notes and coins by road between participating EU countries.
KEY POINTS
Cross-border CIT transport
The regulation applies to the transport of €100,000 and €500,000 in euro cash by road by CIT vehicle between participating Member States in accordance with the conditions laid down in Regulation (EC) No 1172/2009 on common rules for access to the international road haulage market (see summary).
It does not apply to:
cash deliveries/pick-ups of €10,000 or €50,000;
cash transfers between Member States of less than 5 days’ duration;
cross-border cash deliveries of €500 or €1,000 per day.
Companies operating in the CIT sector must apply for a CIT licence from the competent authority of the Member State of origin.
The licence must be valid for a maximum period of 4 years from the date on which it is issued.
CIT companies must comply with the following conditions:
the vehicle is of ordinary appearance;
there are at least 2 CIT security staff per vehicle;
none of the security staff wears a uniform.
the company is established in the country of origin;
the CIT company’s employer is located in another participating Member State.
If the company does not have a licence, it must provide the relevant authorities with:
a copy of the licence,
the original or a certified copy of a valid CIT certificate,
a certificate of authorisation issued by the granting authority,
an application form and a copy of an application form.
In addition, the company must:
provide the competent authorities of the host Member State with information on the type of vehicle used for CIT deliveries/picks-ups and the number and duration of deliveries and pick-ups per day;
ensure that the vehicle is equipped with the necessary equipment to carry out the deliveries and/or picks-ups;
apply for and receive an ad hoc initial training module as detailed in Annex VI of the regulation.
Where a company is found to be in breach of the above conditions, it may be subject to an administrative penalty of up to €10 000.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
 
For more information, see:
‘Cash in transport’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Ибъбрашкованска граблак города
Commission Implementing Decision 2010/852/EU of 20 December 2010 on the cross-Border Transport of euro Cash in–Cash Transport by Road (OJ L 183, 21.12.2010, pp. 1–8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (Euratom) No 1080/2010 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 140:
Foods — labelling and labelling of meat and poultry
Foods— labelling
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1169/2011 on food information law
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the labelling, labelling* and information on meat, poultry and fish in the EU.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all foods intended for human consumption, including those intended for animal or vegetable consumption.
It does not apply to:
meat and poultry;
eggs and poultry products;
fish and shellfish;
salt and sugar-free fish;
meat, poultry or poultry products.
The food must be labelled with the following information:
the name of the meat or poultry species and the type of meat;
the amount of protein, carbohydrate, fat, saturates, sugars, salt, protein, fibre and other nutrients and the percentage of the reference intakes of each of these nutrients and nutrients;
a list of the substances or products which may cause allergies or intolerances;
an indication of the origin of the food.
In the absence of a list of ingredients, the label must contain the word ‘contains’, followed by the name of a substance or product which is likely to cause an allergy or intolerance.
Nutrition declaration
The nutrition declaration must include the energy value and the amount of nutrients and/or nutrients, as well as a percentage of reference intakes. It must be expressed on the basis of per portion or per consumption unit alone.
Additional mandatory particulars for specific types or categories of foods are listed in the annexes to the regulation (Annex I and II).
The label must include:
a description of the protein and carbohydrate content, the protein, the fat, the carbohydrate, the sugar, the fibre and the salt content, and an indication of any other substances or substances causing allergies or intolerance to the food, as listed in Annex III of the regulation;
instructions for the preparation of the nutrition declaration and for the use of the information provided in Annex IV.
Annex V sets out the information to be provided by the food business operator.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
  
It has applied since 1 January 2012.
BACKGROUND
The EU’s non-preferential rules of origin are laid down in Council Regulation (EEC) No 2913/92 establishing the Community Customs Code.
For more information, see:
Food information law (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Food information law: the regulation lays down the rules for food information laws in the European Union (EU).
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
Council Regulation (EU), Euratom, Euratom and the European Parliament of 11 December 2011 on the approximation of the laws of the Member States relating to food information in the field of food law (OJ L 183, 12.12.2011, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC) no 1169-2011 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 141:
Euro coins — circulation and 2-euro commemorative coins (2011-2013)
Euro coins – circulation and two-coin commemorative coin sets
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) No 552/2011 on the issue of euro coins
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the issuing and circulation of 2- and 3-coin euro coins.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all EU countries whose currency is the euro.
It does not apply to coins issued by non-euro-area countries.
EU countries may issue two types of euro coin: circulation coins and collector coins. These coins are intended to commemorate specific subjects, subject to limits set per year and per issuing EU country for the number of issues of such coins. They may not have a shaped edge with fine scallops or a ‘Spanish flower’ shape.
Collector coins are not issued with a view to their entry into circulation.
The Commission must conduct an impact assessment on the continued issuance of 1- and 2 cent coins. This assessment must include a cost-benefit analysis which takes into account the real production costs of those coins set against their value and benefits.
Issuance of circulation coins must not exceed the higher of the following two ceilings:
0,1 % of the cumulated total net number of 2 euro coins put into circulation by EU countries up to the beginning of the year preceding the end of the calendar year for each individual issue;
0.1.5% of the total number of circulating 2-centimetre coins in circulation coins for each issue.
Collection coins are issued on an aggregated basis in the volume of coin issuance to be approved by the European Central Bank. Collection coins have the status of legal tender only in the issuing Member State.
FROM WHEN DOES THE IMPLEMENTATION APPLY?
The implementing regulation has applied since 1 January 2012.
BACKGROUND
  
For more information, see:
‘Euro coins’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Circulation coins: coins denominated in euro and cent and complying with the denominations and technical specifications laid down by the Council of the European Union (ECU.S. 1-cent coins are legal tender in the United States, Canada, Japan and the United Kingdom (1).
* Collector coins are coins intended for collection.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Implementing Regulation 2011/552/EU of 20 December 2011 on the issuance and circulation conditions for the issue and circulation limits for the 2-coin and collector coin sets and repealing Council Regulation (EC) No 974/98 of 3 May 1998 on the introduction of the euro (OJ C 273, 16.12.2011, pp. 1–8)
RELATED DOCUMENTS
 
Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 1201/2013 of the Council and of the Representatives of the Governments of the Member States meeting within the Council on the harmonisation of the laws, regulations, administrative provisions and administrative provisions relating to the circulation of coins, notes and certificates of authenticity of coins and notes of authenticity, and amending Council Regulations (EC), Euratom and the European Economic and Social Committee on the payment of taxes and other administrative provisions related to the monetary policy of the Union, and on the application of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU, and repealing Regulations (EEC, EC) No 652/2008 and (EC).

Summary 142:
The European Social Fund (ESF) and its specific objectives
The European social fund (ESSF)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1081/2006 on the European social Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It sets out the mission and scope of the ESF, together with specific provisions concerning the type of activities that may be financed by it.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The ESF supports the development of social inclusion and combating poverty, in particular with regard to disadvantaged people such as the Roma.
It supports the social inclusion of young people and their families.
Its main objectives are to:
encourage young people to participate in the labour market;
promote the mobility of workers and social entrepreneurship;
contribute to local development;
support the social dialogue between social partners.
Programmes
The regulation sets out a number of specific priorities for ESF projects, including:
supporting young people who are unemployed or underemployed to find a job;
encouraging young people in education and training;
improving employability and promoting health and safety at work and increasing employability.
In addition, the regulation also sets out priority axes for the implementation of social innovation and transnational cooperation.
Cooperation between ESF and social partners
In order to achieve its objectives, the European Commission and the Member States must:
cooperate with the social partners and the relevant national authorities;
coordinate with the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee (EESC) on the development and implementation of ESF policies and actions;
assess the effectiveness, efficiency and impact of projects and actions in connection with its missions, taking account of the relevant Integrated Guidelines and relevant country-specific recommendations adopted in accordance with Article 121(2) and Article 148(4) TFEU and, where appropriate, at national level, the national reform programmes as well as other relevant national strategies and reports.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The Regulation entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The Social Fund is one of the main instruments of the European cohesion policy.
For more information, see:
‘The social fund’ on European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Employment, training and social inclusion (EYI): the social dimension of employment, training, social inclusion, social entrepreneurship and social dialogue.

Summary 143:
European statistics
European statistics	SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 on the production and dissemination of European statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the production, dissemination and analysis of statistics at European level.
KEY POINTS
EU countries must provide the European Commission (Eurostat) with data on the total population at national level for specific EU purposes.
The data must cover:
live births by sex, month of occurrence, live birth-order, mother’s age, country of birth, mother's country of citizenship and mother's region of residence;
deaths by age, sex, year of birth and country of residence.
Data sources must be based on the data sources chosen by the EU country in accordance with national law and practice.
Eurostat must ensure the quality of the data transmitted.
National and European statistical authorities, and, where applicable, other relevant national and regional authorities, should take account of the principles set out in the European Statistics Code of Practice, as reviewed and updated by the European Statistical System Committee on 28 September 2011.
In order to facilitate the carrying out of the feasibility studies referred to in this regulation, the EU may provide financial support to the national statistical institutes and other national authorities.
Implementing acts
The Commission may adopt implementing acts to ensure uniform conditions for the implementation of this regulation. These implementing acts must be adopted in line with the examination procedure laid down in Article 10(2) of the regulation.
References
Each year, EU countries must send Eurostat data on:
the total population of their country of origin, as defined in Regulation (EC) No 1059/2003;
the number of people who have been born or who are expected to be born in the country of their birth;
total deaths by age and year of occurrence.
Each reference period for population data must be between 1 January and 31 December. The first reference period was 2013 and the last reference period will be 2027.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2012.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for producing and disseminating European statistics.
For more information, see:
‘European statistics’ on Eurostat's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Total population: the total number of persons who are born or expected to live in a given EU country.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  барска градка

Summary 145:
European Maritime and Fisheries Fund (EMFF)
European Maritime & Fisheries Fund
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2018/852 — establishing the European Maritime and fisheries Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
 
   
It sets out the EMFF’s objectives and aims.
KEY POINTS
The EMFF supports the implementation of the Common Fisheries Policy (CFP).
The CFP aims to:
promote sustainable and selective fishing in EU waters;
contribute to the conservation of marine ecosystems;
encourage the sustainable development of coastal and rural regions;
support the sustainable management of marine resources;
provide environmental services.
The fund supports:
fisheries and aquaculture;
the promotion of human capital, job creation and social dialogue;
environmental protection;
stakeholder participation and cooperation between EU countries in designing and implementing conservation measures and regionalisation.
Funding
EMFF support is based on the following criteria:
the total financial contribution from the EU financial support allocated per EU country is not more than 5% of the total amount of the EU budget allocated per country;
measures taken by EU countries to reduce the fishing capacity of EU waters are not covered by the CFP.
Support for business start–up
The Fund supports small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) in the fishing sector, as well as SMEs in other sectors such as tourism, agriculture and forestry.
Fishing vessels are not eligible for EMFF support.
Aquaculture is also not eligible.
FROM WHEN DOES THE IMP APPLY?
The IMP applies from 1 January 2014 to 31 December 2020.
BACKGROUND
For more information, see:
‘The IMP’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Fishing vessel: a large-scale fishing vessel that can carry more than 1,000 tonnes of fish per year.

  Еганска грацка, г.бракскога,   бърабка.

Summary 146:
Insurance-based investment products for retail investors — key investor information
Insurance - investment products — key information information
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1094/2010 on the key information document for retail investment products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules to ensure that retail investors have access to a standardised information document on investment products designed to help them understand and use the products they buy.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all insurance-related investment products (PRIIPs) which are marketed, distributed or sold to retail investors in the EU.
It does not apply to pension funds, life insurance, annuities, pension funds or other forms of investment that are not covered by Directive 2009/65/EC (see summary).
KEY TERMS
PRIIP:
an investment product designed to provide specific investment solutions tailored to the needs of retail investors, which are frequently combined with insurance coverage or can be complex and difficult to understand.
MAIN DOCUMENT
The European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority (EIOPA) is responsible for drawing up and publishing a ‘key information document’ to help retail investors to compare different PRIIPs. It must be accurate, fair, clear and not misleading.
The document must contain information on:
the type and nature of the investment product;
the risks and risks associated with the product and its risks;
a description of the product’s investment objectives;
its risks and benefits;
how the product can be taken out early;
where a retail investor can take money out early.
A person advising on, or selling a PRIIP may satisfy the requirements of the regulation by providing a PRI document to a person with written authority to make investment decisions on behalf of the retail investor in respect of transactions concluded under that written authority.
An explanatory statement must appear directly underneath the title of the document.
REFERENCES
Act
Entry into force
Deadline for transposition in the Member States
Official Journal of the European Union
Directive 2009/64/EC
20.12.2009
20th day following the date of entry into force of its publication in the Official Journal.
OJ L 331 of 24.11.2009.
Amending act(s)
Entry in force
Obligations
The EIOPA may impose a prohibition or restriction on the marketing or sale of an insurance product if it considers that the product does not comply with all the relevant requirements of this regulation. It may also impose a ban or restriction if the following conditions are fulfilled:
it is contrary to EU law in the area of accounting according to the last available consolidated financial statements approved by the management body of the ultimate parent undertaking.
If the conditions set out in the first subparagraph are fulfilled, the competent authority may prohibit or restrict the sale of the insurance product on a precautionary basis before the product has been marketed or sold.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
  
It has applied since 1 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
The key information documents must be drawn up in standardised format which allows retail investors easily compare different products.
For more information, see:
‘Insurance products’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY INFORMATION DOCUMENTS
KEY ISSUES
 
KEY INSURANCE DOCUMENCE
The product information document must include the following information:
a summary of the risk and risks involved;
an explanation of how the product is designed to be taken into account in the investment decision-making process;
information on the risk profile of the products and the risks and advantages of taking out early investment.
This information must be made available to the consumer in a format that is clear, understandable and understandable, and must be accompanied by an explanatory statement.
In addition, the document must be reproduced in a language that is easily understood by the consumer and that is not misleading or unintelligible.
PRIPs must be published in accordance with Regulation (EC) No 45/46/EC on the processing of personal data and must comply with the relevant disclosure of product information requirements for those products or whether to include pension products in their product information.
WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLYING?
From 1 January 2012.

Summary 148:
Noise-related operating restrictions at European Union airports
Noise - related measures
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2014 on noise-related measures at EU airports
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to improve the effectiveness of the EU’s air navigation and air traffic management networks by limiting noise at certain EU airports.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU airports, whether or not they are international airports. It does not apply to aircraft such as military aircraft and aircraft undertaking customs, police and fire-fighting operations.
It does not affect the allocation of slots for the provision of air navigation services and network functions at these airports, nor does it apply to the operation of air traffic control (ATC) services.
Rules on the introduction of operating restrictions
EU countries must ensure that:
noise performance information is obtained in a transparent manner and that it is accessible to the relevant authorities and stakeholders;
airport authorities and local residents, or their representatives, and relevant local authorities are consulted, and that technical information on noise mitigation measures is provided to them;
the cost-effectiveness of any new operating restriction is assessed, including, where relevant, their cross-border impact.
The European Commission must report to the European Parliament and to the Council on the application of the regulation by 14 June 2021.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
 
It has applied since 14 June 2014.
BACKGROUND
The Regulation is part of a package of measures adopted by the European Commission implementing Directive 2002/49/EC on the implementation of common EU rules on noise.
For more information, see:
Airport noise (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Noise: any noise emitted by an aircraft that is likely to have a significant impact on human health or the environment.
* Noise: any sound emitted by the aircraft of a given size and duration.
ACT
Council Decision 2014/852/EU of 13 June 2014 on the harmonisation of the laws of the Member States relating to the imposition of certain types of noise operating restrictions (OJ L 94, 14.6.2014, pp. 1-8)
RELATED ACTS

Directive 2002/48/EC lays down common rules for the allocation and management of slots at Community airports (See summary).

Summary 149:
Cross-border insolvency proceedings: common rules for creditors and practitioners
Cross-Border insolvencies: Common rules for creditor and practitioner
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1215/2012 on the application of certain provisions of Regulation (EC) No 1346/2000 on cross-border proceedings
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down common rules to ensure that creditors who have their habitual residence, domicile or registered office in the EU are informed about the opening of proceedings relating to their debtor’s assets.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all proceedings, whether they are opened by a court in the country in which the debtor is resident or in another EU country.
It does not apply to proceedings opened before the entry into force of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU).
Creditors are entitled to participate in other proceedings on creditors to oppose such lodgement or to withdraw the lodgement of their claims where the law applicable so provides.
The creditor has the right to request that proceedings be opened in a country other than the country where the proceedings have been opened. The creditor may also request that the proceedings are opened in another country if they have not been opened in their country of habitual residence.
A coordinator is appointed by the court to assist the creditor in the preparation of a group coordination plan. The coordinator must communicate with the court in accordance with the official language applicable to that court.
Cooperation and communication between courts
The coordinator is assisted by:
the debtor in the debtor in possession of the debtor's assets
the creditor in possession
the court which delivered the decision to open proceedings.
the coordinator who has been appointed.
Amending Regulation (EU countries
In addition to the general rules laid down in the regulation, the European Court of Justice (ECJ) has adopted a number of specific rules. These include the following:
a list of the parties involved in the proceedings and the terms and conditions under which the proceedings may be opened.
An obligation on the creditor to inform the creditor of the date, time and location of the proceedings in which they are to be opened and the nature and content of the undertaking to avoid secondary proceedings
A requirement for creditors to be informed when the proceedings relate to their assets are opened. Creditors must also be informed of the conditions for publication in the Official Journal of the Courts of the EU country of the country of origin of proceedings for which they have been appointed, as well as of the terms of the agreement between the parties to take, or to refrain from taking, certain steps or actions.
In the event of a dispute between the creditor and the creditor, the creditor is entitled to lodge an undertaking to be treated as if secondary proceedings had been opened if the proceedings had already been opened, as long as the undertaking has been given in writing. The undertaking must be binding on the estate.
Where the creditor lodges a claim against the debtor, he or she must be informed in writing of the grounds for lodging the claim.
If a court considers that the creditor has not complied with the undertaking, it may order that the claim be withdrawn or that the claims be lodged in another court. In such cases, the court must inform the debtor of the reasons for the lodging of the claim and of the measures to be taken to prevent the claim from being lodged.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
Directive 2014/33/EU has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
   
 
For more information, see:
‘Cross-boundary insolventcy proceedings’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Егράντικη (OJ L 157, 29.4.2012, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EEC) no 1215-2012 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 150:
Athens Convention relating to the carriage of passengers and their luggage by sea
Athens convention relating to passenger and their Luggage by Sea
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 552/2008 — liability rules for damage caused to passengers and luggage by sea under the Athens Convention
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for liability rules to ensure a proper level of compensation for passengers involved in maritime accidents.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to the liability of the carrier and the performing carrier for the loss of or damage to passengers’ cabin luggage, as well as the carrier’s servants and agents acting within the scope of their employment.
Limits of liability for death and personal injury are set out in the annex to the regulation.
It does not apply to:
the carriage of goods by sea;
the carrying of passengers by a performing carrier;
damage caused to the cabin luggage.
Liability of carriers
The liability of carriers and their performing carriers is limited to 2 250 units of account per passenger, per carriage.
Insurers
Each EU Member State must issue a certificate to any carrier or performing carrier that has been party to the convention. Such a certificate must be in the official language or languages of the issuing State.
The carrier must inform the State of the place of departure of the ship on which the carriage is to be carried and the place where the luggage will be re-delivered to the passenger within a reasonable time after the departure.
A State must also inform the claimant of any delays resulting from labour disputes or any other causes of delay in the return of the luggage, but does not include delays due to labour disputes.
Notice of loss or damage
The passenger must be provided with a written notice of loss and damage to the luggage before departure. The carrier must provide the claimant with a copy of the certificate.
In addition, the claimant must be informed of the date and place of arrival of the vessel and of any damage caused by the carrier.
If security is furnished in several Member States, the carrier must also provide the passenger with a notice of the security measures to be taken in the event of a security breach.
Implementation of the regulation
Member States must apply the rules laid down in the regulation when drawing up their national insurance policies.
An EU country may withdraw from the regulation if the conditions under which they have been issued are not complied with.
Amending Regulation (EU) 2019/852 amends the regulation to take account of the changes to the International Maritime Organisation (IMO) Guidelines on the insurance arrangements for the carriage by sea of passengers, their luggage and their means of transport.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
    дарскаблакова барка
  гаровка 
It has applied since 1 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
 
  δαρημάντικη (European Commission)
For more information, see:
‘The Athens Convention’ on the European Commission's Directorate-General for Justice website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC), Euratom, Euratom and the European Economic and Social Committee of 15 December 2008 laying down liability rules on damage caused in the case of damage caused on board a passenger ship by accident (OJ L 136, 17.12.2008, pp. 1-8)

Summary 152:
Road transport operators — professional qualification
Road transportation operators — Professional qualification
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2010 on professional qualification for road transport operators
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It sets out the rules for the professional qualification of road transport companies.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all road transport undertakings operating in the European Union (EU).
It aims to improve the level of professional qualification and the transparency of the EU’s national electronic register of road haulage and passenger transport companies, in order to improve road safety.
It does not apply to undertakings that have been suspended or withdrawn from the market because they no longer fulfil the requirements laid down in the regulation.
The European Commission must draw up a list of categories, types and degrees of serious infringements of EU rules which, in addition to those set out in Annex IV, may lead to the loss of good repute.
Penalties for serious offences are effective, proportionate and dissuasive.
EU countries may decide to exempt from examination certain persons who have continuously managed a road transport undertaking or a road passenger transport undertaking in one or more EU countries for the period of 10 years before 4 December 2009.
Certificates of professional competence
The competent authority of an EU country must issue a certificate of competence to any person holding a licence to engage in road transport activities. This certificate must contain the following information:
the name and address of the transport company;
the date and place of establishment of establishment;
a copy of the driving licence and the number of the driver and the place of the vehicle;
any other relevant information relevant to the undertaking.
Where an undertaking no longer meets the requirements of the regulation, the competent authority may suspend or withdraw its authorisation.
In addition, EU countries may require an undertaking whose authorisation has been suspended, withdrawn or suspended to ensure that it no longer fulfils the requirements listed in Annex II.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
It has applied since 4 December 2010.
BACKGROUND

Summary 153:
Social security insurance for EU residents moving within the EU
Social security Insurance for EU nationals moving within EU
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 883/2004 on the application of social security schemes
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for applying social security insurance to employed persons and their families who move within the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all EU citizens who are covered by the social security system of an EU country and who have moved to another EU country to work or live.
It does not apply to people who have left the EU or who have not yet moved to the EU.
The aim of the regulation is to simplify and streamline administrative procedures between social security institutions in the EU and the EU countries of origin and destination.
In addition, it aims to improve cooperation between the authorities and the institutions of the different EU countries.
Scope
It applies to:
employment, employment, self-employment or residence completed under the legislation of a Member State;
social security schemes for the period between 1 January and 31 December of each year;
periods of insurance completed in another Member State, provided that these periods do not overlap.
Beneficiaries and employers
When a person applies for social security benefits, the institution responsible or the scheme applicable or for designating periods of insurance to a specific scheme must inform the institution of the place of residence or of their place of employment or of stay. The institution must then inform the person concerned and employers of any changes in the law of the Member State in which the benefits are to be applied.
If a person is refused access to the benefits, he or she must be informed of the reasons for the rejection and of the measures to be taken to remedy the situation.
When an institution rejects a claim, it must provide the applicant with a certificate to prove that the claim has been rejected. The certificate must be forwarded to the competent institution in the country of origin or to the institution which provided the benefits in kind, which will then be considered as sickness insurance benefits.
Where a claim is rejected, the claimant must be notified of the result of the review in writing.
A dispute concerning a particular claim may not hinder the reimbursement of another claim or other claims.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2005.
BACKGROUND
 
 			
For more information, see:
‘Sickness insurance’ on the European Commission’s website.
KEY TERMS
* Social security insurance: a system of social protection for people who are unemployed or self-employed.
* Employer: the employer of a person who has been employed for a period of at least 6 months.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Игородскаблакова града  года   бакта

Public health & health and safethe safety of workers
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 on the collection of comparable data and information in the area of occupational safety and health at work
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
