Summary 155:
Quality of job vacancy statistics in the European Union (EU) — quarterly production of statistics on job vacancies and seasonal adjusted job vacancies
Quality of employment data in the EU
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2004 on the quality of EU job vacancies statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the requirements for EU countries to collect and transmit quarterly statistics on employment vacancies*.
KEY POINTS
EU countries must collect and send to the European Commission (Eurostat) statistical data on the number of job vacancies in their country each quarter.
The data cover all economic activities defined by the common classification system for economic activities in the Community (NACE) in force, except for the activities of households as employers and activities of extraterritorial organisations and bodies.
Data are collected using business surveys. The data are transmitted to Eurostat by EU countries on the first reference quarter of each calendar year. The date of the first data delivery is determined in accordance with the regulatory procedure with scrutiny provided for in Decision 1999/468/EC (see summary).
The Commission assesses the quality and timeliness of the data transmitted by the EU countries.
Eurostat then forwards the data to the Commission, which then forwards them to the Statistical Programme Committee, which assesses their quality and ensures that the data comply with the regulation’s requirements.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
  
It has applied since 1 January 2005.
BACKGROUND
The regulation is part of the Action Plan on EMU Statistical Requirements for the development of a legal basis for EU statistics.
For more information, see:
‘Quality of Employment Statistics’ on Eurostat's website.
KEY TERMS
Job vacancy statistics: statistical data covering all types of employment, including vacancies broken down, inter alia, by economic activity.

Ensuring competition in the EU’s natural gas transmission market (Regulation (EC) No 713/2009 on conditions for access to the internal market in natural gas (ENTSO for Gas)
Establishing competition through liquid wholesale markets for gas
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2009/73/EC — rules for the establishment of a European internal market for natural gas
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
 
It sets out the conditions for the creation of a competitive market for gas transmission networks in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all natural gas distribution and transmission networks, except for storage facilities, which are covered by Regulation (EU) No 1775/2005.
It does not apply to gas storage facilities.
Transmission system operators must publish at least annually, by a predetermined deadline, all planned maintenance periods that might affect network users’ rights from transport contracts and corresponding operational information with adequate advance notice.
National regulatory authorities must ensure compliance with the rules contained in this regulation and the guidelines adopted by the European Network of Transmission System Operators for Gas (ENTSO).
Transparency requirements concerning transmission system operators
Transmitting system operators are required to provide the European Commission with:
transmission system users with the technical information necessary for network users to gain effective network access;
information on the operation of the transmission system;
transparency requirements regarding exit points within a system or subsystem that is not connected to another transmission or distribution system but to a single industrial final customer, where the publication of such data would reveal confidential information as to the production process of that final customer.
The Commission must ensure that the information is made available on request to those affected by any disruption.
In addition, the Commission must take appropriate action to ensure that:
the Commission adopts a Community-wide network development plan, the draft annual work programme, the information regarding the consultation process and the other documents referred to in the regulation;
the Agency adopts an opinion on the proposed amendments to the network codes and recommends them for adoption by the Commission.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLACE?
It has applied since 1 July 2009.
BACKGROUND
  
For more information, see:
‘Transmission of natural gas’ on the ENTSO website.
KEY TERMS
* Transmission system operator: a natural gas system operator responsible for the transmission and distribution of gas from a gas distribution system to a gas storage system.
* Storage system: a storage system that is used to store gas for use in the production of electricity, heating, cooling and heating of a gas-intensive industrial final consumer.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Implementing Decision 2009/83/EC of 20 June 2009 laying down rules for establishing a European Internal Market for Natural Gas (Ensco for Gas Regulation)

Summary 158:
Agreements between EU countries and non-EU countries on civil law
Agreements with non-European neighbours
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2009 on mutual legal assistance in civil matters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a procedure to authorise an EU country to amend an existing agreement or to negotiate a new agreement with a third country on matters of civil law.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all EU countries, except Denmark, which is bound by the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU) and the Protocol on the position of Denmark.
It does not apply to certain regional agreements between a few Member States and a few third countries, for example two or three, intended to address local situations and not open for accession to other countries.
The aim of the regulation is to provide an adequate legal framework to meet specific needs of a given EU country in its relations with a non-EEA country.
Amendments to existing agreements
An EU country may wish to amend or negotiate an agreement between itself and a third EU country on the same subject matter. It must notify the European Commission of its intention to do so within 90 days of receiving a notification from the other EU country. The Commission must assess whether the agreement meets the conditions set out in the regulation.
If the Commission considers that the agreement does not meet the conditions, it must give an opinion on the application of the EU country within 30 days of receipt of the notification and give a reasoned decision on the authorising the agreement to be concluded.
Authorisation to conclude the agreement
The agreement may contain a clause providing for either:
the inclusion of particular clauses in the envisaged agreement or
the possibility for a direct replacement of the relevant provisions of the agreement by the provisions of such a subsequent agreement.
Notification to the Commission
The Commission must give its opinion on whether the proposed agreement meets all the conditions for authorising its conclusion.
In the event that the Commission does not authorise the opening of formal negotiations on the agreement, the agreement may be terminated.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
 
It entered into force on 1 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
  
For more information, see:
Judicial cooperation in civil law (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* Mutual legal assistance: the legal assistance provided by the EU to a third party in the event of a dispute between the parties.
* Civil law: the law of a country with which the EU has a formal or informal relationship.
ACT
Council Regulation (EC), Euratom, Euratom of 20 May 2009 on the Mutual Legal Assistance in Civil Matters
REFERENCES

Summary 159:
Statistics on migration and asylum — collection and analysis of EU statistics
Statistics on migrants and asylum
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 311/76/2008 — collection, analysis and dissemination of statistics on migration
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the collection and collection of statistics in the field of migration.
KEY POINTS
The regulation requires EU countries to provide the European Commission (Eurostat) with statistics on the number of persons illegally resident in the EU and on the total number of asylum seekers.
The statistics covered by the regulation relate to reference periods of one calendar year and must be supplied to Eurostat within 3 months of the end of the reference year. The first reference month is January 2008.
Data sources and quality standards
EU countries must provide Eurostat with all the information necessary to ensure the quality, reliability, objectivity, scientific independence, cost-effectiveness and statistical confidentiality of the statistics.
Eurostat is responsible for collecting, analysing and disseminating the statistics to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee, the Committee of the Regions and the Committee on the Statistical Programmes of the European Communities.
It must also ensure that the statistics provided comply with the statistical standards set out in the annex to the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 20 August 2009.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Migration statistics’ on Eurostat’s website.
MAIN DOCUMENTRY INTO FORCE
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 652/2008
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATIONS DO?
This regulation lays down the rules on how EU countries must collect, analyse and disseminate statistics on immigration and asylum in order to ensure fair and effective EU policies on migration, as well as to ensure accurate, timely and harmonised statistical information for EU countries and the European Statistical System Committee (ESSC).
KEY TERMS
* Migration statistics:
statistics on the numbers of people illegally entering or staying in an EU country and the number who are granted or refused entry or stay.
* Asylum seekers:
the number of requests for information for the taking back or taking charge of an asylum seeker;
the decisions taken in response to the requests referred to in point (a);
the numbers of transfers to which the decisions referred to point (c) lead;
illegal entry and stay: statistics on illegal entry and staying of people who are not entitled to stay in the country.
ACT
Council Decision (EC), Euratom of 20 June 2008 on the application of Council Regulation (EEC) no 311/1976 of 20 August 2008 laying down detailed rules on the collection, processing and dissemination by Member States of statistics relating to migration and on asylum (OJ L 284, 20.8.2008, pp. 1-8)

Summary 160:
EU statutory audit rules
EU statutory auditor rules
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 10/2011/EU on statutory audit
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
  
It aims to improve the independence of statutory auditors* and audit firms* in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out the rules for the selection of statutory auditor* firms and the selection procedure for their engagement with EU countries.
The selection procedure is based on a recommendation by the audit committee of the audit firm. The committee recommends at least two choices for the audit engagement and must express a duly justified preference for one of them.
A sound engagement quality control review of the work carried out in each statutory audit engagement should be conducive to high audit quality.
EU countries may apply more stringent requirements than set out in this regulation.
Auditors must ensure that their work complies with the principles of independence, confidentiality and professional secrecy in relation to cooperation among competent authorities and with the competent judicial authorities.
An audit report must be in clear and unambiguous language. The audit committee must be able to identify any irregularities and take appropriate measures to deal with such irregularities and to prevent any recurrence of such irregularities in the audit report.
Quality assurance, market monitoring, and transparency of competent authorities
The audit committee is responsible for:
ensuring that the competent authorities have a quality assurance system in place to ensure that the audit firms comply with the regulation’s requirements;
providing a report on the overall results of the quality assurance systems on an annual basis;
assessing the overall quality assurance of audit firms’ work on a regular basis.
reporting on the quality of audit work on the basis of an annual quality assurance report;
checking that audit firms are complying with the requirements of the regulation and that they have complied with its requirements.
Exemptions from the regulation
The European Commission may exempt cooperatives within the meaning of point (14) of Directive 2006/43/EC, savings banks or similar entities as referred to in Article 45 of Directive 86/635/EEC or their subsidiaries or legal successors from this regulation provided that they comply with its principles of impartiality and that their independence are complied with.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2012.
BACKGROUND
 
For more information, see:
‘Auditors’ on the European Commission's website.
KEY TERMS
* Statutory auditor: a statutory auditor or an audit firm that performs audits on behalf of a public-interest entity.
* Audit firm: a firm that carries out audit work for a public interest entity, such as a bank or a company that has a market capitalisation of less than €100 million.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC) No 2010/660/EU of 13 December 2010 on statutory auditor selection and selection procedure (OJ L 183, 14.12.2010, pp. 1-8)

Summary 161:
Conservation of marine biological resources and fisheries targeting them (Common fisheries policy)
Conserving marine biological resource and fisheries targets them (common fisheries policy).
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2010 — common fisheries policy
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down common rules for the conservation of the marine environment and the management of fisheries targeting it.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to the EU’s Common Fisheries Policy (CFP).
It aims to ensure that the long-term conservation of marine biodiversity and the sustainable management of fishery resources is ensured.
The CFP is based on the ecosystem-based approach to fisheries management, which ensures that negative impacts of fishing activities on the marine ecosystem are minimised, and ensures that aquaculture and fisheries activities avoid the degradation of marine environment.
It applies to all EU countries, except Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway, Switzerland and the United Kingdom (1), which are responsible for managing their own fisheries.
In addition, the CFP applies to non-EU countries as well as to the European Economic Area (EEA).
The European Commission is responsible for the implementation of the regulation.
Regionalisation
The EU countries are required to develop and implement regional cooperation on conservation measures.
To achieve this, the Commission must encourage the exchange of information and best practices among EU countries and facilitate the coordination of national measures foreseen in the multiannual national strategic plan.
Sustainable fisheries partnership agreements (SFPs)
SFPAs are signed between EU countries with the aim of ensuring that sustainable fisheries are managed in line with the objectives set out in the EU fisheries policy.
EU countries must ensure that sustainable fishing opportunities are allocated according to transparent and objective criteria, including those of an environmental, social and economic nature.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2011.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Fisheries policy’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Common fisheries policy: a common framework for sustainable fisheries management.
MAINTRODUCTIONS

Entry into force
Deadline for transposition in the Member States

Summary 163:
Securities settlement systems (CSDs) — rules for cross-border services
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1095/2010 on securities settlement systems
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the establishment, operation and supervision of the securities settlement system (CSD) market in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all CSDs providing securities settlement services in the EU.
It does not apply to non-banking-type ancillary services, such as investment banking services, which are regulated by the European Securities and Markets Authority (ESMA).
It lays down detailed rules on the conduct of business rules for CSDs.
Settlement periods
CSDs are required to:
ensure that their services are available to all market participants, irrespective of their country of establishment;
provide the relevant information to the relevant authorities of the EU country in which they are based;
keep records of their activities, including the date and time of their initial book-entry into the settlement system;
report to the European Commission every 3 years on the activities of the CSD.
The CSD is subject to the supervision of EU countries’ competent authorities.
Authorisation
A CSD must apply for authorisation from the competent authority of the host EU country to provide services to an issuer. The authorisation must specify the core services listed in Section A of the annex to the regulation, as well as part of its business rules.
An EU country’s competent authority may withdraws the authorisation if it becomes aware of one of the circumstances which give rise to a change in the identity of the persons exercising control over the operation of a CSD, or if it is unable to fulfil its obligations.
EU countries must ensure that CSDs comply with the rules laid down in the regulation and that they are subject to appropriate sanctions and other measures in the event of infringements.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 18 June 2010.
BACKGROUND
 
The European Commission adopted Directive 2014/65/EU on the harmonisation of financial rules for securities markets.
For more information, see:
‘Settlement systems’ (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* Securities settlement system: a system used to settle securities transactions between issuers and counterparties.
* CSD: a company that provides services to issuers in order to facilitate the settlement of securities transactions.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 			
Council Regulation (EU), Euratom, Euratom and the European Parliament of 17 June 2010 on the establishment of a framework for the operation, operation, supervision and enforcement of the Securities Settlement Systems Directive (SDS Directive) (OJ L 183, 18.6.2010, pp. 1–32)

Cohesion fund
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1316/2013 establishing the European Regional Development Fund (ERDF)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up the Cohesion Fund to provide financial support to projects in the fields of environment and trans-European networks in the area of transport infrastructure.
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out the type of activities which can be supported by the fund, in order to contribute to the investment priorities within the thematic objectives set out in Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council.
The fund is funded by the European Commission and the European Economic and Social Fund (ESF).
The European Commission has the power to adopt delegated acts on the basis of Article 290 TFEU of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU.
It provides financial support for projects of European added value (e.g. projects of common interest) in the areas of environment, transport infrastructure, public authorities and stakeholders and efficient public administration.
Scope of support
The Cohesion fund supports transport infrastructure projects under the Connecting Europe Facility (CEF) for an amount of EUR 10 000 000 000 in accordance with Article 92(6) of Regulation (EC) No 1303/2013 on the European Union’s common output indicators (see summary).
Specific provisions concerning the type and scope of support are laid down in Annex I to the regulation.
In order to increase flexibility and reduce the administrative burden through joint implementation, the ERDFID and the EEFID are aligned with the EDFID priorities.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGULATION APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE?
   
It entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EDF is one of the main instruments of the ESMART programme.

KEY TERMS

* Transport infrastructure: projects that contribute to improving the quality of life of people, goods and services in the EU by improving the safety and environmental performance of transport networks and reducing congestion, pollution and noise.

WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the general rules for the EU’s cooperation programmes with non-EU countries in the field of European territorial development (ERDF).

The regulation aims to strengthen cooperation by means of actions conducive to integrated territorial development linked to the EU's cohesion policy priorities and to reduce the backwardness of the least favoured regions, among which particular attention is to be paid to rural areas, areas affected by industrial transition, and regions which suffer from severe and permanent natural or demographic handicaps such as the northernmost regions with very low population density and island, cross-border and mountain regions.

The objectives of the regulation are as follows:
to strengthen cooperation in the fields of territorial development and sustainable development;
to contribute to the sustainable development of rural areas and to the development of industrial transition regions, particularly in rural areas; and
to reduce the disadvantaged regions’ social and economic development, in relation to industrial transition.

transnational cooperation;
interregional cooperation.

Summary 167:

WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to streamline, improve and simplify permit granting and financing procedures for energy infrastructure projects in the European Union (EU).

gas distribution networks;

the exemption from Article 16(6) of Directive 2009/72/EC or an exemption from Articles 36 and 37 (6) and 38 (10) of Regulation 2009/73/EC;

Summary 168:
Alternative dispute resolution (ADR) for online sales and service contracts
Alternative Dispute Resolution (ODR)*
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 on alternative dispute resolution
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the use of an online dispute resolution* platform (ODR) to resolve disputes between traders and consumers over online sales or service contracts.
KEY POINTS
Directive 2013/11/EU sets out the conditions for the establishment of the ODR platform.
The regulation lays down the rules for use of the platform, which is operated by the European Commission.
It also sets out a case management tool to be used by traders to settle disputes between consumers and ADR entities.
EU countries must ensure that the platform is up-to-date and that it is easily accessible for consumers.
To resolve disputes, the parties must:
agree to use ADR procedures to resolve the dispute;
set up an electronic complaint form to be made available on the platform;
provide an electronic translation function to enable the parties and the ADR entity to have the information which is exchanged through the platform and is necessary for the resolution of the dispute translated, where appropriate.
ADR entities must automatically and without delay transmit the complaint to the trader that the parties have agreed to use in accordance with the rules of the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
 
The ODR regulation entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to improve consumer protection in the EU’s online marketplaces.
For more information, see:

Summary 169:
The EU’s Common Agricultural Policy (CAP) for agriculture
The EU's Common Agriculture Policy for farming
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on the common agricultural policy
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the application of the common agriculture policy (CAP).
KEY POINTS
Directive 2014/40/EU
The regulation sets out rules for applying the common European agricultural policy for farming in the EU.
It repeals Regulation (EC) No 228/2013 and introduces a single-area payment scheme for farmers in EU countries having applied the single area payment scheme (SAP) since 1 January 2014.
In addition, it introduces a new system of direct payments for small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and small-scale enterprises (SSEs).
The new system is designed to reduce the administrative burden on farmers and to improve the efficiency and effectiveness of the current system of payments.
Direct payments are based on the following criteria:
the total value of the payment entitlements per hectare;
the number of hectares of land covered by the main crop; and
the average yield of the main crops.
The main crop must not cover more than 75 % of that arable land.
EU countries may decide to apply certain limitations for the first allocation of payments, such as the number of hectare and the maximum number of payments per year.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCELEGAL DOCUMENTIONS
   
The legislation applies from 1 January 1, 2014. It does not apply to:
direct payments for 2014 and 2015;
total payments for 2016 and 2017;
coverage of payments for 2018 and 2019;
capped payments for 2020 and 2021.

Summary 170:
Cooperation measures for agriculture, food production, forestry, rural development and sustainable rural development
Cooperation Measures for Agriculture, Food Production, Forestry, Rural Development and Sustainable Rural Development
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1303/2013 — co-operation measures between the European Commission, the European Agricultural Fund and the European Rural Development Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the conditions for granting aid under the Co-operation Measures (CMS) and Rural Development (RDP) measures.
It also sets out how the measures are implemented.
KEY POINTS
CMS
The regulation applies to:
agricultural, forestry and rural development programmes;
climate change mitigation and adaptation and biodiversity.
Rural development programmes
The aim of these programmes is to support the development of small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and women in rural areas by:
fostering innovation in agriculture and forestry;
encouraging and facilitating research and development;
providing financial support for rural development projects;
supporting the implementation of rural development strategies;
promoting the sustainable management of land and water resources;
improving and facilitating management of their holding.
Crop, animal, and plant insurance
The CMS and RDP provide financial support to farmers who lose more than 70% of their income due to natural disasters, adverse climatic events and catastrophic events.
The beneficiaries are:
farmers who lose at least 70 % of the income they make during the year in which they become eligible to receive the aid;
agri-food producers who lose 70 % or more of their incomes during the period in which the aid is provided;
small and medium sized enterprises which lose more money than they make from the loss of their production;
fisheries and aquaculture producers whose losses are less than 70 %.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2014.

Summary 173:
Service of judicial and extrajudicial documents in civil and commercial matters in the European Union (EU)
Service of legal documents in Civil and Commercial Matters
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1348/2000 on the service in the Member States of judicial* and other legal documents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the service of legal and other documents to be served in another EU country.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
the service of a document on the party’s authorised representative in the EU country where the proceedings are taking place regardless of the place of residence of that party;
the subsequent service once the addressee has exercised his right of refusal.
It does not apply to service of documents on the person authorised to represent the party in civil or commercial matters.
EU countries must designate the public officers, authorities or other persons, who are responsible for the transmission of judicial or other judicial documents to other EU countries, as ‘transmitting agencies’.
Each EU country must designate one or more agencies to be responsible for serving judicial and/or other documents. These agencies must:
ensure that the document is served within a specified period, the date to be taken into account with respect to the applicant should be that determined by the law of that EU country;
send a receipt to the transmitting agency by the swiftest possible means of transmission using the standard form set out in Annex I of the regulation;
make available to the Commission a manual containing the information referred to in Annex II of the information relating to the service.
send to the receiving agency a copy of the agreements concluded between the EU countries as well as drafts of such agreements or arrangements which they intend to adopt;
inform the Commission of any denunciation of, or amendments to, these agreements and arrangements.
The Commission must draw up and update regularly a manual, which must be made available electronically, in particular through the European Judicial Network in Civil Matters (EJNIM).
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
 
It has applied since 1 January 2006.
BACKGROUND

Summary 174:
Medicines for human use — advanced therapy medicinal products
Medicinal products for human uses — advanced therapies
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 726/2004 on the marketing of advanced therapy medicines
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the marketing, labelling and labelling of advanced therapies* for the treatment of diseases and dysfunctions of the human body.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all medicinal products intended for human or animal use. It does not apply to:
products containing or consisting exclusively of non-viable human, animal or animal cells and/or tissues and which do not act principally by pharmacological, immunological or metabolic action;
combined advanced therapy products*;
products which are not intended for use in combination with other medicinal products.
It does not cover:
tuberculosis, hepatitis B virus, hepatitis C virus, HIV/AIDS, tuberculosis of the skin, hepatitis A virus, cancer of the lungs, HIV-AIDS of the brain, and hepatitis C of the spine;
cancer of the heart, lungs, heart, brain, liver, lung, spine, spine and other organs;
sensory disorders of the central nervous system, such as chronic inflammatory bowel disease, chronic obstructive pulmonary disease, endometriosis and endometrial cancer.
Requirements for marketing
Manufacturers must ensure that their products comply with the regulation’s requirements.
They must ensure the following:
the product characteristics are listed on the outer packaging of the product and on the package leaflet;
the label and the product information sheet are clearly visible on the outside the packaging;
patients and healthcare providers must be informed of the products’ safety and efficacy;
they must have a system for patient and product traceability.
The European Commission must review the regulation in the light of scientific and technical developments in the field of biomedicine in order to adapt it to the specific nature of those products. It must also review the scope of this regulation, including in particular the regulatory framework for the manufacture of medicinal products for the use of human tissues and cells.
Post-authorisation follow-up of efficacy and adverse reactions, and risk management
The manufacturer must detail, in the marketing authorisation application, the measures envisaged to ensure that the product is followed-up after the end-use of an advanced therapy product and of adverse reactions thereto.
A Committee for Advanced Therapies is responsible for preparing a draft opinion on the quality, safety, efficacy and efficacy of each advanced therapy medicine for final approval by the European Medicines Agency's Committee for Medicinal Products for Human Use.
In addition, the Commission must draw up detailed guidelines on good clinical practice specific to advanced therapies.
Implementation
The Commission must adopt the measures necessary for the implementation of the regulation. These include:
implementing measures to ensure the information on envisaged measures is made available to interested parties without delay;
establishing a system allowing complete traceability of the patient as well as of the finished product and its starting materials;
ensuring that information on the products and their starting materials is kept up-to-date.
Amending Regulation (EU) 2019/852 amends Annexes I and II to the regulation to allow the Commission to adopt delegated acts to amend Annexes III and IV to this regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2005.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Advanced therapy medicinal product: a medicinal product which is designed to treat a disease or disease-related disorder in a non-clinical, non-therapeutic manner.
* Combination therapy: a combination of two or more medicinal products designed to be used together to treat the same disease, disease or disorder.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 			
Commission Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 768/2004 of 20 December 2004 laying down the general principles and guidelines of good manufacturing practice in respect of the manufacture, marketing and distribution of medicines for the human use and investigational medicinal products (OJ L 127, 24.12.2004, pp. 1–8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EEC, EEC) no 768/04 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 175:
Emissions from motor vehicles — type approval and type-approval requirements for certain types of vehicles
Exhaustive list of types of motor vehicles and their trailers in the European Union (EU).
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 — type-applying requirements for motor vehicles
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the type approval of certain motor vehicles, their trailers and systems.
KEY POINTS
The regulation lays down the obligations of motor vehicle manufacturers, importers and distributors to ensure that their vehicles comply with the requirements of Directive 2005/55/EC on type approval.
Manufacturers’ type approval obligations
The manufacturer must provide the competent national authority with:
information relating to access to vehicle repair and maintenance information and to the information referred to in Annex II to the regulation;
information on the type of vehicle and its emission control systems;
technical information on exhaust emissions and exhaust particulate emissions.
The vehicle manufacturer must also make training material available to independent operators and authorised dealers and repairers.
Importers must ensure that the exhaust emissions of their vehicles are measured in accordance with the European Harmonised System for Harmonised Emissions Control Systems (EEC) and that their exhaust emissions are recorded and recorded in the Annex III of the regulation.
In addition, the manufacturer must inform the competent authority of any use of defeat devices that reduce the effectiveness of the vehicle’s emission control system.
EU countries must introduce a new measurement procedure to measure the mass and number of particulate emission emissions in the laboratory.
If a vehicle is fitted with a positive ignition particulate mass (PIPM), the manufacturer is responsible for measuring the mass of the particulate matter and the number of particles emitted by the engine.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
 
For more information, see:
Types of vehicles and systems in the EU (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Emissions: the total amount of total and total non-methane hydrocarbons emitted by a motor vehicle.
* Particulate matter: the volume of particulates emitted from the exhaust system of a vehicle when it is tested in a laboratory. It is calculated using the mass, volume and percentage of the particles emitted.

Summary 176:
Scientific assessment of substances on the EU’s list of foodstuffs (Safeguard of human life and health)
Scientific Assessment of substanceson the EU's list of foods
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2004 on the European Food Safety Authority's list
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the rules for the European Medicines Agency (EMA) to assess substances on its list of substances to be added to the European Union (EU) list.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to substances listed in EU countries’ sectoral food law, which contribute to the free movement of food within the EU and to a high level of protection of human health and to the protection of consumer interests.
It does not apply to substances which are not listed in the EU list and which have been added to it by the Commission.
The list is updated by the European Commission on a case-by-case basis, taking into account the different criteria set out in each sectoral law, as well as taking account the time needed to consider the different aspects of each food law and to ensure adequate time for consultation when preparing the draft measures.
In addition, the Commission is assisted by the Standing Committee on the Authority, which assists the Commission in its decision-making process.
EU countries must inform the Commission of the substances on their list and inform it of the reasons for adding, removing or changing conditions, specifications or restrictions associated with the presence of the substance on their market.
Implementing measures
In the event of an emergency concerning a substance on the list, measures must be adopted in accordance with the procedures laid down in the regulation.
Amendments to the list
The Commission may supplement the list by supplementing it, inter alia, with measures designed to amend non-essential elements of the EU law, i.e. factors relevant to the matter under consideration.
If the Commission considers that the measures are not necessary, it may adopt them on the basis of the information already provided by the applicant.
Applications for the inclusion of substances in the list are sent to the Commission on its own initiative.
Information relating to the following is confidential:
the name and address of the applicant;
the names and addresses of the supplier;
any other information which might significantly harm their competitive position.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATED APPLY?
   
It entered into force on 1 January 2005.
BACKGROUND
The EU lists of substances are published in the Official Journal.
For more information, see:
European Medicines Authority (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Foodstuffs: substances used in food, such as food additives, flavourings, preservatives and flavourings.
* List of substances: a list of chemicals used in foods, which contributes to free movement within the Community.

  баркова  грацига года

Summary 177:
Rules on accreditation, market surveillance, controls of products from non-EU countries and the CE marking (until 1 January 2020)
Rules on accredited and market surveillance bodies
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 — rules on the accreditation of conformity assessment bodies
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for accreditation*, market surveillance* and controls on products imported from third countries.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all products covered by the EU’s common framework for the marketing of products.
It does not apply to certain products, such as medicines, medical devices, medicinal products for human and veterinary use, motor vehicles and aviation.
Accreditation
The European Commission recognises a body that meets the requirements of EU legislation to carry out conformity assessment* to ensure that a product complies with the relevant EU legislation.
The accreditation procedure is carried out by national accreditation bodies (known as CE bodies) recognised by the European Commission. The Commission may not recognise more than one body at a time.
Market surveillance measures
EU countries must periodically review and assess the functioning of their surveillance activities.
If a product does not comply with EU legislation, it must be released for free circulation, provided that all the other requirements and formalities have been fulfilled.
Where the market surveillance authorities find that the product is not in breach of EU harmonisation legislation, they must suspend the release of the product and take further measures, including the involvement of the European Anti-Fraud Office (EFTA).
The Commission is responsible for coordinating the activities of the EU countries’ market surveillance and information exchange system.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY APPLY?
 
   
It has applied since 1 January 2010.
BACKGROUND
The legislation is part of a package of measures designed to modernise and simplify the rules on product safety in the EU.
For more information, see:
‘Accreditation’ and ‘market surveillance’ on the European Agency for Harmonisation of the laws of the Member States’ websites
KEY TERMS
* CE marking: a CE marking affixed to a product to show that it meets all the essential requirements of the relevant legislation and that it has been tested and certified in accordance with EU standards.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Егранска года баркова
Council Regulation (EU) No 550/2008 of 20 December 2008 laying down rules on accreditations, market Surveillance, controls on imports of products and on the CE mark (OJ L 183, 21.12.2008, pp. 1-8)

Summary 178:
EU-Norway agreement on extradition of suspects arrested on the territory of another EU country (SUMMARY OF:
Agreement between the European Union and the Kingdom of Norway and the Republic of Iceland on extradition
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND OF THE DECISION?
 
The agreement aims to facilitate the transfer of suspects between EU and non-EU countries who have been arrested in the EU and whose country of residence is not the EU.
The decision concludes the agreement on behalf of the EU with Norway and Iceland.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The aim of the agreement is to:
facilitate the exchange of information between EU countries on the arrest warrant issued by the EU’s judicial authorities for the arrest of a person who has been arrested on their territory;
ensure that the person concerned is given the right to legal counsel;
provide for the possibility of a period of detention in the country in which the person is to be surrendered;
allow for the person to be informed of the consequences of the decision on surrender.
It does not apply to double criminality.
EU countries may apply reciprocity in relation to the EU countries concerned.
Procedures for transmitting an arrest warrant
The issuing judicial authority is the judicial authority of the country which is competent to issue the warrant by virtue of the law of that country. It decides whether to execute the warrant on the basis of a declaration or a notification from the requesting country.
If the request for surrender is made by the requested person, the executing judicial authority decides whether the warrant should be executed or not.
In the event of multiple requests for execution, the requesting the execution of the warrant, it must decide within 10 days of the new date agreed by the requesting judicial authority. The executing the warrant may decide to postpone the surrender of the person so that he or she may be prosecuted in the executing country or to serve, in its territory, a sentence passed for an act other than that referred to in the warrant.
Surrender or subsequent extradition is subject to the condition that the acts for which the warrant has been issued constitute an offence, whatever the constituent elements or however it is described.
Conformity
The requested person must have the right of legal counsel and be able to renounce his/her right of appeal against the decision to execute or to be extradited to the country where the warrant was issued.
Consent and renunciation
The requesting country must ensure that consent and, where appropriate, renunciation are established in such a way as to show that the persons concerned has expressed them voluntarily and in full awareness of the consequence of the action.
This consent must be recorded in accordance with that country's national law. The requested person may not be deprived of his or her right of liberty or of the property which is liable to seizure or confiscation in the issuing country if the property is needed in connection with pending criminal proceedings, or temporarily retain it or hand it over to the issuing state, on condition that it is returned.
Decision on surrender
The executing country must decide, within the time limits and under the conditions defined in this agreement, whether the person should be surrendered or whether he/she should be held in detention for a period longer than the 10-day limit set out in the agreement.
Time limits for surrender
A decision on the surrender must be made within 10 working days of a new date, unless the requested persons has already been detained for more than 10 days. In that case, the surrender should take place within 10 more working days.
Where the requesting person is not subject to a speciality rule, the requested country may decide, after deciding to surrender, to extend the period for which detention is served or to postpone it for a sentence other than the one referred to, to serve a sentence which is not related to the act for which it has issued the warrant or to which it is related.
Amendments to the agreement
Amending the agreement has been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
References
Act
Entry into force - Date of expiry
Deadline for transposition in the Member States
Official Journal
Council Decision (EU) 2015/852/EU
-

Summary 179:
Compensation and assistance for passengers in the event of major disruption to a rail passenger service
Compensation & assistance in the case of major disruptions to a railway passenger service	SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2004 on compensation and assistance to passengers in connection with major disruption of rail passenger services
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down common rules for the liability of rail carriers and passengers in relation to major disruptions of their passenger service.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all passengers travelling by rail, irrespective of their age, gender, nationality, place of residence or place of employment.
It does not apply to:
passengers travelling by road, air, sea or inland waterways;
passenger vehicles;
vehicles used for the carriage of passengers on board a train;
carriage charges levied by railway undertakings.
Amending Regulation (EU) 2017/852 amends Regulation (EC), which lays down rules on the liability and assistance of passengers and persons with reduced mobility on board trains.
The new rules apply to the following categories of passengers:
persons who have been injured or who have suffered loss or damage as a result of an accident, accident or damage caused by a railway carrier.
Persons who are entitled to compensation for damage caused to their personal property as a consequence of a railway accident.
Passengers entitled to assistance on board the train.
People entitled to reimbursement of the carriage charge levied by the carrier for delay in delivery of a passenger’s luggage.
In addition, passengers entitled to payment and refund of a carriage charge.
Directive 2004/49/EC on railway infrastructure charges for the use of railway infrastructure.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLIMITATION APPLY?
   
 
It has applied since 1 January 2005.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a series of measures to improve consumer protection in the field of transport.
For more information, see:
‘Railway passenger rights’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 180:
Production of specific statistics on education, training and lifelong learning (2009-2010)
Performance of specific EU statistics
The production of specific European statistics
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2009 on the production of statistics on the quality of education, learning and lifelong education
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It lays down the rules for the production and transmission of specific statistical information on education and training in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to EU countries’ national statistics on:
education and training systems,
participation of adults in lifelong learning and
the quality of lifelong learning.
It does not apply to:
employment and social security statistics;
employment statistics; and
social security statistics.
The European Commission (Eurostat) collects annual data on education from the EU countries on a voluntary basis, through a joint action carried out with the Unesco Institute for Statistics (UIS) and with the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD), usually referred to as the ‘UOE data collection’.
Data sources and sample size
The data source must be a sample survey.
EU countries must transmit confidential micro-data resulting from sample surveys to Eurostat in accordance with the rules on the transmission of data subject to confidentiality set out in Regulation (Euratom) No 1588/90 on Community statistics (see summary).
The Commission is assisted by the Statistical Programme Committee.
When significant new data requirements or insufficient quality of data are identified and before any data collection, the Commission may institute pilot studies to be carried out on an EU-wide basis. These studies may not necessarily lead to corresponding implementing measures.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2010.
BACKGROUND
The Lisbon strategy aims to contribute better to the Lisbon strategy and to establish comprehensive lifelong learning strategies.
For more information, see:
‘Lifelong learning’ on the European Commission’s website.
KEY TERMS
* Education and training statistics: the statistical information that EU countries provide to the Commission on their education systems, their training systems and the quality and relevance of their lifelong learning policies.
* Longevity learning: lifelong learning is defined as the period of time in which a person remains active in a lifelong learning activity beyond the age of 18.

Summary 181:
EU energy statistics — energy data
EU energy data — energy statistics
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 552/2013 on the collection of energy statistics and on the quality assessment and reporting of data
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the collection, reporting and transmission of EU-wide energy statistics.
KEY POINTS
The regulation requires EU countries to collect and transmit to the European Commission, the European Atomic Energy Community (Euratom) and the European Statistical System Committee (ESSC) data on energy production, consumption and consumption by energy-intensive sectors.
The statistics cover:
energy supply and consumption;
energy consumption and use;
production and use of fossil fuels and their derivatives;
the production and consumption of industrial gases, chemicals and waste.
It does not apply to the following sectors:
agriculture, forestry, fishing and aquaculture;
pulp, paper and printing;
paper and printing.
EU countries must also report on:
the number and types of electricity generated by electricity generating plants;
total energy consumed by electricity generation and distribution;
transmission of electricity to and from power stations and other sources of electricity;
gas used for heating, cooling and air conditioning;
natural gas used for power generation and heating.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
  
It entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
Energy statistics have traditionally been focused on energy supply and on fossil energies.
For more information, see:
‘Energy statistics’ on Euratom’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Fossil energies
* Fossil energies: hydrocarbons, such as oil, natural gas, coal, hydrofluorocarbons, kerosene and other fuels, as well as their derivatives.

Summary 182:
Passengers’ rights when travelling by road, rail and air
Passengers' rights when traveling by road or air
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 552/2014 — passenger rights on road transport
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down common rules on the rights of passengers and persons with reduced mobility to travel by road and air in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Passenger rights
The regulation applies to all passengers travelling on road or rail transport in the EU, irrespective of their physical or mental disability.
It does not apply to passengers travelling with occasional services where the initial boarding point or the final alighting point of the passenger is situated in the territory of a non-EU country.
In addition, it does not cover:
passenger rights in the event of cancellation or delay of a bus or coach transport service;
passengers travelling with a package tour which is cancelled for reasons other than cancellation of the transport service.
Conditions for reservation and ticketing
Carriers, travel agents and tour operators must ensure that passengers travelling by public transport have the right to a reservation and a ticket at no additional cost. Reservations and tickets are offered to disabled persons and persons who have reduced mobility at no extra cost.
The carrier or the terminal managing body responsible for the operation of the terminal must inform the person concerned about any alternative service operated by the carrier.
If the carrier refuses to accept a reservation or to issue or provide a ticket on the grounds of disability, the passenger must be informed about any other alternative service available.
Personscancelling, re-routing and reimbursement of the ticket price
The passenger may be entitled to compensation for death and personal injury or loss of or damage to their luggage. The amount of compensation is calculated in accordance with applicable national law.
Compensation is paid within 1 month after the submission of the request for compensation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
The legislation applies from 1 January 2015.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
Directive 2014/33/EU on the European Commission’s Directorate-General for Consumers’ Rights website.
KEY TERMS
* Passenger rights: the right of a passenger to travel on the road or by air by means of a ticket or a reservation.

Summary 183:
Aquaculture statistics
Aquatic statistics
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 788/96 — statistics on aquaculture
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the collection of statistics on the production of fish, crustaceans and molluscs (aquaculture) by EU countries.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
the annual production (volume and unit value) of all species of fish and crustacean* in EU waters;
the number of species of molluses and other aquatic animals kept in hatcheries and nurseries;
production methods used for collecting the data.
The data must relate to the reference calendar year and must cover:
fisher species;
crustaceans;
molluses;
other aquatic animals.
Data must be submitted within 12 months of the end of the reference year to the European Commission (Eurostat).
EU countries may request a derogation from this regulation in so far as the application of this regulation to their national statistical systems requires major adaptations and is likely to cause significant practical problems.
National authorities must ensure that the data are collected in accordance with the rules laid down in Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on the statistical system of the European Union (see summary).
The Commission is assisted by the Standing Committee for Agricultural Statistics.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a common fisheries policy for the period 2008-2020.
For more information, see:
‘Fisheries’ on Eurostat’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Aquaculture: places for the artificial breeding, hatching and rearing through the early life stages of aquatic animals, such as fish or crustacea.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EEC, Euratom) No 768/96 of 20 December 1996 laying down rules on the compilation of statistics for the production and use of fish (OJ L 347, 20.12.1996, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC, EEC, L 347) have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Summary 184:
Convention on the rational conservation and management of fishery resources in the area covered by the International Convention on the Lawful Conservation and Management of Fishery Resources (ICC-19)
CONVENTION ON THE LAWLAW
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) No 1224/2009 of the European Parliament and of the Council on the application of the Convention for the Lawfulness of the Conservation of Fishery Resources in the Area of the International Fisheries Convention (the Convention Area)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION AND OF THE DECISION?
The regulation aims to ensure the effective application by EU countries of the convention on the lawlaying of the rules on the conservation of fisheries and the management of fisheries by non-contracting parties.
The decision repeals Regulation (EC) No 1005/2008.
KEY POINTS
The convention covers:
fishery resources (e.g. fish, shellfish, crustaceans and crustacean species);
fishing vessels flying the flag of a non-member country;
non-member countries’ fishing vessels flying their flag.
EU countries must:
ensure that all non-fisherying vessels entering one of their ports are inspected.
Ensure that non-Fishery Parties to the convention are notified of the vessel monitoring system (VMS) and of information obtained by the VMS, including the vessel’s call sign and the total round weight by species, the vessel intends to land or transship, the time and geographical position of the planned transshipment and the number of vessels to be off-loaded or on-loaded.
Importers must inform the European Commission of vessels that are suspected of carrying out IUU activities in the convention area.
Report to the Commission of catches of regulated resources
The Commission must forward the information promptly to the NEAFC Secretary.
Vessel Monitoring System
Member States must ensure the automatic and electronic transmission to the Secretary of the Nomenclature of information on vessel monitoring systems.
Monitoring of vessels
VMSs must be set up in accordance with the International Code of Signals (ICS) and the rules laid down in the Convention.
National authorities must ensure that vessels entering a port designated by a Member State are given prior notice of their entry into port.
If the vessel is found to be in breach of the above rules, it must proceed immediately, and in any case within 24 hours, to a port of that flag Member State, for a thorough inspection under its authority.
Inspections must be carried out by inspectors from another Member State who are permitted to carry out inspections on board the vessel.
Fishing vessels must not board any fishing vessel without prior notice being transmitted by radio to that vessel or without that vessel being given the appropriate signal using the International code of signals.
Where the vessel exceeds the limit for the number and weight of fish to be landed or transhipment, the inspection report must be recorded in the vessel's inspection report. The reasons for exceeding the limit are recorded in an inspection report and the vessel must be informed of the reasons for the infringement.
Non-Member States are responsible for enforcing the rules of the regulation.
FROM WHEN DO THE REGOLATION AND DECISION APPLY?
Directive 2012/13/EU entered into force on 1 January 2013.
BACKGROUND
  
The Convention provides for an appropriate framework for multilateral cooperation to ensure full respect of the conservation, management and management measures adopted by the non-signatory countries.
For more information, see:
Fisheries and fisheries management (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENTS
 
Commission Implementing Decision 2012/23/EU of 20 December 2012 on the implementation of the Agreement for the law laying down the rules for the conservation and conservation of Fishes and Fauna in the Areas of the IUC-19 Convention (OJ L 136, 20.12.2012, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Directive 2012/24/EU have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENT
Council Implementing Directive 2011/12/EU amending Decision 2011/11/EU on the enforcement of the Treaty establishing a European Union Fisheries Union and amending Council Regulation (CFSP) No 652/2011 on the control and enforcement measures for fishery resource conservation and the Management of Fauna and Flora in the areas of the EU Fisheries Union

Summary 185:
Ecodesign requirements for energy-related products — EU Ecolabel (2009) — summary
EcodesIGNOSIGN requirements for Energy-Related Products — EUEcolabel
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2009 on ecodesign requirements
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
It sets out rules for the setting of ecodeign* requirements for products and services which are supplied for distribution, consumption or use on the EU market.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to any goods or services which:
provide energy for the production, distribution or consumption of energy;
are used for the manufacture, manufacture, storage, transport, storage or storage of energy, whether or not they are manufactured in the EU or in non-EU countries;
have a significant environmental impact.
It does not apply to:
foodstuffs;
materials used in the manufacture of medicines, cosmetics, cosmetics and personal care products;
medical devices;
personal care products.
Requirements
Products covered by the regulation must meet the following criteria:
have at least one of the following characteristics listed in the regulation’s annexes:
a minimum energy efficiency rating of at least 80% and a maximum energy efficiency of 80% for each product group;
an environmental impact rating of between 0.5% and 1% of the total energy consumption;
be free of any harmful effects on the environment and have a minimum energy consumption.
The Commission may adopt additional criteria based on the best available scientific evidence, such as the most significant environmental impacts on human health or the environment, and on the most environmentally soundness of the product.
Products must be labelled with the following information:
an optional label with three key environmental characteristics that may be displayed in the optional label;
a description of the products’ life cycle and the relevant period of validity of the criteria and of the assessment requirements;
the degree of product variability allowed during the period of time during which the product group meets the criteria.
Market surveillance and control of the use of the EU label
EU countries must ensure that the Commission carries out market surveillance and controls to ensure that products comply with the requirements of the regulation. The Commission may also carry out random spot-checks.
EU Ecolabelling may also be promoted via the European Union ecolabel website, which provides basic information and promotional materials on the European label, and information on where to purchase EU EColabel products, in all EU languages.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2010.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for implementing the regulation and ensuring its proper functioning.
For more information, see:
‘Ecosign requirements’ on the Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Ecodesign: an environmental label that provides information on the environmental impact of a product or service on its environment.
REFERENCES
Act
Entry into force
Deadline for transposition in the Member States
Official Journal
Council Regulation (EC) No 550/2009

Summary 186:
Protection of medicinal products protected by patents
Protection from patent abuse
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2006 on the protection of medicines protected by basic patents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the granting of patents on medicinal products covered by a certificate of protection.
It aims to prevent patent abuse and to improve the free movement of medicines within the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation lays down the conditions under which a patent is granted to a medicinal product which is protected by a basic patent.
The protection conferred by the patent is limited to the product covered by the authorisation to place the product on the market as a medicine.
A certificate granted by the competent national authority of an EU country is valid for a period of 20 years.
Application for a certificate
The application must contain at least the following information:
the name and address of the holder of the patent;
the number of the basic patent,
the title of the invention, the number and date of the first authorisation, and the product identified in that authorisation.
Applications for an extension of the duration of a certificate already granted must contain the particulars referred to in the annex to the application, and a copy of the certificate, as well as the copy of a copy already granted.
An application for a renewal of the protection granted under a certificate may be lodged within 6 months from the date of application for renewal.
If the application is rejected, the certificate is notified to the competent authority of the EU country.
Duration of protection
The term of protection is reduced by the number of years by which the patent exceeds 20 years, unless the term of a patent exceeds that amount.
EU countries may require that the certificate be subject to the payment of annual fees.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLYEAR OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
It entered into force on 1 May 2006.
BACKGROUND
The European Medicines Agency (EMSA) is responsible for administering the Medicines Directive.
For more information, see:
‘Medicines Directive’ on the European Commission's website.
KEY TERMS
* Patent protection: the protection conferred on a product by a patent which, before 2 January 1993, had its term extended or for which such extension was applied for, under national law.
* Basic patent: a patent granted by a manufacturer to a manufacturer of a product which has been patented for a limited period of time.
REFERENCES
Act
Entry into force
Deadline for transposition in the Member States
Official Journal
Commission Implementing Decision (EU) 2018/852
1.5.2018
-
OJ L 183 of 1.5-
Amending act(s)
Subsequent amendments and corrections to Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 550/2018 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED ACTS
 
Regulations (EC), Euratom and Euratom of the European Parliament and of the Council of 11 December 2009 on the application for the protection by a medical product of patents and repealing Council Regulation (EEC, EC) No 1768/92 and Regulation (EC, EEC, EFTA) No 1011/2006 (see summary).

Summary 187:
Convention on jurisdiction of courts in civil and commercial matters in the EU and the EU’s eastern neighbourly countries
Convention of the Court of Justice of the European Economic Community on jurisdiction
SUMMARY OF:
Decision 2005/852/EC on the conclusion of the Convention on jurisdiction in Civil and Commercial Matters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE CONVENTION AND OF THE DECISION?
The convention aims to ensure that the courts of the EU countries have exclusive jurisdiction in all matters relating to the protection of persons’ rights and obligations under the law of one or more EU countries.
The decision approves the convention on jurisdiction.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The Convention applies to all matters of law, whether they are civil or commercial, where the parties are domiciled in the country where the event occurred or may occur.
Jurisdiction
The courts of each EU country has exclusive jurisdiction, regardless of domicile, in proceedings concerned with:
the registration or validity of any European patent granted for that country irrespective of whether the issue is raised by way of an action or as a defence;
any action on a trust instrument conferred on a settlor, trustee or beneficiary, irrespective of their place of residence;
all actions on a contract of insurance insofar as it covers immovable property in a country not covered by the convention, except insofar as the insurance is compulsory or relates to immovable properties in a State bound by this convention;
actions on a warranty or guarantee or in any other third party proceedings.
Lis pendens — related actions.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCELEGAL DOCUMENTS
 
The Convention entered into force on 19 October 2005.
It has applied since 1 January 2007.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
The Hague Convention on Jurisdiction (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision 2005/884/EC of 20 October 2005 concerning the conclusion, on behalf of the United Kingdom and of the Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland, of the Conventions on jurisdiction and on the application of the laws of the States bound by the Convention (OJ L 183, 29.10.2005, pp. 1-8)
last update 04.02.2016
